si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	Push the instrument called "cultellar" into the first incision, and it is very sharp on one side and soft but not sharp on the other, and its shape is:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	 And make the incision cutting towards the raw flesh at will, and the incision soft towards the bone, and push until it comes to the middle cleavage.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And gather all the vessels that descend from the head towards the eyes until the incision is continuous up to where it opens the raw flesh, and then another part should be made in the middle cleavage up to the opposite hollow; and then drain blood evenly, and press firmly for the blood taken; then put a tent of old cotton in each incision, and place wet linen soaked in vinegar and oil and alum on top, and make sure no pus comes; on the third day, untie the ligature, and apply great heat with warm mustard, then heal with ointment of basilicon with rose oil, and other treatments for wounds until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	the root of the hairs
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When anyone comes with an acute catarrh, you see the eyes becoming swollen and small, blurring the vision, and burned papers; hairs fall out, and a headache ensues due to pain, and the patient coughs; then recognize these symptoms that those substances and this catarrh do not come from anywhere else but multiple veins, and the remedy for this illness is what is needed.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	 And you instruct the patient to lean back their head, then make a large incision on the forehead and another deep one at the base of the neck.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	 From the temple on the left to the temple on the right, and the incision should go up to the bone; move your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move while eating; when the bone is exposed, suck all the blood with a sponge, then insert cotton between the two lips of the incision and sew it closed with linen thread; then place damp cloths soaked in wine and oil on top, take care to avoid abscessing hot; once removed, you must rub the bone until char begins to grow, then treat it with things that promote the growth of flesh.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take two parts of wheat flour and four parts of colophony, and make a plaster with it; apply it to these wounds in order to promote the growth of char everywhere.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the stoppage of ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Anything falling in the ears is one of the four things: grains, animals, stone or similar things like iron; seeds such as peas, lentils, beans; or something flowing like water and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	 When it falls in the ear stone or another manner of thing that does not adjust itself to the ear, and does not heal in the ear, put the ear on the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	 If you see the stone, distill a little of purple oil or sage oil, then apply extraction; and make it vomit from conditon, and stop its nostrils when vomiting comes, and place around the ear pieces of fabric or wool; and hold it above.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	 Many times it causes farting with this cure; and if it does not cause farting, apply extraction using fine tweezers, in which case the form is:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it jumps at the hinges, that is good; if not, bring forth extraction with subtle thin forceps of small double curvature; and if it does not jump by this means, make a fishhook of wax and thrust its tip into the ear strongly, and stop up that which is around the hook with soft wax so that the vein cannot enter with the hook; then pull it forth, for it often comes forth as we have said; and if it does not come forth in this manner, take glue of that and take the birds, and put any instrument that is pointed for this purpose, and put a bit of cotton around it; then press the glue onto the stone or something else, and pull it forth.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it does not jump in any of the ways we have said, hurry to cut the ear so that abscess pus and spasm come out; and the manner of cutting is that you first make the patient sneeze from the cephalic vein, and draw blood according to the measure of its power, then seat the patient between your hands and turn the ear upward, and make a small cut in the root of the ear where the fat or flesh depends; let the cut be like a moon until you reach the bone, then break it according to your power, and suck it out quickly with your mouth; and cure it until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is a grain that swells, administer extraction; and if it cannot come out, administer one thin, subtle spatula according to this shape:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	 and make an incision of that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	 But do not do that when you think the grain is moist due to ear moisture, until you have made many cuts; then extract it with fine tweezers and apply suction, as we have said, so that the extraction is aligned.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	 Then, when pus falls into the ear, the patient should use warm compresses first, and stuff the ear with soft cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	 And lie there on that very ear where the pus is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	 If it jumps out because of this, that's good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	 If it does not jump out, take many small and light pebbles according to the size of your thumbnail and heat them slightly in the fire; then make the patient hold a cotton-wool swab or piece of cloth in their ear, and press one stone on the other side, and strike another stone against the stone that is in the ear; continue this process of stone against stone until the pus has completely drained out and jumps out entirely; if you see, take a thin stick, and push one cheek in the ear, and hold the other cheek with fire until the thinnest part is burnt; then do the same with other sticks until the pus has completely drained out, as we have said earlier.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the removal of a beast (insect) that is small like a flea and similar things, treat it as we have said in the previous section; but if it is large and can be felt, make an extraction using tweezers; it is the lighter things that are easier to remove from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms in the ears, when you cure it as we have said in the division and where to treat distillations, if the treatment does not help, then you should look at the ear in the sun: if any worms open, you should take them with subtle tweezers, and if they do not open, then you should take the cane of which this form is.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	 And narrow underneath and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	 And insert the small head into the ear according to the amount of pain the patient has, then suck out all the canine teeth; do this often until all the worms come out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	 And if they do not come out, stop the canine tooth with cotton as I said in the earlier section; and if they protrude as we have said, administer distillations that the ancients have proven effective in removing worms. You will find or treat the distillations here. Distil your oils and medicines into the ear with this equipment as shown:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And it should be narrow inside and wide outside made of silver or lead with one small hole, and above a distillation chamber for distilling; and to press the distillation within this device made of lead, and if you see that you need a scraper, you should wrap cotton around the tip; then pour your oil or juice, and whatever medicine you have into the cane, which is in the ear; then push the scraper into all the cotton and press your hand evenly until the oil distills or moves from the ear; let the patient smell inside, and the distillations should be about one spoonful heated in fire thus it is distilled in the ear; make sure that it is not too cold, for the medicine will not be as effective.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the stoppage of ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born who does not have any birth defects in the ears; and this same thing happens to adults through ear stoppage caused by pus or pus inside the ear, and this stoppage can sometimes be deep within the ear, which cannot be seen; and sometimes it causes one of the eardrums to move out, which is easily visible.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Therefore, if it cannot be seen deep within the ear, it is a serious condition in many cases, and in this case you must put the sick person's ear in the sun; look inside: if you see the accumulation clearly, you should use the spatula shaped like this one to remove it:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And let it be sharp and incisive all around, so that it does not pierce the ear; if the opening is of soft flesh or cartilage of the ear, hold it with subtle tweezers and strike gently until all the flesh is completely removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	 And if the swelling is entirely in the ear, take the fine razor and slightly heat it over fire, then place it in the ear canal.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	 If the patient feels swelling that causes pain in the ear, make a small incision carefully, ensuring not to harm the nerve of the ear; then insert a tube according to the size of the opening, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this every day until the wound is healed, or take a plug and moisten it with rosewater, add powdered vitriol; if you see the ear swell, then it is necessary to draw out the plug and insert another plug moistened with roset oil and beeswax until the swelling disappears; then let it heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding occurs, immerse a sponge and cold water in it, and place it on the ear, and use other treatments that stop the bleeding which are to treat distillations.
de la char des papieres	of the bark of poplars
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This is the method that comes in papers from the eyes when they are moist and dry; it must be stretched with tongs and tweezers, and then struck with a spatula at its roots; then place it on the side of vitriol powder.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if not dressed (cauterized), the subtle lenticular cautery should be applied to it, and afterwards the cauterization following the incision is worthwhile; and they often heal, because nothing remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of the hailstorm
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	 Often, in papers, there come things that appear like hail in shape and hardness, and for this reason this disease is called "hail", and it is a collection of thick moisture on the paper above and below; the procedure is as follows: watch carefully if the hail becomes silent from both sides, and it is an easy matter to know; then make a large opening, then peel off each side gently, then take hold of it with pincers, and squeeze.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	 If you cannot cover it with something and pierce a little of the paper, nothing hurts the patient; and if the tear is large, assemble it with a stitch and cure it until it heals; and if it is small, do not force it because the oil heals it soon enough.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the pus is descending within the ear towards the upper part, turn the paper over, and grasp the pus with forceps, then press it from both sides; and if the paper is pushed away by the incision, it does not matter; and when the pus is pressed, apply salty oil to the area where the patient has an infection until the patient recovers.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat from the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	 External ointment is applied on the papers of children more than with adults, and it hurts their eyes very much, and they come down with catarrh in the mornings, and cannot bear to look at the light of the sun because tears run into their eyes quickly; therefore they lie on their faces immediately, sleep, and keep their papers moist under their eyelids that the excrement and appearance are covered by the ointment which spreads in the oil.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	 And when you press the joint with your fingers and feel the dislocation coming between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the method of work is that the patient places their head in your lap; and then takes one piece of linen cloth, and prepares a tent in the shape of a circle according to the size that contains exirnach for each part, then puts it on top; and presses with both hands from one side and another, so that the exirnach is assembled within the circle; then makes an incision in the middle of the moisture with a pointed spatula cutting a slit wide, but not larger than the wound made at the vein opening; and cuts the skin completely until you can see the exirnach; and in various positions, the exirnach comes out from the slit, according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Then, place a piece of linen cloth between your hands and spread it apart; and make sure you do not displace the spatula in the slit, go up to the oil but do not pierce or cut it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	If the exirnach does not open at the beginning of the slit, slightly enlarge the slit until it appears; then pull as previously stated, moisten cloth in oil and water, place it on top, and hold with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	 And to those who grind seeds and put it on top to corrupt that moisture which remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then heal it until it is sound.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If an abscess comes to the joint which is hot, heal it with plasters softening it until it is sound.
des poilz des papieres	the hairs of the paper
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When paper hairs grow other than naturally and are nurtured, they harm the eyes and bring on various diseases such as common eye ailments like tears and swelling of the paper and albugine, which cause the destruction of the eyes; and there are four ways to cure it: either by cautery with fire, or with medicine ointment according to what is stated in the previous chapter about cautery, and this is done either by incision and stitching, or with canes, as I will explain.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is required that you place the patient's head in your lap, then turn the paper of oil on your left hand; if it has been converted, that is good; if not, push a needle through one thread above it; and it should be pierced where the edge of the paper meets the hairs, or where the hairs grow from those hairs, and pull one thread across the whole paper, and turn to the razor; then make in the part beneath the paper, under the hairs adjacent, as wide as a spatula, from the large blister until the small one; then pull one thread, and place a small tent of cotton and linen underneath the paper, then mark on the paper a sign of a thorn, as a bunch of myrtle, and it is necessary that the figure be according to the quantity you wish to lift the paper which has been designated for all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	 If the wound requires much paper according to how the paper is softened; then take all the space of two lines that you have marked, and start from the large tear until it becomes small; and let one of the cuts be near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root; then insert an onion into one of the two angles; then peel everything off; then bring the two lips together to a suture with a needle and all fine linen thread, drain the blood, and make the excess threads sticky using any glueing substance if you want to do this; but if not, do not have any care, leave the suture and threads for three or four days; then heal the wound without sutures using drying and tightening substances, because the paper revives at the edge of the wound and its assembly, but the suture is rotten (as the ancients say), and this is a job without fear; and there is another way: it is to sign the paper with a figure like the leaves of myrtle, as we have told you, using three onions cut in the form that is shown here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then bind equally with cords, according to the shape shown below:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	 And if you cannot hold the pliers, and the object is not even, take a needle with thread, and insert it into the opening; then insert another thread through the large incision, and the third thread through the small, and arrange the threads equally between your hands; then lift your hand equally, and lift all the skin as you have described, then sew up the edges of the wound using stitches, and treat it until it is healed; if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with ointment and similar healing balms; and sometimes the hair from the wound may turn inwards: in this case you must use what we have said about the incision; but the stitching in one or the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure for bites is as follows: You are to fold the paper and place it inside as I have said, and then make 2 stitches with art, and 2 subtle threads of the same length as the paper and width of the spatula; take 2 pieces of each piece where you hold the threads; then bring together one and the other delicately on top of the paper oil, and bind the 2 stitches of the 2 parts; leave it for some days, and the skin that is bound will rot and die, until it dries up.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	 If it takes a long time [for the wound to heal], if he strikes with force, then cure him until he is healthy; and when the wound is sutured, and the paper is raised, and the hairs will not grow there anymore; this is the shape of the two wounds that you will make according to this figure, and according to this length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work is such that you take a subtle needle and insert one thread of fine silk; then assemble the pieces and join them delicately, and let the length of the threads be about a span; then arrange another fine silk thread briefly, tie the threads together; then make the patient put his head in your healthy one; and place it in the sun so that the work is exposed, for this is a subtle and delicate work, then insert the needle all along the root of the hair next to it, and pierce through the paper quickly until you pull up the natural hair above; then pull out the hair up to the needle, if there are one or two or three or more hairs; then hold your hand until the hairs come out fully with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the wound is treated and the hairs do not come forth with it, you shall draw out the arrow beneath to its full length that you have ordered, until the arrow comes forth from the flesh above and you see it by the vision of the eye; then you shall draw out the arrow and the string, and close the eye and leave it closed for two or three days, until the hair grows in its place and new flesh is formed; and if the hairs are small, one long hair of a goat's beard should accompany it, and let it be raised with this until it is distanced and then cleanse it.
de la porriture de l’oil	Of the boils on the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	 When this disease called "alecratis" or the eruption comes in the eye, it can occur in two ways: one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	 And it happens suddenly due to a wound, or from cutting or cauterization, or similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	 And the method of work is to cut that suture and separate the edges, and put inside threads of flax, and tie it until it is healed; and you should not use drying or constricting agents in its treatment.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	 If you do this, the disease will worsen more than before; but if you work with softening things, such as fenugreek; and the broth of water or milk and flax seeds are cooked, and then clarified in any oil, and it is wrapped in a cloth, and it is cured using it.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your care is that you do not allow it to heal in its previous form; and this treatment that we have said is only appropriate for correcting this disease, so that it does not return in its previous form.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the fat that comes in oil
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	 This disease which truly is called "axacrati", and is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	 The accident is due to wounds and cuts and cauterizations and similar things; and the work procedure in it is that you take a needle with double thread, and stick it into the flesh, and make it pierce from the left eyebrow to the right one, so that the threads come out at both cheeks of the flesh; then lift the flesh over the whole needle, and apply the spatula wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the shape of the paper returns as it should be, that's good; if not, take the razor and place it in the cut, turn the paper, and make two cuts where the bone protrudes inside the paper; let the edges of the two cuts be the angles of the incision you made, and form an angle so that when they are assembled, the shape is like the letter 'I greek'; then remove that cartilage, according to its thickness that its sides are pointed beneath the paper, then join the two separated parts with a linen thread; then treat it with the medicine for softening and healing as we have said before, until it heals.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the illness comes from a fracture or sewing or cauterization, then you must make a full incision under the hair of the paper, as mentioned before; then separate between the two leaves of a bandage, as I have said; and it is necessary to do the work according to the shape of the illness, because it is very diverse in shape, and the wise masters prepare devices with all possible skill to bring the figure back to its natural form; and the patients themselves, according to what is required for the work and instruments in various positions.
dou soudement de la papiere	swiftly of the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this adhesion occurs in the hands of men in such a way that the paper above is glued with white oil, and cannot move or perform its natural functions, it is necessary to insert the tip of a razor beneath the paper, lift it up; and hold it with pincers until you reach the cartilage that is subtle, which should not be too sharp nor too jagged, so that the patient does not suffer from too sharp spatula piercing the oil; and make your incision, from which you scrape the assembly, lightly, so that the paper returns to its natural form; and the entire assembly heals, and sometimes becomes infected with foul oil, and lifts of sweet oil and colirium; then place between the paper and the oil a tent of linen, and put on the oil wool moistened abundantly with egg; and after the third day use the colirium and other healing substances until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the nail of the oil
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the nail is of two kinds: it is nerve-like and resembles a hard horn, and another which is not nerve-like but resembles white solidified moisture, such that when it is touched by iron and boiled with pincers, it cannot be moved; and both seem to start from the great root, and grow little by little until it covers the whole eye and light and the movement of the oil.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of incision is that the patient places his head in your hand, then you open the eyes; take paper into your hand, then hold the nail with small pincers and lift it up; then take a needle, put one hair from a horse or cow or ox, and a strong thread; bend the tip of the needle slightly and insert it into the nail, piercing it all the way through, and tie the nail with the thread and lift it up; then scrape off all the hair on the side of the nail that follows the root and the silk to the hair until the skin, then cut the remaining part in the root of the finger as finely as possible with a small knife or tweezers, leaving the natural flesh at the root of the finger so that by the incision no blood comes out as usual; and sometimes the nail is held only on the end, and along the thread, as we have said; then scrape off all the soft tissue of this shape:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be careful that the soft tissue does not touch the flesh and tear it, and that the pulp is not pierced; and after the incision pour oil a little bit of broken sebum, and let it sit until the next day; then treat it as necessary until it heals.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nerveous and you cannot insert the needle, and the unguents cannot enter, many times this appearance of the nail is cured with medicines; and they grow as I have said in the division, and if you see it covered, it works the oil of the sick person, and take the spatumile lightly pointed according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	Gently press the nail upwards, and if you see that it does not shrink at all and the reason persists, distill from your mouth into the collyrium oil made of litargyre and red collyrium powder, and strain the oil until the next day; then repeat the work according to this same procedure until it is completely healed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing goes against you in the oil, as a general rule of abscesses, then milk it, and first heal the abscess hot until it is healed, then repeat the work as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh at the wound worsens greatly in oil, suspend it on a hook, and cut off a part but not all, so that tears do not come forth; then distill in the oil collyrium made from litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	And if the growth arises on the eyelid
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	 When certain men's nails grow red and cover the nail bed, they swell up on paper and turn towards the fingers, resembling a rosebud; and in such cases, the patient should place their head on your lap, then you should cut the nails, and as all that reddened flesh is conveniently reached, hold it with force; then strike the first piece of flesh, and keep striking until smooth to the end, taking care not to pierce the oil at the incision; and make the incision with a spatula as we have said in the nail incision and small forces similar to that used to remove the skin, as the form after this chapter demonstrates; and when the incision is complete and all the flesh is removed, use oil of sulphur or distill red collyrium and medicines corrosive, spread cotton with egg white on top to ensure the wound heals properly; if anything remains, let it heal by itself, and should doubt arise about proper healing, leave the oil and treat the wound with soothing substances for proper healing; then return to your work when the wound is healed, and do this for every nail that grows red in this manner.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But you must alleviate the cure of each oil with weak natural remedies; and in the work of iron, alleviate with hot remedies; and do not put your hand into any of these works until you see that this member is strong enough for that work.
des voines des eulz	the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	 Should be red veins covered by oil that are visible to the eye, and they hinder their work and weaken the oil every day.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	 Therefore, the first thing to do is to examine if there is oil, in which case there is no other disease except sebel; then treat it as follows: instruct the patient to lower their head and press those veins all along for a while according to their wisdom, and let the pressure be subtle double, following this shape:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And be two incisions by degree in one body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then squeeze those veins gently, and suck out the blood hour after hour until you see them move away from the oil; and be careful not to prick the oil with the points of the spatula, and perform this task at noon before the sun, and be very warm in your work so that you do not cut anything but those veins; and when you have done this, if it distills green and red collector oil for correcting those remaining with the sebel.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you do not have the power to hold it all in that hour, apply a plaster over oil of soothing things on the eyes, and leave it for some days until the pain is eased and assured of abscess healing, then resume as before until it is healed; this is the form of strength.
de la fistule de l’oil	And from the fistula of oil
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The mirror is named "arissati" fistula: when you cure it with cautery and burning medicine as I have previously said, and it is not healed, there is an engine in it that you cut open above the abscess where it should die, and drain all the moisture that is there until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed, and you see corruption and blackness, if it requires all the tools as stated here; it is called "rough head", and one should make a hole in it, exactly round, and point it like a chisel as shown in the current form.
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place the tool on top of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your hands and press your hand slightly so you know that the corruption is removed; do this once, then restore the position of the medicinal tool.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	 If the shoulder joint is fused, and char (pus) arises, and the body of the humerus (arm bone) is also fused, and remains like this for 40 days without healing or becoming inflamed, and no serious accident occurs, it is known to be healthy; if not, there is no other remedy but to return the fistula (a tunnel-like passage) to its original position according to this form: and it is that you expose the bone a second time with iron, and with hot medicines, and when it is exposed, take the iron as shown here: and the iron should have three angles, and the shaft should be attenuated (thinned) up to the head as you can see here.
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	 Then place it on the bone next to the ligament, and move your hand away from the oil hole, then turn the iron completely so that it pierces the bone and the patient feels it through the vein if he holds his hand above his neck; and then restore the joint with dry medicines as I have shown you, and when pus arises and hardens the joint, the matter goes to the neck; it is easier for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	of the oil issue
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes are wide open all around and there is no dislocation or decrease in size, it is necessary to hold the patient; then clean it, apply leeches or cauterize to aid healing, then place oil made of acacia, aloe, incense, and sarcolaxis on it, and tie it with a bandage, and then wrap it with strips and cloths; the manner of the cloths is that you take soft cloths, fold each one in four, and then put one on top of another according to the quantity that the eyes require; then bind it with a durable bandage form and repeat the leeches or cauterization without cutting again; then remove the leeches and leave the tied oil for a day and night, and if the lien becomes loose, you must tighten it; then remove the lien after the day and night, and if you see the oil healing, that is good; if not, repeat the application of the poultice and cloths and the lien and the leeches until it heals.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	The broken separation of a ruptured membrane
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When disruptions come in the ruptured membrane, it opens and is forced out like grains of paper, which are frightening to see; then you cover it over. The procedure for this is that you insert an awl into the root of the affected area up to where it ends above, followed by another awl or a double-threaded needle from the tear edge; and make it perforate, leaving the first awl as it was; then hold the eye of the double thread and tie a part of the umbilical cord around it, tighten it well, then remove the awl and apply moistened linen oil over it; and let it remain until the threads adhere to the umbilical cord, then treat the oil with soothing things until the wound is healed; and sometimes the wound is restrained by the umbilical cord on both sides of a circular piece of cloth, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes appear large, pierce with a fine spatula that comes from oil, and remove the moisture and soften the eyes, then insert it immediately; then pull it out when it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	From the bone of the oil [it is made]
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	 This disease called "alcunnati" is not foreign but it assembles in oil, resembling an abscess draining, and yet it is not an abscess; and the appearance of its work is that you make the patient sit on a prepared chair and straight, then take the head between your hands from both sides, and move it until you see the abscess come up to your eyes; then it should be lanced, and do not drain and let the light out, and let the patient see things as he is used to; and if it does not drain under, know that it is an abscess, and if the draining of the abscess is not prepared as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 Place the patient sitting between your hands, then take the thin spatula and make it pass through the corneal membrane hole with the cornea and the crown as it moves; and when it comes out, distill it into sharp hot oil mixed with honey or boil water, fenugreek and honey, afterwards treat it with another cure until it heals.
des aigues de l’oil	From the waters of the oil
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	 We have found the similarity of hot waters in the division, and that which is necessary for piercing; do as it suits health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	 It is necessary that you place the patient sitting cross-legged, away from light for the sun, and hold the oil clean and press it very tightly; then take the paper of the oil with your left hand if the eyes are on the left side, or with your right hand if they are on the right side; then take the instrument called "almagda" in your right hand if the eyes are on the left side, or in your left hand if they are on the right side; then place the point of the instrument near the cornea by a quarter inch in that part of the oil at the smaller tear duct, then push the almagda instrument skillfully and keep your hand steady until it pierces through the oil, and you will feel that almagda comes to the empty place; and the measure of the path of the almagda should be at the full extent of the space from the pupil to the end of the iris; this is the cornea of the oil; then you will see the bone through the paper due to the clarity of the corneal membrane, and afterwards place the instrument until it reaches the bone or the water, then press it forcefully down a channel after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	 If it burns now, then the patient sees it before him and the instrument in its oil.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	 After a short rest, if the burn rises again on the second path, set the fire with the instrument, and when it is fully inserted and does not rise further, gently move your hand around it a little; then apply another small amount of gemstone oil inside.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	 Then pour on the ointment made of flax cloth soaked in rose oil and egg, and bind it with the healing oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	 We and those of our time apply on it a mixture made with plenty of eggs.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if almagda cannot enter into the oil due to its hardness, for there are some people who have excessively hard eyes, then you must take the instrument called "alberit", which is as follows:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	 Therefore, only pierce the conjunctive and do not go too deep, but make it subtle; then apply a little pressure as we have said; and when the work is complete, arrange the patient lying on his back in a dark place where he can sleep; and be careful of all movements, and give him light foods, and do not move his head to either side, and bind him according to his disposition until the third day; then unbind him in the same dark place, test his vision, and make him see some things, and then re-bind him for seven more days; and it should not be done during the time of the cure or after the incision now, but it should be done when the burn subsides quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	 If an abscess swells up, you should lance the oil before the seventh day, and pay attention to those who soothe the abscess; and when it is soothed, you should then lance the eye (of the abscess) and place the ointment on its surface to cover for any day, and stay in that dark room immediately.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	 And then go little by little from the house and convert to your chamber; and know that no disciple should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from Iriha, who told us that in his country people pierce alum, so that the pain subsides, but I have never seen anyone do it on our land, nor have I ever read it in the books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the appearances of forms of almadga, for this reason those who do not recognize them will see them; and they are of iron properly speaking:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And their heads are of the same subtlety, and the points in four angles are sharp.
de la char sor le neis	Of the flesh on the neck
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	 Sometimes are born or born cysts of various sorts, and there are some that resemble scorpions with many feet; and if there are such cysts whose skin is darkened by pus, and if the cyst is hard from the bone.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	 In such a case of soft and not hard char, it is necessary that you make the patient sit between your hands towards the sun; open his nostrils, and pour the onion juice onto those chars, and draw them out; then grip what you can support with a sharp and subtle spatula from one side, until you know that that char is entirely stopped.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains any matter which cannot be covered, open it all with subtle and light instruments, so that nothing remains; and if without your protection or abscess covering, it should break, assist it as necessary; and if the abscess is malignant, hurry and cauterize it until the pus is drained and all the charring is removed, then pour in oil or warm water or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	 If it does not open and moisture comes up to the palace (nasal cavity), know that it is healthy; if moisture does not perforate as necessary, know that there is a char bone growing in the bone above, to which the instrument does not come to cut: then bind a thread, somewhat thick but not too large, with your hands and at each knot allow the required space; put the patient's head into the thread at its widest part, and draw it out while smelling (applying pressure) until it comes down through the nose to the mouth; and many times children in school do this, and it is easy for whoever wants to perform it; then hold the chief (bone) coming from the nose with one hand, and the other chief coming from the mouth with the other hand, and know which one follows the other while we who are the thread pull.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	 Perform this action as you know that the nerves have been corrupted in that flesh. Draw out the thread, squeeze the blood, and moisten the thread with Egyptian ointment, then replace it back into the nose as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointment has corroded everything that remains of the flesh. Afterwards, place a plank splint on the nose for some days until it is healed, and if there is a need for drying medicines, use them; this is the form of the instrument to purge the head, as one distills oils and medicines in the nose:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it is made of silver or brass, resembling a lamp with an open top, like a funnel, and guide it in this way; and if you see, make a closed funnel, and have the instruments full for purging the head; and have one handle on the head to hold when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	Of the flesh on the neck
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times a disease called "telul" arises on the head of the neck, which grows and becomes large enough to see; and because of this, you must cut it at the beginning, excise all of it, then put fire cautery or burning medicine on the place; if it is delayed until it becomes large, if it is hard, blackish, with poor sensation: do not touch it with iron as it is an enlarged abscess, for when it is cut once, it causes great harm to the patient; and if the abscess is of soft touch, not blackish, and you can cover it, then empty the patient and cauterize with fear, and treat the place with drying and constricting agents.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the neck is cut and sewn up
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	 Know that when continuous solution comes into one of these cartilage joints, it benefits little, unless in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Therefore, when this happens to anyone, look if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then bring together the two lips to a stitch, then heal it until it is healed; and if the lips have already separated from one side and the other, you must cauterize all the edges of their wound until they heal, then bring together the two lips to a stitch, tighten it, and sprinkle powder of dragon's blood on powdered incense, and apply some plaster of strong or other plaster, and leave it until it dries, then heal it with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of stitching is that you bring the solution together: either with needles, as we have said in the abdomen stitch; or with thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	In the hands of men, there often forms an abscess deep within the lips, resembling grains of wheat, smaller or larger; then you must turn the lips, and cut open each side, take it with tweezers and squeeze in each part; then apply the powdered vitriol to the wound until the pus is drained; and then apply alum to the wound, and treat the wound with dry things until it heals.
de la char des gencives	of the gums (of the teeth)
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.
