Many times a pimple appears on the gums, which the ancients called “albulus”; then you must hold it with tweezers, and squeeze its root, and let the blood flow; then apply vitriol powder or other powders that restrain and dry it; and if the pimple returns after the incision, and this happens often, then squeeze it again and cauterize it; it will not return after the cautery; and these are the instruments to cover (the wound).
des sordens	The sores
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes there are sores around the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, rough and harsh sores; and sometimes the teeth are black and yellow and decaying when corruption comes to the gum, and the teeth stink; you must make the patient sit between your hands, and his head should be in your lap, and you should remove the sores or the roughness that appear, until nothing remains; and do the same for the blackness and greenness, and the yellow and other spots, until they are cleaned; and if you remove what is there at first sight, it is good; but if not, start again on the second day and third, as long as you have completely cleaned them; and know that the teeth need different forms of instruments for cleaning, according to what the work demonstrates, because the instrument used to clean the teeth has other forms than that used between the teeth; and these forms and others should be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you treat the tooth of its pain that you delay drawing it out as much as possible, for this should not be done at all; for this is a very high substance up to which there is no excuse for scraping.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	 When the patient must draw the tooth, you must be certain of the root direction.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	 Many times, the patient experiences pain and believes it to be toothache, and draws out the bad tooth; however, the pain does not subside until the rotten part is removed, for we have seen this happen with these people; and when you are certain about the tooth that needs to be pulled, you must first scrape around the tooth thoroughly with a strong spatula to protect the gum from all sides; then press it with your fingers or delicate pliers at the base of the tooth, little by little, until it is completely loosened, then tighten the pliers firmly; and keep the patient's head between your knees so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	 After pulling the tooth correctly to break it, if it does not come out by itself, take one of these instruments and gently push it from each side, and move it as you did before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	 And if the tooth is pierced and eaten, you must fill it with cloths where the holes are; and if you pull it gently with the pliers so as not to break while pulling; and very carefully operate around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	 Make sure you do not break it and leave a part behind, because the patient will suffer greater pains from the root later due to the injury.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	 And beware that you do not act like ignorant lords who in their haste and recklessness often break the cart (teeth), and they do not bring what we have mentioned; but they sometimes cause great disease for the roots that remain or for the broken tooth, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is pulled, wash the area with wine or water and oil, and if bleeding occurs, which often happens, use vitriol powder; and if it does not work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of the instruments, with which one silences the teeth first, should have long points and large handles, so they do not double when you extract the tooth; and these are their shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And should be large handles so they do not bend when pulling, and made of good iron, and have teeth for holding on.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the tooth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	 When the root remains at traction, you must put cotton soaked in butter on it for a day or two.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	 while the joints are softened, then insert the pliers called "algefri", making the head look like a beak of a pincer; and inside make it as smooth as a chisel, which is its shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these tools, then you must expose the flesh entirely around the root, and place the instrument called "althali," which is known as palancha, of this form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And it should be thick and large so as not to break it, and if the root jumps out through those tools, that is good; if not, help with all the instruments, from which the shapes come after:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you use an instrument with two prongs, of this form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	And other instruments which are before the teeth, and of this tool that seems like large pincers, whose shape is as follows:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And it should not break, and know that many instruments of the teeth are; and also other instruments, which are not counted; and the wise masters find their tools by themselves, according to what their work and the illness indicate, for there are such diseases where the old masters did not teach any tool because of the diversity of ailments, and if it breaks a chariot or another bone, or if it could, then seek the instruments that are required, which I have told you, and help with gestures, as follows:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And they should be large and sturdy to hold the bone and not slip, but it can hold and extract; then restore the joint with appropriate medicines, and if there is pus in the bone, and it is small, use this entire instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When teeth appear not according to natural shape, and the form is ugly, even in girls, you should know that if the tooth is not born after the gum, and it is not correctly positioned, and cannot be straightened or filed: drill (it); and if it is exposed with the tooth, take this tool whose shape is like a small beak, made of hard steel at the tip:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the handle of the copper instrument is held for long hours due to the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the others; if it appears that one can file it, then file it with a small flat file like this shape:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and is similar to the file used to make needles; and file the tooth gently for long hours until it stops hurting; then plane the end with any rasp, and if the tooth is too sharp and bites the tongue, you must file the sharpness until it is even, so that it does not hurt the tongue or corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the teeth fall out
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	 When the teeth are about to loosen, either by percussion or falling out, and the patient cannot press up on it when they eat, making them fall out, and you have treated them with constricting medicines, but that does not help; then they must be held in place with a gold thread, for silver threads turn green and rot, but gold never changes; and the gold thread should be medium-sized neither too thick nor too thin, according to the space between the teeth; and if you see the teeth moving, take the thread and double it between the two healthy teeth, then insert the pliers between the loose teeth, if there are one or more, until you reach the healthy tooth on the other side; then continue covering up until the part where you started, and hold your hand gently but firmly so it does not move; and tie the thread to the root of the tooth so it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	 Then thread the shoulders with a wire using pliers, and align them, and put them back in their proper place so they do not cause bleeding; then leave it as tight as it can stay in place, and if it dislocates or the wires break, hold it in place with another wire; if it stays and serves for that time, and this is the form of teeth and the arrangement of the two healthy teeth and the two molars, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, put it back in its place, as we have said; and let no one interfere who is not wise and patient, and sometimes the shape of a bone tooth is made and placed where the lack exists, and hold it together as we have said, and remain and serve for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	To cover the ligament of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	 There is sometimes a ligament that comes beneath the tongue or is born in this way; or by accident of sutured wounds; and the operation is such that you open the mouth of the patient, hold his head steady, and lift the tongue; then take hold of the nervous ligament with a wide grip, until the tongue is dislocated from its place, and if it is hard or swollen, and this is due to sutured wounds, put in an uncine and widen the grip on the ligament; and make sure that the incision is not too deep, for the artery that is below; and when you have done this, lift the limb from warm water and oil, then place a linen tent under the tongue; and tighten the patient's limbs each night so they do not heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	 And if blood flow comes out, put on it vitriol powder; and if the wound bleeds, cauterize it with the slow cautery (or cauterizing iron), which is good for this purpose; then cure it with another remedy until it heals.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you see it (the wound) of pale color or black or hard, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is a cancer; and if it is declining towards a blister and there is moisture, pour unguent onto it, and loosen it from both sides with a thin spatula; and if the wound weeps at your work, apply vitriol powder until it is drained, then return to your work until you drain all of it; then lift fresh lambskin or silk and treat it with other remedies until it heals.
des apostemes de la gorge	abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	 Sometimes inside the throat there come swellings called "godath", which are properly called almonds, and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, be careful: if it is a hard abscess of small size and pale color, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	 And if it is red and the root is thick, do not touch it with iron, also because of blood flow; but let it be until it becomes soft, and then you will separate it, or it will break by itself; and if it is of white color round, and the root is slender, prepare the instrument for covering, but first examine whether the abscess has cooled down and been soothed.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	 Then make the patient sit in front of the sun, and his shoulders be healthy, and he opens his mouth wide and the servant takes hold of it between his hands, pressing the tongue down to the instrument, as shown here; and it should be made of silver or thin bronze, like a knife.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Can you press the tongue with the whole instrument, and you see the abscess, take the hook and pierce it into the mandible, and draw it upwards more than you can; and draw any cloth away from it, then strike with the instrument, which is its form, resembling a spear; but be aware that the head is curved, one end towards the other, and they are very sharp, made of iron or bronze:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, hold the object with pliers, of which shape is as follows:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And if you do not have this instrument present, hold the object with pincers, of which shape is as follows:
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	 And I treated a woman of an abscess that was inside the throat, to wit an abscess of small size; and I had tightly closed the entire throat, so that the woman could not breathe through the constricted passage, nor eat or drink, and she would have died if she had remained in that state for a day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	 The abscess was so high that it had to be cut into two through the two passages of the throat.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	 I immediately thrust it then, and pierced through one side, afterwards pulled it far away, and through that great hole in the bowel; afterwards I set right the other wound near the nose, and opened his mouth and pressed his tongue; afterward I pierced through that side into the abscesses, and cut off a part of it, and no more blood came out but a little; and thus the throat of the woman was detached, and she began to drink water and then wine, and did not stop cutting off from that abscess for long times; and the abscesss grew again immediately, and filled up the hole I had made, so much so that it became very large; therefore I tricked him and cauterized inside his throat. Thus it remained without growing; and I left those parts, and only God did something with them after me.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	 When it protrudes at the eye and is swollen and long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is large and round beneath, it is called "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	 When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not improve, and you see that the abscesses are eased, and it is subtle, then you must cut it; and that which is round and gathered but not long; and it is bloody or of thin color or black, then you should avoid cutting it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	 For there is great danger for the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	 Therefore, when you see it (the eye), as I have said in the manner, of its bladder and length, you must make the patient sit before the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument that we have mentioned before; then pierce the onion into the eye, and pull it out, and cut it at the two places (2-3 millimeters) that I have said in the incision of the two almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And you must not cover any more than the surplus that is beyond the natural limit; for if you do so, it harms the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what has been said in the incision of the two anuses, and cure it until it heals.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	 And if the patient fears covering [the affected area], then you must use an instrument for the cauterization to alleviate his fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	 The manner of cautery is sharp and hot.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	 The patient must place his head in your lap, and then press his tongue against the instrument mentioned in the cauterization chapter, and hold it with sharp hot iron, but not too thick or too clear; and use the handle of this instrument, which is shaped as follows:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And have a hair or a piece of cloth where medicine is placed, like the handle of a spoon, and put the instrument completely over the medicine on the eye; and let the patient lie on his side, so that the saliva and mucus flows from his mouth into the medicine, but does not go down the throat or nose; then hold your hand over the entire medicine and press it on the eye, for about half an hour, until you see the swelling and pain of the medicine subside; and if you see, take cotton and wrap it around some instrument, wet the cotton in the medicine, and insert the instrument into the sheath above, so that the cotton adheres to the eye; and do this frequently, until the cauterization is complete, then let it dry, and wait for four or five days. And if you need to reapply the cauterization of the medicine, do so, and after the cauterization rinse around the eye with a cotton swab dipped in warm water, and clean what is around the medicine; and apply cool water and gargle until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is more effective than incision, not the cautery; if it is cured by fumigation in this manner, take camomile and hyssop and origanum and rue and chamomile and wormwood and similar herbs, and put them all together or any of them in one pot, and place it on a fire; and let the pot be well sealed with strong earth, and in the pot have one instrument hairy according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	 And it shall be silver or lead, and one of the heads pushed into the mouth of the patient until the vapor rises to the eye through the canal, until the eye is putrefied; afterwards it frequently recurs, until the eye dries up, and ensure that you do not perform this at the beginning of the abscess's eruption, for many things happen; and do not do it unless during the decline of the abscess's eruption.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	 If this is not present, take a canal and put an eggshell crack into the patient's head so that the mouth does not get too hot; for the eggshell does not let the vapor burden the mouth, and it is good healing together with salvation.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times an eel or spine of fish, or something else is lodged in the throat; therefore, you must draw out what you can see, and press the tongue to the sun with the entire instrument so that you can see movement; and if it does not open and is pushed back into the throat, the patient should vomit as soon as the food is cooked in the stomach; by chance, this may dislodge the thing. Or, the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of soap, or a radish root, or one morsel of dry bread; tie one thread to the sponge, and then swallow it; and when it comes to the place, it will stick, and you will draw it out again. And if it does not come out as we have said, take a splint of wood according to this shape:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instrument be curved at the head so that it can enter the throat more easily, and raise the head high; and watch that you do not touch the epiglottis, as it would die or push the bone inside; it is better if the patient pushes the instrument, because he will move or the thing is loosened; if he pushes downwards, or pull it out completely to equalize the instrument, until it is out.
de la sansue de la gorge	the windpipe of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	 At no time is the saliva of the patient considered as medicine, as I mentioned in the division, through the treatment of medicines; and when it does not benefit, then look at the throat of the sick person in the sunlight, since you press the tongue with the instrument that I told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	 And if you see the saliva, draw it out very carefully with a small spoon or delicate tweezers suitable for this purpose.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	 And if that does not work, take a heated iron and put it in the throat of the sick person, and do this frequently.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	 And anoint the patient with water all day long.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	 Then take a full glass of cold water, open the mouth, and pour it in to rinse, moving it with your hand frequently; and as soon as the saliva senses the water, it falls out.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	 And if it does not fall as we have said, you should sedate the patient with anesthetic, using the instrument that I mentioned for anesthetizing the eye; do this many times, for it will surely bleed.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	 The method of anesthesia is as follows: you take the pot that has charcoal in it and cover it with a cloth pierced in the middle, and place the head of the instrument inside it; then pour your anesthetic, and the patient puts the head of the cane in his mouth, and closes his mouth so that the smoke does not escape but comes up to his nose; and the smoke will now make him sleep, and if he does not fall asleep, you should repeat the anesthesia many times; let the patient suffer thirst, and eat salty and alkaline things and drink nothing; and then it will be necessary for him to release urine through this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	The form of the instrument with which to treat the snake, is such that when it can be seen, resembles curved pincers for entering the throat; and has the shape of a syringe's tip, and it should have a liming sharpness so that what it takes, it cannot lose; and here is its form:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapters on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	 Many abscess-like symptoms appear, as remembered below in this book from one and the other; they are different in perforation and incision; and it is in two ways that one resembles its likeness, and because it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	 And the second way is for the lymph nodes that are within the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	 For abscesses in the head are different than those in the body, and abscesses of the charntre (lymph nodes) are different from those that come in the joints; each should be judged separately in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	 And if there are abscesses that should not be pierced until the bowel is ripe according to its completion; and those of such kind that it is necessary to pierce when they are hardened, but do not die according to their completion, as abscesses that come near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	 For when an abscess comes from a joint, and it is left until it bursts on its own, possibly the ligament and nerve of the joint may be corrupted, causing contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	 For when an abscess comes from the main body part and you delay the perforation until it has ripened, this will damage the main body part; or if it is located at the base, one should pierce it as soon as it has ripened; and should not perforate an abscess without complete digestion, except when it is located at the base, which cannot be opened fully, and become elongated inside, and a fistula forms, and cannot heal in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And you should know the time of piercing the abscess that is ripe according to its completion, and it is when the pain is alleviated, and the departure of the fever, and the decrease of pain and redness, and the swelling and movement of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and you should make the piercing sit where the abscess depends more closely, and where it has opened; and let the piercing be long in the body, and if the abscesses are in the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all even places where there is no plaque.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	 In those that fall, according to that limb.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	 And when an abscess is in a charned place, it is beneficial to leave the perforation until it is confirmed by complete digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	 For if you pierce it beforehand, the body will flow from it, and it will be full of much filth; and by chance, the lips may harden and it will become sealed off.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	 And if there is any abscess that needs to be pierced according to the size of the body, as required by the limb.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	 And it is necessary to make small incisions for small abscesses and large incisions for large abscesses, and many cuts according to the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where caution is required, they should be covered; when they have become as a cloth and swollen, it should be treated in the same way as for babies: and if there are those that are cut into three angles or such that are covered like the leaf of myrtle, like abscesses of the joints; and if there are such where a round incision is made and other incisions, they should be treated accordingly.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	 Who have no head, as an abscess superficially, it should be pierced fully; and when the abscess is large and has collected much pus, and you pierce it, do not draw out all the pus in that hour, but only a part; stop up the abscess until the next day, then draw nothing crooked; do this many times gradually, until the pus disappears; likewise, if the patient is weak or a woman bearing, or small children, or old men debilitated.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	 The pus sometimes spasms with the release of the pus, which may accidentally cause the death of the patient, but you need not worry about it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Therefore, be extremely careful with this chapter, and when you have opened your abscess, drain the wound, and check if the wound from the abscess is small; and if it is a large one, bring linen or old cotton bandages; and if it is a large abscess and there is much pus, you must place a bandage in each one so that they come against each other; and if you have cut into the abscess part of the skin, and you have shaved around it, you must fill it with old cotton or linen gauze without moisture, tie it until the third day; then open it, and cure it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	 And if bleeding occurs in your work, apply cold water and linen, wet the cloth, and place it on the wound repeatedly.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the bleeding persists, provide treatment and care, and the powders I have mentioned in this book should be used on the wounds or abscesses; if it is winter, or the wound or abscess is very nervous, then you must place hot towels and cloths soaked in wine and oil on top of them; if it is summer, and the wound is fleshy, then you must place hot cloths soaked in water and oil, or cold water and oil, for three days as we have said; then drain the abscess, dress it, and cure it until it heals.

des soros	This means "of sores".
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	 For small abscesses at the head, there are ways known to us that are in cloths, as the gardener of a linen plant, and there are many similarities.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	 There are some fat and similar ones that have moisture like pulses; and there are some hard and stony ones in the cutting, without any doubt that the arteries do not oppose it.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	 And the work of cutting is that you prove with all instruments called "entre-missoire", from which the form comes afterwards, what it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	 If it contains moisture, they do it above the long one.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	 And when the moisture is emptied, they scrape without leaving any hair that contains the moisture, because it returns immediately if left; then put cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present; if not, in vinegar and oil, and apply it to the wound, and leave it until the next day; and those who are delayed at night will be healed.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés. And if in any of these abscesses or head, there is no moisture, and those were the abscesses that I treated or the head of an old woman; and I found the abscess as hard as a stone, rough and white, and could not break it; and if one had pierced it with anything, one would have made a wound like from a stone.

des scrophules	of scrofulas
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	 Often this abscess occurs at the neck, under the jawbones, in hollows, and sometimes it appears elsewhere on the body, and they are large and are connected to each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	 And each scrofula is properly within its side, as the neck and the abscess of the head, as we have said; and there are many similarities to these scrofulas.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	 Some contain moisture, and some are malicious ones that do not wish to obey health.

In the one that you see with good position on the shoulder, and resembling the color of the body, and mute in every part and not pierced by the neck or the artery or the vein, and not rotten; you must cut it from above, peel off each side, and place the two lips of the incision as close together as possible, if you need to, as we have said about the abscesses of the head; and draw it out little by little, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve or the vein, and do not use the spatula or lancet too deep, so that the hand does not slip, and look carefully before you cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	 And if you open the vein or artery and it does not yield, put vitriol powder into the wound, or some powders that stop blood, and hold the wound; let it remain until the abscess is pacified, and the wound softened and begins to rot.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.
