Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	 If there is a vein running deep in the root of the scrofula, it is not necessary that you cut the scrofula at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread and let it hang, without harm; then treat the wound with old cotton dipped in Egyptian ointment, then cure it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	 And if you excise the entire scrofula, it is necessary that you bring together the two lips of the wound and stitch them now because there should be no excess remaining due to the largeness of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	 It is necessary that you understand how to cover the root of it and draw out pus, and stitch it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Those scrofulas with excess, pierce there where the pus has accumulated; and pierce it as described earlier, on that spot, then introduce lints with ointment and similar things so that they corrode what remains of corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, cure it with healing ointment until it heals.
de squinance	And if you lancet a sciatic vein (swelling in the lower limb), you must cauterize the opening with a hot iron and bind it up, then keep the leg raised for seven days without moving it; otherwise there will be excessive bleeding.
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke of the measurement of the throat, but I have never seen anyone do it in our land, and this is their written word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those who have squinancy, it is necessary that the throat slit called "epiglote" should be opened; and no aid should be given by these, because all the veins and the pore of the sick person are in those who have an abscess hot in the mouth, or in the throat, or in two tonsils.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the sickness is in the channel of the pore, it is necessary to cover the epiglote to avoid the destruction that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	 Therefore, when we want to cut the epiglottis, it should be cut below three circles or four small slits across, between two circles or by the size of the incision without damaging the cartilage; and these parts are suitable for cutting the epiglottis such that there is no cartilage present, and the vessels are long enough.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	 If the master is afraid, he must stretch out the skin of the throat to its full length, then cut the neck until it reaches the windpipe; and cut away any blood vessels that you see, and then chop the cartilage as we have said; and this is demonstrated by the sectioning of the gland in the windpipe that jumps out when the throat is broken, and by the lack of voice; and leave the wound open for a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the hour has passed in which there is doubt about strangulation, bring together the two edges of the wound with care, and sew it all around the cartilage; then administer medications that cause pus to form, until it heals.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albuscasis says that this should not be done until the throat is completely stopped up, and the patient has been judged to be dead, and the bird removed from him.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	 Then you should press on the throat because the patient cannot swallow, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is guarded from death; and for this, the ancients instruct to keep the wound open until the malice of the disease has passed, which it does in three or four days. And then they would command to sew up the wound and cure it when it was cured; and I will tell you what I have seen.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	 I saw a young woman take the knife and thrust it into her throat and sew part of her windpipe; and I was called to treat her, and found her as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I found the wound, and saw the blood flowing from it, and knew that she had not coughed or breathed except through the throat, and the wind passed through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	 I quickly sewed up the wound and cured it until she was well; and no harm came to the woman except that her voice was hoarse, and she returned to her normal state; for this reason I say that in such a situation of the throat one should not be afraid.
de la grosse gorge	from the thick throat   (in this context, "gorge" refers to the neck)
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	 This abscess is called "hernia of the throat," and it is a large abscess in color like a bladder, and it is most common in women; and it occurs in two ways: natural, and accidental; where natural has no artificial cause.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 And the accidental is also of two types, one resembling fatty lumps and the other resembling an abscess that comes from an artery; and there should be fear, and no force should be applied except in small ones, and it must be proven and searched through the intromissoire: if you find it as hard as fat, and it does not yield to any pressure, if you squeeze it, as one squeezes lumps, and pull it out completely, if there is any; and surround it well, and cure it as necessary until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	The bones   (the affected area being the bones)
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	 Many ways of us are, which I will describe all their similarities; and now it is necessary that I say the entire difference between a notch and an opening.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that an ulcer is heat and continuous fever until the eruption has passed, and the purulent matter has been completed; then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	 A notch has no heat, fever, or pain, and contains a cyst that is its own sac and is according to the color of the body, and begins like an ulcer, and becomes large; and it is similar in two ways, either fatty, or moist, and they are mostly colored as I have said in division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the treatment of the knot, that you test and inquire first about all the instrument called "entromissoire", according to its form or chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	 And the method of the incision of the abscesses is to take the moistest place you find in the abscess and turn your fingers little by little until you feel that the straw has pierced the core, then according to the size of the abscess; then remove the contents, and be careful not to let it burst.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	 If moisture flows from the wound, let it be colored as I have said for other abscesses; and if afterwards no moisture comes out of the opening, know that it is filled with pus, then make a cross-shaped incision, take hold with the forceps, peel it gently on both sides and pull the affected area where it lies, ensuring you remove it whole along with the thread; and if you cannot remove it whole, remove it in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	 If something remains, it returns many times and if a small amount remains and troubles you, apply some corrosive powders to the wound, hold it closed, apply warm things to alleviate the abscess, and treat it with other remedies until it is healed; and if it grows large, cut it in two at the edge of the wound and treat the surrounding flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the vein beats against you or otherwise is in opposition and you hurry and use vitriol powder, leave it lying for 2 to 4 days, until the wound heals, and let the inflammation of the blood subside; then apply the ointment where it has remained unhealed.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	 Behold the shapes of the probing instruments, and there are three kinds: large, medium, and small; and within them are three cross-shaped ones called "albarets," and one called "breb," and there are also three kinds for encircling abscesses: large, medium, and small; they resemble the needles used to sew shirts, and are made of citron wood, iron, or silver; those that are yellow are more valuable, and are sharper for encircling fistula openings; they come in three sizes: large, medium, and small, according to the width of the wounds.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	 The shapes of these forceps are in many forms as you see here: large, medium, and small; they also have forceps with two prongs in three ways; they have forceps with three prongs, in three ways; they also have forceps with two prongs, and some have only one prong, and there are three types of each. All these are necessary for their use.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	 The first part of the shoulder that is cut into is sharp, and those who do not cut deep from one side only are at risk of injuring the vein or nerve; and in these cases, the arteries are tied off before they are cut, so that the patient does not feel pain when abscesses are opened; and there are three types: large, small, and medium, as you can see; and they are not used anywhere except in charnut regions, such as legs, arms, breasts, and groins, and sometimes a smaller tool is used, similar to fistula scissors, according to this shape, for draining blood.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is placed at times on the joint that heals from veins, and arteries, and sometimes it returns in this large shape:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	 Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they start to decay, until they resemble female breasts; and they remain ugly and swollen. Whoever wants to treat them must do so according to this form from line b to g:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	 Then cut the fat, apply medicine to the wound with soothing herbs, then bring together the two edges of the wound and sew them shut, and let it heal until it is healed; if it swells downwards and is flattened by its size as happens with women, make two incisions above it, in the shape of two fissures; so that one remains attached to the other at the end of each, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line .b. up to line .g.; then cut the skin between the two edges, remove the fat, and bring what we have said about sewing and powders, and whatever is necessary for the cure, until it heals; if it does not heal or the incision is not complete because the patient does not want to rest or due to bleeding, you must fill the wound with cotton soaked in corrosive ointment; leave it until it softens the remaining fat and wound, then let it heal until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses on the buttocks
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come beneath the buttocks are handled as hard scrofulas where there is a hardness, and if they contain moisture within them.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	 Those who contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from line b up to line g:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the entire cavity in the abscess is emptied, you should use old cotton on the wound and leave it until the next day; then remove all the cotton, and apply ointment to it until it heals.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is similar to scrofula, you should treat it as we have said in cutting scrofula, and if the wound forms a cavity, you should apply a fire cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	Of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	 When the artery is ruptured and the skin above it becomes attached, there are often abscesses, and the same happens with a swollen vein and an abscess; if one recognizes it by the artery, the abscess is long in depth; when you feel it with your fingers, you should feel it tightly; and when it is due to the vein, it appears round on the outside; it is foolish to cut this abscess, especially when it is under the joints and angles, and when it is at the neck and near other important places, and it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	1. Therefore, the treatment with iron must be avoided for one who is ill and for the one at the head, as well as in one who has a swelling of an artery beneath the skin; then open the abdomen in a regular fashion, cut out the artery carefully from the layers, until it is exposed; then place an awl under it and pierce it to the opposite side, and bind the artery with a double thread as I have shown you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples; then hold the part between the two ligaments with an intromissoire until the swelling subsides which is there, and cut off the abscess; then apply the treatment of a bowstring, until the ligament gives way; then treat it with ointment as needed, until it heals; and if the abscess is due to a vein opening, then you should mark your hand with the color of the abscess over the entire skin, then pierce the awl under the part which you hold in your hand, and let it penetrate, and have the thread double, so that you draw it from the opposite side; then tie the abscess as I said, or a ligament of one of the two sides with the thread; and if you doubt whether the threads will pass through, then insert another awl along the entire length of the thread under the abscess at the incision of the first awl, and bind the threads in four places; then compress the abscess until the excess subsides, then compress the excess and leave what is bound; then place a damp cloth soaked in wine and oil on it, then apply treatments of tents and ointments until it heals.
des apostemes des ners	From abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	As abscesses come in the artery and the vein, so abscesses come to the nerves when they are wounded or from too great work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	 And this often occurs in the shoulder and the thumb and in all joints where there are joints, and it is called an abscess, and its color appears similar to that of the body, and it is in various positions causing pain; and when it is forcibly squeezed, the patient feels pain, and it is not entirely within the body, but beneath the skin; and it is quiet in all directions, and does not go forward or backward, neither under nor over, and the one who is in joints should not be covered with iron: perhaps contraction would occur; and if it is in the head or the forehead, cut open the skin.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the abscess is small, hold it with tweezers and strike its root; if it is large, pierce it at the edge, peel off the skin, then bone and close the wound with stitches, and let it heal until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	Large lumps hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	 Sometimes it happens in bellies and nowhere else, and it is a disease called "funge," resembling mushrooms, and it has subtle roots and large heads; and there are small and very large ones; and I have seen a man who had two bellies that resembled mushrooms more than anything else, and there was no difference between them, and they were white, and had fine roots, and were cut open, and moisture flowed from them continuously.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	 I weighed and found one at 18 ounces, the other at 6 pounds, and when the incision is made you can see if the patient is moist, and the color of the internal organ is pale and wet with a fine root; if you cut it widely, have the fire cautery ready in your presence.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	 For in the thigh there often come very large hemorrhages of blood, and if it overwhelms [the patient], then hurry to cauterize; and if you see the patient frightened and afraid of the iron incision, take fine thread carefully made, tie it around the artery as we have said, and leave it for two days; and then tighten it, and do not stop tightening the thread until it stops the flow, and feels a hard pressure; and if the roots are large, be cautious about pressing it completely due to the stomach, but you can certainly press half of it, then cauterize so that it does not return; then cure the wound, and make sure you do not cauterize the part which is of dark color and poor sensation and milky eyesight.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this abscess has grown large, and I will come to treat this syphilis afterwards.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the boil is mature
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	 If the appearance of the boil comes from cautery of a wound or a fissure in the bladder, and it is above the abdomen and in some of the testicles, as happens in other routes, or from blood that leaks from veins or arteries, according to what is beforehand, or due to windiness; and if it comes through the route of the bladder and through the exit of the bowel, then the color of the abscess resembles the color of the body, and it is a light thing without pain, and wide in various openings.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is by the exit of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when pressed with hands, it returns and comes back again, and in some cases may become hardened, and increases greatly at the entrance of the bath and through heavy labor.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	 And if it is due to moisture, it is a light thing and wide when you press it with your hand, but do not constrain it; and if it is due to blood, the abscesses are large and hard, and are filled according to a quantity; and if it is due to windiness, it is soft to the touch, and the work indicates that you look to see if the appearance is due to the blood of an artery or vein, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	 It is necessary to let the treatment rest.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	 For there is doubt and fear, as I have said in the chapter on abscesses, about the artery and the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	 And if the appearance is due to the intestine or bowel, you must command the patient to strain his anus, and stretch out straight, then lean down all around the belly; then command him to press gently between your hands, then go around the place that you have signaled with a spatula, then extend half of the abscess above the great spoon; then tie it tightly with a strong thread or a strong cord made of strong silk, and leave the patient to hold onto the string; then open half of the extended abscess over the string, and insert your finger, and search for the intestine; if you find it caught by the string, release it, and push the intestine out of the belly; and if you find a bowel, take it with the spoon, and cut off the superfluous part; and if the artery or vein opposes, go around carefully, then return to your work and take two needles, and insert two sharp points, and place them around what you have made in the shape of a cross that you pierce; then press the abscess for four leagues above the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, and leave the place as it is until it becomes soft, and cut the dead flesh as it becomes soft and can be removed, then cure it according to what is necessary, and close the abscess as we have said; and draw out the pus or moisture that you find, then cure the place according to what is necessary, and stitch the place.
dou chancre	The pustule
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division the likenesses of pustules, and how one should treat them with medicines, and how one should choose the cure of iron; and we shall say what a pustule is, and great caution must be taken in its cure, and the ancients said that when pustules are in a place where they can be shaved like a pustule on a mamel, and in the thigh, and in similar places, one should remove it completely when it begins; and when it is large and old, it is not good to approach it, for I never knew anyone who could heal it; nor has anyone healed it before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the operations, when it is in a place where it can be removed as we have said, are that you purge the patient once with black bile; then make him purge if there is manifest distention, then shave the patient one good length for the operation; then take your lancet or pustule, and shave off all hair and flesh from all parts, leaving nothing remaining; and allow the blood to flow freely, and anoint the wound well with your hand or something else, and if the discharge of blood makes you hesitate about incision of the artery or vein, cauterize it until the wound is cauterized; then treat it with other medicines until it is healed.
de ydropisie	Of hydropisy

We have told in the division the ways of stone, and extraction along with medicines; and I have said the difference between the stone embedded in the flesh, and all the signs, and in which stone one should operate by cutting; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell it openly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is embedded in the bladder occurs more often in children, and this is a sign that the urine jumps from the bladder like water in its subtlety; it opens a small hole, and the patient's penis swells, and it pains him many times, and then wraps itself up again; and often the foundation of these jumps causes the stone to move downwards; and the healing of children is quick until they reach four years old, and it is very difficult in the elderly, and it is among the middle-aged, for those who are between youth and old age; and the cure is easier for those who have large stones, than for those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	 And when we come to the treatment, it is first necessary to cleanse the patient by enema, to draw out all the filth that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	 For it sometimes blocks the stone from being sought after.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	 Then take the patient by the feet, bend and move them downwards, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and sometimes upwards a little; then make him sit between your prepared hands, and his hands should be below his hips, so that the bladder is completely declined downwards; then grasp it and feel inside; if you feel the stone in the space, hurry now to cut above the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	 And if it does not fall to the touch, you should anoint your left hand with oil, if the patient is a child, or use your finger, if the patient is an adult; and push it into its foundation, feel for the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, make it go towards the neck of the bladder; then press upwards with your finger, and push it out in the direction where you intend to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And instruct the assistant to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend his right hand above the testicles, and with his left hand push aside the skin that is below the testicles in the area where they make the incision; then insert the spatula, which is shaped like this:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	 And they make it between what is between the coccyx and the sacrum, not in the middle but on the left side of the lower back; and it should be straight above the pelvis, and your hands should be at its base or the pelvis, and let the opening be wide along the length but narrow within, according to the size of the bone, not too large; by chance, the hand that is at the base might press, causing it to jump out unexpectedly; and know that there is such a bone or it has angles and edges: it is groin-like to be extracted; and if it is rounded, like a plum stone, and convex, from where the opening is light.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	 Then if it has edges and margins, make the incision larger; and if it does not jump out, you must pull on pliers that resemble a chisel at the tip to force the bone back into place; or you press down with a subtle curved instrument at the tip; and if you cannot maneuver it in this way, spread open the wound slightly, and scrape it with vitriol; and if there are more than one bone, push on the largest one first near the bladder hole, then strike, pull it out, and remove the smaller ones afterwards.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	 And if it is very large, it must be made larger by making a bigger incision.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	 There are two things that happen to the patient: either he dies or urine comes out constantly because the wound cannot heal; but despite this, try to drain it, or break the nails with pliers as you pull it apart piece by piece; and when you have completed your work, fill the wound with incense, aloe and dragon's blood, and bind it up, and place a damp cloth soaked in oil and wine, or oil and cold rosewater and cold water, to cool the abscess; then make the patient lie down on his neck, and do not loosen the binding until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you dislocate [the limb], anoint it very well with oil and water, then treat it with ointment of dyafinicon and ointment of basilicon until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	 And if abscesses boil up in the wound and corrode the flesh, and if blood congeals in the bladder, causing urine to be retained which is known in this way that without straining with urine: then put your finger into the wound, and draw out that blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder and the urine will flow; then lift up the wound from pus and pus-like matter and skin, and help in every possible way that you know until it heals; and it is necessary that all the wounds that you treat, that you tie them with two bandages, and place the medicines on top.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	 If the wound is small and it is conducted by the penis and pierced through, and urine cannot flow out of it; then treat it as I say before, that you cut it several times, or else the wound will not heal due to this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	 I have already experienced this way.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take a piece of iron in this shape with four corners pierced into one thong:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	 Then take the thread and tie it around the base of the stone [inside the bladder], so that it does not come back into the bladder; then gently push the probe into the base of the stone; and gradually turn the probe in the stone little by little, until you can pierce the stone from the other side; soon after, urine will come, then press your hand on those parts that remain inside the stone within the bladder.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If it is broken and falls out with the urine, the patient will be cured; if you cannot do this due to some obstacle, tie the thread under the stone and one above, then push the probe towards the stone between the two threads, pull it out, release the thread, and clean the congealed blood in the wound; treat it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	from the stone of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It happens that stones appear in women, and if it ever occurs, it is a serious matter, and it is forbidden for four reasons: one is that by chance the woman may be a virgin; and the second is because one cannot find a wise woman who reveals herself to mirrors, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	 And the third method is that by chance one cannot find a woman well skilled in this art of hands; and the fourth method is that the stone of the woman is deeper than that of a man, therefore it requires a deeper incision, and much fear there is. If such necessity arises, then you must take a midwife who knows, and if one is not found, cast your subtle gaze; and present a wise matron in the art of women's matters, or a woman who knows some part of the craft, and command her to do as you command for the incision of the stone; and carefully observe whether the woman is a virgin: then you must put your thumb or bottom and seek the stone; and if she finds it, you should force it beneath her thumb, and command her to push with her hand on the left side of the bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	 If it is found, you should move it gradually from the entrance of the bladder to below, all the way until it reaches the root of the thigh; then strike on the stone in the root of the thigh near the round bone, where the bone is moving, and feel the stone in that part; do not move your hand above or below the stone, and make the first incision small; then press the opening tightly so that the stone can exit as easily as possible, and know that there are many types of stones: such as small and large, rough and smooth, long and round, and those with rains.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	 know the appearances to understand the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	 And if the bone protrudes, put vitriol powder on it and hold it in place for an hour until the bone stops bleeding; then return to your work, until the pain subsides, and have instruments that I told you about for the extraction of the stone in humans to assist you in your work; and if the bone protrudes again, and it is an artery that was cut, put powder on the area and hold it with tourniquets and bandages, do not continue this, and leave the bone and do not pull it out, as the patient might die; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	When the heat of the blood has subsided and the limb can be moved, if the arrowhead is still in, return to your work until the arrowhead comes out by itself.
de hernie carnouse	of a hernia carnivorous
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	The first sentence to translate:
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the production of this ramice is due to weakness that comes from the kidneys, and the matter spreads out.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	 Sometimes there is percussion on the skull, and this moisture may have various colors: either it declines to yellow, or without redness, or black, or whitish, and this happens more often; and these are the signs to recognize this assembly, for if it is white as we have said, it is a good abscess, long like an egg, and do not open the skull, because there is moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	 And if there is moisture in the very cloth [bandage], it is believed that abscesses are reasoned with a part of the egg; and if the moisture is between the skin and the flesh, one can feel it well; therefore, to know the color of the moisture, probe it thoroughly, so you may know its form as described before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what follows after the incision, judge what is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when we treat the patient with fire [cautery], it is necessary that the patient be purified according to our ability and the fullness of their body; then place them on their back, on something slightly elevated, and lay many cloths under them; then sit on their left side, and command the assistant to sit on the right, and extend the arm at one of the two shoulders closest to the neck; then take the spatula, pierce the skin between them along its length until reaching the flesh white, and peel the skin subtly according to our ability; then pierce the white flesh deeply with water, drain all the water, then put your fingers, and close the white flesh above; do not touch the neck, but only the white flesh; strike everything or in pieces delicately the costal part of it, so that if you do not strike it correctly, the water will return; and if the egg bursts during your work, reset it to its place when you have completed the white flesh procedure; then stitch the two shoulders together at a suture, and treat the wound as others, until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the egg corrupted by another disease, it is necessary to tie the vessels that are suspended, being careful not to release the flow of blood; then cut the bone all around the suspension, and drain the egg, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	 And if an injury is assembled into two parts together, know that these are the branches; if you strike the other part as you did the first equally, then suck out the blood, and put moistened linen in oil of roses into the wound; and put another moistened linen in wine and oil on it, and put the two cords on top, and put over them doubled fabrics, and tie it all with the string according to this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	 Then take the fabrics and use them with linen thread according to this shape and sew them into the girdle of the arm, and one of the heads takes hold beneath the foundation until the back, and the other at the hilt part; and the other two heads on the two angles, and the rest is restrained in the buckle of the lacer; and sometimes this branch of cautery is used instead of iron-cutting, and you should take the cauterizing knife and strike the skin of the cords, and it must be heated as we have said, so that the white pus that contains the water is exposed; then take the cautery according to this form, and pierce the pus pocket with onion-like holes, and scrape the pus with this hot cauter.
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	 And the cup in all ways that you can, as long as it is heated; and ensure that the fire does not touch the egg; and know that this work is more effective; and be careful of the decorum of blood, and be aware of the operations of cutting; and if anything opposes you, or an abscess opens or flow of blood or something else, then cure what opposes you, according to what was said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	 If the patient is afraid and does not wish to endure this operation due to its horribleness, then you shall perform perforation, as I tell you, and when you are certain by the signs we have said that ramice aquouse is present, you should make the patient sit on a raised seat; then pierce the abscess in the area below the whole spatumile wide, and put the perforation along the length of the body; and let the wounds be large, so that all the pus can come out; then place cotton on the wound, hold it, and let the remaining pus drain, then cure the wound until the lesion is healed; and if the whitened cloth does not allow the pus to issue from the mouth of the lesion, you must apply a pen or instrument for treating pus of hydrops, as its form has been described earlier; enlarge the opening of the lesion, know that the pus will return, and collect it after six months or thereabouts, and when it is collected as described before, then the patient's days will pass.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess on the cheeks
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	 Know that in the section of this ramie there is fear in many positions, which is why it seems to me that one should leave it [the ramie]; and I will tell you the work and similarities of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	Therefore, I say that many abscesses come from the body or from the kidneys; and this is often so.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	 It is to be known by sour and acrid superfluity which spreads in the joints or from blows; it [the abscess] takes on the color of the body; there is no pain found, and the abscess is serious; and sometimes an abscess may be swollen and hard, and of this color, and at times comes from arteries, or from inflammation of veins.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	 When it is from an artery, it can be known by the abscess's hot position when you press it with your fingers; and one should not touch it [the abscess].
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	 One who is swollen with tumor of vein is known by its disposition to the expression of the touch of the fingers, and he can well make the incision on this appearance, and on other diseases; it is that you cut the tip of the bones, then the yolk is above, and the tract deep into white, and delivers the suspensory from all parts of the yolk.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	 If the yolk is already soft with these diseases arisen, then it is necessary that you draw out the yolk and cut it; if it is in the white or in that which is within the vessels, it is necessary that you deliver all of that tender part and cut it roundly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	If the birth of the boil is on the backside, you must cut it all off and extract the egg, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is done, apply linen moistened in rose oil and wine to the wound, then heal it with other remedies until it heals completely.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess on the cheeks
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent. Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier. Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	 The extension of this incision occurs due to a tear that comes from the perforation or the expansion on the abdomen in the area of the intestines; for which reason the intestines descend through that tear at one of the openings; and this tear can be either from the perforation, or from the expansion, and these two types of tears occur due to multiple causes: either by impact, jump, fall, sudden movement, or similar things; and the signs when it is from the extension of the perforation, are that it occurs gradually over a long time, and does not come suddenly; and the abscesses are evenly distributed up to the full extent, because the perforation follows the intestines.

Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; dou chastrement	of the lancing
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes. de erratique	Of the erratic growth
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile. Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	 If there is an effusion (swelling) near to the surface, it can be felt with your fingers or hand.

Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	 For an abscess that has formed within the wound, no treatment should be done.
des emorroides	If the nature of a woman is not perceived or small; it may be natural at birth, or an accident due to illness that comes upon her; or it may be due to discharge, whether subtle or thick, and this occurs in the rectum, or on the side, or underneath, wherever it may be; they should be aware of it, and know when to treat and cure it; and knowledge of these things is by the observation of the physician. If the discharge is approaching, whether at your hand or in the rectum, if it is subtle, move quickly and follow these steps: put both hands together, and the woman should be on her back, with her legs spread apart; then the subtle discharge will form, as long as the thick discharge subsides; then take wool, moisten it in oil, and place it on the rectum, and have the woman lie down each day so that it does not heal. If the discharge is hard and thick, you should cut it with a spatula resembling a myrtle leaf. If the discharge is of blood, suspend it at the anus and cut; and apply medicines to stop the bleeding, such as acacia, dragon's blood, incense, together with much egg; then place a large bandage around the wound so that it does not heal; and in this way it should be kept open for a long time, and you should also apply a linen tent; then treat her of other ailments until she is healthy. And when there is blood in the rectum, if necessary, cover it in this manner, unless it is an abscess that has grown. For an abscess that has grown in the rectum, one should not touch to treat.
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	 Emorroidal openings are the outlets of veins that usually do not close by themselves, and when emorroids become old, they swell; and we have said in the division, their resemblances, and signs, and I will say here those which receive treatment.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	 When emorroids and swellings become completely closed, and they cannot be felt by touch, there is no cure except by iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	 Those at the mouth of the anus, which can be felt, are those that can be cured.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	 Therefore, you must put the woman in a cold house, then stretch the anus with tongs to its roots, then sprinkle medicinal powders that stop bleeding, such as acacia and dragon blood and incense, and similar things; then hold her legs apart for an hour, then immerse her in cold water; and if bleeding occurs again, make her sit in a decoction of sumac bark, pomegranate rind, wild gale, and similar things, and then take barley flour, mix it with honey and oil, and make the plaster on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	 And if it bleeds, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	 If it does not bleed, you should apply blisters to the back and breasts (chest) without hurting them; then take linen, moisten it in the juice of onions or marigold with old wine, and apply it to the area.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When the abscess subsides, you should treat the area with ointment until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red, similar to a rough leaf, it must be covered as I have said in the manual; then you cure it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	openings of the anus
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	 Many types of abscess come in marriage, such as sores, painful abscesses, herpes, stomach ailments, fistulas, hemorrhoids, and hot abscesses, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the classification.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	 Therefore, I shall say in this treatise about the abscess that comes in the marriage (meaning a boil) which is not the same as those that wrap around; and if you want to know the work of iron, observe whether the abscess is hard at the beginning of its coming, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red when you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	 Therefore, do not hurry to pierce it, but let it heal as much as the pain subsides; and then make the patient sit on a stool, and have two stools or he leans, and support his back and gather his feet at the parts opposite the leg; and let his thighs be spread out, and place his arms under his knees, and bind them well with a good rope; then press the pus towards the right side of the abscess, and bring the instrument to open the mouth of the boil, from which follows the form; and it is necessary that when you bring this instrument, you pierce the rod first inside to know the depth of the boil, so that what enters inside of the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and does not burn the patient; and if the instrument is larger, it is necessary to cover the depth of the boil with cloths, so that the instrument does not hurt him; and it is necessary that he puts the mouthpiece of the instrument above, and marks the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	 And when the abscess is opened and it is treated with soft hands, it must be covered with a lint cloth; and when the boil is empty, you must put dampened, oiled cotton wool or green dry oiled wool in the wound; place the damp wool on the full side of the wound and on top of the wool, clean, damp linen cloth over it; then cure for two days with ointment afterwards until it heals; and sometimes lift the boil and the wound with a water and honey enema, and then water or longis and aristolochia roots cooked; then return to the ointment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	 And if the wound is healed in the sea, you must avoid heating with iron, but heal it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	Of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.
