First, it is necessary for the midwife to recognize the figure of natural childbirth and its signs when she sees the woman after labor and desires to push; then hasten the birth of the infant; afterward, know that this birth is according to the natural figure and the issue comes out of its head, and the second follows with it; and when you see these signs, it is necessary to gently press on her abdomen so that the infant is born quickly; for when it descends toward its head, the afterbirth also comes forth with it, and the sea is cleansed of its superfluities by good purification; and one who comes otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	 Sometimes it happens on the feet, or the body swells or the shoulders, or the hands, or it occurs on the abdomen, or elsewhere, and by chance it is turned around the neck, or in other evil ways; therefore, it is necessary that the woman who bails be wise and skilled in these things, and she must avoid error and deception, and I will show you all the figures on how to help.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the infant comes out through its head naturally and the woman is laboring intensely with weak vitality, let her sit on a saddle or have women hold her; then apply oil or fenugreek that has been cooked to her nature. Then insert the small spatula-shaped instrument shown here between her fingers.
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	 And cut the second birth canal, and strike its claw until the water that is within it goes out; and grasp the woman's abdomen until the child comes out, and if it does not come out, you must administer a poultice of fennel with camomile oil to the woman; then make her take emetics and purge herself with cathartics, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: now the child will come.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	 And if the two hands come out, you should reset them gently bit by bit; and if they cannot be put back, place a woman on the seat, lift her legs up; then tilt the seat onto the ground, and hold the woman so she does not cry out during the tilting; and if the hands cannot be put back, and the child dies, cut open the mother with the knife that is placed in front of you, extract the child, and reset gently.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	 of the birth of the child on his legs
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	 When the child comes out on his legs, you must push him upwards; and then turn him bit by bit, until he is straight; then take one of his legs and stretch it bit by bit.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	 The shoulder cannot jump up to anyone's knees, if it is commanded to leap, it makes him vomit in fright; if it jumps, let it be as God wills.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not as we have said, it should be turned bit by bit, until it is according to the natural shape.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	And therefore it should be done gently.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	 And if it does not jump as we have described, say that you give a potion of strong musk, oil of ambergris, and melted gum, grind everything together in a mortar; then put the nature of a woman within this ointment and apply it externally; then make her sit in hot steam until she is below the ribs; and when she becomes softened below, let him apply the collyrium of myrrh and put it on, and leave it for an hour; then make her sit on the seat, then make her vomit and hold her mouth and nose shut, and gently press her abdomen, because the infant is now moving.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	Of the birth of the child upon its knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	 When the child comes in this form, place its feet on the floor one by one; then lay it on its back, and let its legs hang down, and lie it on the bed; and fold its hands one by one, and then take hold of its hands above the stomach, and press the hips underneath, until it is arranged below; and if the child does not come out, grab its feet and push them forward, then push its belly upwards, then put your hands in; and handle the child hand by hand; and command the woman to seize herself until the child is born.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	The issue of the child coming through one hand wide;
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	 It is necessary to find a way to pull back the hand: if you cannot pull it back, then make the woman stand up and walk; if she cannot walk, then make her sit on the bed, spread her legs widely; then bring the mustard plaster that I have mentioned; and if she does not give birth, then make her sit on the chair, then try to pull back the hand; and handle the child according to its natural shape, and make her vomit, and command her to hold herself until the child is born.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	Hold the issue of the child by its neck, and spread your hands wide apart, turning your body towards the back of its mother;
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	 It is necessary that the servant grip his hand, then turn it little by little and gently; and when it is equalized, place upon it a plaster of alum and oil, as we have said, then command it to move little by little; and when you have done this, make him sit on the seat, and command him to grab it; and make him vomit.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	In the same manner, apply the remedy to all the others.
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	 When it comes to push the afterbirth in this manner completely, grip the afterbirth with your nail until the moisture is emptied; and if the child presses on his face and neck, strike it from the buttock so that it is not retained, and the child dies; then push the child inside as much as you need to, and command the woman to grab it slightly: then it will slip out easily.
de l’issue des gemelz	of twin births
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four; and this is not strange and rarely happens.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	 Two are strange things, and do not live unless they are named; I know what they are, namely multiplied ones, and they are desired by the one who divines them, who is linked to the devil; and sometimes they arise naturally like snakes under a tree, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	 And if they come out with groans, the treatment is as we have said, and let the bailiff be subtle, and do quickly and lightly whatever it does; and do as much as possible to its advantage.
de plusors enfans	of many children.
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	 Sometimes they are formed in the womb I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or more up to XV, and they are all shaped like a child by the measurement of the wise glorious one, and it is necessary that the bailiff knows this, for by chance similar things happen; do as required.
de l’enfant mort	of a dead child.
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	 When you are treating a woman for a stillborn child or an unborn baby, as I have said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are forced to perform surgery by hand; then you must know if the woman is of pure virtue, and has no accident or fear of death; then the woman should lie on her back, with her hips inclined downward and her legs raised; and the assistant should press her two parts, or tie her to the bed so she is not treated in the evacuation of the child; then rub the mouth of the mother with moist oils with musk and fenugreek and linseed; then anoint the midwife's hands with these oils and these musks; then insert them gently into the mother, then seek the place where she pushes the childbirth contractions that are necessary for this purpose, and be careful if the child is presented on top of its head; then pierce the child in its eyes or neck or mouth or palate or under the beard or in the navel or near the sides or near the ribs, and if the evacuation is through the feet, pierce or squeeze it gently at the mid-ribs; and hold the umbilical cord with the right hand, and put the crook between your left thumb and index finger, and press gently to the place where you have pierced, and insert the umbilical cord in any of these places until it reaches an empty place; and this is the shape of the umbilical cord:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	 Then pierce it against the other one, if necessary, so that the extraction is even; and then equalize it by moving from both sides to make it move, and make the points sharp for holding it in place, as shown in the figure:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	 If there remains a part, then the ball will be pierced with oil from one of its fingers and pushed into that part, and draw out the other part; if it remains without part, then place this pin or higher and continue until it comes out completely.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	 And if one hand comes before the other and it cannot be returned due to being held back, then you should wrap around a cloth until it comes out; then break it at the joint of the toes or near, and do the same with the other foot.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	 And if the child's shoulder is large and it is narrow at the exit, or it has a severe assembly of the head, you must insert the spinal spatula between your fingers, and press the head and extract the ailment; or you may use the instrument called "almidach", from which the form comes with the tools or chapter that follows this; and in the same way handle the natural large swelling; then pull out the bones with the pliers, and if the shoulder joint jumps out and it is tightened by force, it should be split as much as the moisture that is at a worse location; and if it cannot move out, strike it with pieces until you can. If it is swollen in the abdomen or beneath the ribs, you must pierce it until the moisture comes out.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the swelling is on the feet, the treatment is light and the reduction to the mouth of the bladder is easy.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	 And if it is strained in the belly or the thigh, you should stretch it with the cloth wrapped around your hand; and piercing the belly or the thigh, where the moisture is located; and if other limbs are dislocated, and the head remains, put your thumb in deeply into the wound, and pull it out to the mouth of the wound; then insert a splint or a pin, and pull further; and if the mouth of the wound is narrowed due to an abscess that has come, you should not work on it, instead administer moist and fat things; and apply plasters, and soak in warm, softening and moistening liquids.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	 And if the infant is on its side, and you can make it straight, bring it back to its original position as we have said in the live child; and if you cannot do this, pull it apart piece by piece, leaving nothing of the afterbirth.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	 When you have done this, bring it back to its original position as we have said in the abscesses that come in marriage; and if bleeding occurs, let it be put in a strong tightening and other treatments are applied.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman whose womb had a child die, then consulted another on it, and revived the other.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, an abscess came in the armpit, and swelled so much that it opened and began to rot.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was summoned for treatment, and for a long time I thought about the wound, but could not heal it.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied powerful astringent, and an bone came out, then after several days another one did.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I marvel greatly, because the belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	 I cut the bone of the wound, as long as the woman is in a better position; and the woman lives for a long time in this way, and then after a little while, a small amount of pus comes out of the place; and I do not remember this chapter except because, when the master finds a strange thing, he knows how to help it.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	To remedy a dislocated joint to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Here follows the form of the pressor, which we use in books; and to the two joints of the two chains at each turn.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	 The shoulders are more subtle to be restrained, and should be made of ebony or boxwood; and the hole in the stick should be large, and the margins of the wood must be, and a palm and a half long; and between the two limbs should be two alignments of the same stick, which are fastened on one side and on the other, half a palm length or a little more; and these two alignments are inserted into the mouth of the marrow to open when turning the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	 Another form, similar but more subtle and lighter, should be made of a stick of ebony or boxwood, like the pliers; and to the two shoulders, there should be two alignments, as you see, a palm long, and two finger widths wide; and when you are about to open the marrow with all the instrument, make the woman sit on the bed, her feet hanging down and legs open, then insert the two alignments together into the marrow, and hold the head of the instrument beneath between her knees; then work your hand with all the instrument as you have done with the pliers, according to the size that you see to open the mouth of the marrow, until the boy does what he wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	This instrument is completely covered, and they are multiplied in their resemblances; and when the patient has arranged them, he works more quickly, and higher for men according to their size.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not unnecessarily discard the instrument you have prepared, for there is no excuse for its necessity.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	 When the afterbirth is retained during childbirth, you should instruct the patient to hold back her lochia, and then make her vomit with a mustard poultice, and hold your hands on her mouth and nose; if she jumps due to this, it's fine.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	 If it's not that [retained afterbirth], you should take peppermint, and either a mortar or a cup, fill it with herbs that can open the mouth of the mother, such as rue, anise, chamomile, calaminthe, and centaury; all these herbs, or some of them, should be cooked or boiled in water over the fire; then put a spout or cup from the pot, and the other end into the mouth of the mother, and hold it until the vapors come inside the mother; then make her vomit, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the second one (the patient) jumps up quickly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	 And if it remains after this treatment, and does not heal as instructed, command the woman to moisten her left hand with sesame oil or musk liniment of aloe, then apply it to nature, and find it again; when she has found it, take it and stretch it little by little straight, so that the husband does not resist the extraction; but you must move it gently right and left, and then pull; it will come out and release.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	 If the mouth of the husband is stretched open, as we have said the cure for this condition is emetics and fumigation of herbs; if it does not improve with everything that has been said, make sure you do not force it to pull out; but whoever is at the husband's mouth, tie him to the woman's leg, then apply an ointment called tetrafarmaçon for clisterizing; he will recover and heal, but if she suffers from bad odor in her stomach and head, it will harm the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	Therefore it is necessary that appropriate fumigation is provided for this: no one of the ancients has tested fumigation with dill and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument with which one fumigates a woman to retain flowers and her afterbirth is as follows:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	 And it appears to be glass-like in shape, and the fine head is placed into its nature, and the broad sides above the fire; and let there be fumigation on the coals, and the tar until it is burned, and begin another.
de percier lou fondement	of piercing the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Many children are born without a perforated foundation but have it stopped up with some thin wax; in such cases, it is necessary to pierce the wax at its proper place, and not too sharp with a pointed spatula; be careful that it does not touch the wound; then put moistened linen on it, then heal it with ointment until it heals.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will reopen, put a plug of wood in it and leave it for several days, and let it be removed when the child wants to go to bed.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes this sudden swelling of wound or abscess occurs; it should be covered: whether it is to be cauterized, as we have said about the lime of lead.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula from the bottom
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	 Fistulas coming from below the foundation are nodules and larger ones that come out of the foundation's opening or between two parties, if there is one fistula or more; and when this nodule has become old, it swells up, and moisture causes a blister or thin bubble to form; at times these fistulas are persistent; they are recognized by those who know them for their discharge or windiness, as the patient has discharge, and sometimes urinates into the wound.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that penetrate to the bladder, and halfway down the penis; they reach the joint of the thigh, and to the knee of the cow.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	 And thus one knows the fistula persistent at the base, but not persistently: and it is that you press your thumb or the base, and press a fine needle of bronze or iron into the fistula when there is no twisting.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	 If there is twisting, you press a thin reed or horsehair until you feel the reed or hair at your thumb; and if you do not feel it, and no pus, gas or worm comes out, as we have said: know that it does not pierce; hasten to cure it.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula extends to the bladder or the channel of urine, if it bursts and cannot be healed by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	 If it is pierced to the joint of the knee, the reed comes up to the level; if there is no twisting and the pain disappears around it, it is that it has been pressed down, and there is no need for medicine or ointment; and in these persistent fistulas, there is no cure except labor, and folly of those who meddle with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	 In a woman who is not paralyzed and not old, with hope of healing by fire, as I have experienced, the patient lies between your hands on her back; then raise her legs up to her thighs, and have her thighs inclined towards her belly; next, thrust a probe made of iron or wood, if there is curvature, until you know where the probe enters.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	 If the patient feels pain around the foundation (pelvis), then you must press your index finger there, and if it feels as if the probe has pierced through, then it will be discovered whether the probe enters the hollow or the flesh; then know that she is paralyzed; do not move it further, for it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	 One should always understand that some can be healed well, but this happens rarely; and the aid one provides, it is that one heats the cautery subtly according to the width of the fistula, as previously stated; and pushes it all hot into the fistula, until it comes out from the base; and do this II or III times, as long as you know that these charred pieces should be burned, which resemble a feather of an eye; and then heal with moistened tents in butter, until those charred pieces disappear, then heal with soothing ointment.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	 If it is thus healed, it is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	 If it cannot be healed otherwise and if the tent enters but does not pierce until the point that is at its base, and between your hand and the tent, place a thick covering of skin or syfac, and you see the fistula under this cover; then press from the beginning of the fistula and push towards the tent, and then bring in the cautery afterwards, until it reaches the end of the tent; and the tent will be released, and charred; then remove those charred pieces that resemble a feather of an eye, and none remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the sinew swells and splits apart, cauterize it with fire or medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	 The cauteries of fire bring two good things: namely, the burning of these attached charms, and the stopping of blood and the healing of moisture; afterwards, they cure tents made moist with butter or cheese mashed up, until the limbs become cold, and the charred bones are buried in it; then, they heal the wound with hot ointments hard char and are the dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	When it is treated, it heals and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula reaches down to the bottom of its foundation and is separated from the body, push your finger into it or its foundation, and examine it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	 If you feel the wound, and between them is the cloth or skin or char, or it is about to be pierced, there should not be any other way except faith and hope, by the administration of one of the three ways: either you cauterize as we have said, or you strike it down to the bottom, or if you can, put tents on it and cure as before; do not go too deep so that you do not cover the foundation's support, and bring out the pus voluntarily; then cure, as we have said; by chance, it may heal, or you remove that covering and clean it when it is separated from the foundation, either with a tent or with another instrument pointed out; then examine the charred piece in the wound, as much as you can; then study to restore the wound, and to keep the fistula in the part farther away from the foundation: this would be easier for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	 And sometimes there are fistulas in this manner: and it is when you bite the tent (or tip) into the fistula, and it is where the tent touches the foundation beneath the skin above, then take a pierced tent at its head according to this form:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And insert one threaded wire in two, and insert the sheath to the entire length of the wire into the fistula until it reaches its end.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	 If it is located along the foundation within, then draw out the thread of that one, biting your tooth or foundation, and pull out the head of the thread, and bring together both ends, pulling them apart and leaving it for a day or two; and tighten it once, until the threads break the hard knots that are between them, and bleed; then heal the wound until it is sutured and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce itself, make it pierce in all possible ways, if it is not too full.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Because it should not be covered too full for the ligation, and then healed as we have said, until it is healthy.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	 The form of the spiny spatula for making a fistula is very sharp on one side and not on the other, so you should not touch what you should not touch, as you can see here:
des emorroydes	piles of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	 Emordisms are of two types: they are within the foundation, like a grain of resin, and there are small and large ones, and on the outside there is blood, and there is one or more, and they are dislocated from the foundation and away from the base of the foundation; but those that are dislocated have little moisture, and immediately or soon there is a little bit of sour citron juice or blood, and they take on the color of the body. And the treatment for these that are within the foundation is to command the patient to strain in order to urinate in chambers, until the foundations move back into place, and this can be felt by the children; if you hurry, take hold of it with pliers or with your fingernail, then strike at its roots. And if the teeth cannot hold them due to moisture, take hold of them with cloth or cotton, or a piece of chamois leather; bind them with your hands, then strike, and powder some hot powders on top that are in place of cautery; or cauterize them as is said in the chapter of cautery. After they have healed, use other treatments until they become healthy. And if the foundations cannot move back into place, clisterize the patient with a bitter and sharp clisterium to clean what is within the foundation, so that it can come out easily; when the patient feels it, and the teeth are forced from the foundation, it is an easy cure; it is that you grasp them with your fingernail or pliers, strike them, heal them as we have said, until they become healthy, and fear the incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 You must apply the stitching in this manner: take twisted thread and insert it into a needle, then pull the thread above and pierce the needle from another side, and twist the two ends of the thread below the needle, making it long; and knot the thread, then sew the needle and make sure to leave space for the excess blood; then place the damp linen cloth soaked in rose oil or turpentine on the foundation, and place it on top, and instruct the patient to rest; then leave it until it bleeds, and when it stops bleeding, you should treat it with ointment and other treatments until it is healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	the drying of the fire or foundation.
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Often, there is drying in the intestines due to fire and by the nature of constraint, and when the disease is old and medication does not work.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 It is necessary that you cauterize the scab of a blister or your fingernail with a spatula or your finger tip, so as not to let it moisten; then heal it until it dries as required; and if it cannot heal, then shave more strongly than before, as much as it bleeds, and be cauterized; then heal it until it heals.
dou fremit	The trembling (or shuddering)
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	 A boil is a small appearance on the body that grows much bigger; and sometimes it freezes and feels like death from shivering, and spreads throughout the body, especially in the hands more than other parts.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	 And the cure is that you take a reed from an ostrich feather or a strong hen's feather and place the reed on the shivering, until the red circles the shivering completely; then turn your hand around the entire reed so as to cover it all over the shivering, and immerse it deeply, and pull out the shivering from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	If you wish, do it with a cane of iron or steel in this form and be subtle underneath and traverse above:   In the medieval context, "subtle underneath" probably means intricate or delicate, while "traverse above" likely refers to applying pressure from above. This sentence might imply making an instrument or device out of iron or steel that is designed for a specific medical procedure. However, this is just an educated guess as the text does not provide further context or explanation.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	Do not pierce, instead hold it tight and press. And if you wish, cauterize the quivering, as described in the chapter on cauterization.
de la forme dou clistere	The form of the cluster.
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes one makes the cluster of silver or iron, or melted tin or wax; and sometimes makes these tools small and large, according to those for whom they are prepared.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Therefore, the ones that are brought in the treatment of infants and those who are weak and suffering, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of a clister (small or large) is above wide, where the bellies are tied in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	 And he should have an opening where the stomach is connected, as you see, and the chest inside pierced; it should have two holes on one side and one on the other; and fill the stomach with medicine from a beast's bladder or parchment, and pierce all around with small holes, and there should be space between each hole, then put strong thread made of twisted yarn through the holes in X or around, and tie the stomach like a sack; and when the medicine is inside, attach it to the instrument with a strong thread, then apply the plaster; this is the shape of a circle.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	 And the medicine should not be too hot nor too cold, and apply oil or ointment of an egg white, or something similar, to the head with a cloth, then put it on gently; then the attendant should examine him with both hands until he is completely visible, then remove the cloth, and make the patient lie flat so the medicine can come out; if it leaks a little, squeeze it as much as possible; if he sleeps all night, it is more help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you plaster the patient with belly distention caused by intestinal blockage and the medicine starts to come out, renew it until it becomes healthy.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	 And if the hemorrhoids are ulcerated or abscessed, it is also necessary to use the enema, even as subtle as for a child. This is the form of the subtle enema where the skin is strained:
des plaies	wounds (plural)
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have said in the division the treatment of wounds; and we shall tell you about the treatments of hands and medicines, according to their completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are various according to what they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and of how they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	 The things that wounds are made of are by piercing with a sword, cutting with a knife or dagger, or lance, arrow, or similar things; or those made according to the laws of the body, such as a wound on the neck, head, chest, belly, liver, and similar limbs. I will tell you the cure for each wound, and I will begin with simple wounds of the head, because remembrance will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	 I say that when a simple wound or abscess comes with no broken bones, beware if it is due to arrow penetration or similar things, and the skin is completely torn and the wound is large; doubt the presence of an abscess strongly: let it drain immediately from the head itself if there is little blood coming from the wound, and let it drain in contrast to the damaged part; and let the patient empty himself of wine and heavy foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If it does not want to drain, let its food be reduced and do not drink wine or eat meat; and place on the wound if an abscess comes out, cotton moistened in rose oil only, or in stiptic wine; and if no abscess comes out, place on the wound if it is fresh with all its blood, and it is not moving due to air, the following powder: and if fire has moved it, place some ointments until it heals.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	If the wound is large like a sword and similar, and the lips cannot be brought together by pressing, bring them together by stitching, as I shall say about abdominal wounds, in stitching.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	 If the wound exposes the bone, is open and does not hold together at all, close it; then treat the wound with medicine, put hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat thick foods, such as cooked heads (testes) and cooked wheat, also like pulses, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	 If the skin or flesh rots away to the bone, and there is nothing left on the bone, close it all, and pour hot liquid on it, then treat it; if there are arteries in the wound or vein that cannot be stopped without cutting, cut it; and if you find a dislocation, tie it with a thread; and if this does not help, cauterize (it).
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, the cure is light; place this powder on it as soon as the arsenic has made it harden.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 And the manner of the powder is: take incense one part; dragon's blood two parts; three parts of live coal, and grind the powder finely, apply it to the wound and press firmly until it dries well and joins completely with all its blood; then bind it well and leave it unbound, if it does not swell; because one does not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes they do this with only calcined substances, when they do not have incense or the blood of a dragon, but the wound has not healed.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the fire has burnt the wound, indeed if it has, do not put this powder on it; but apply some digestible ointments or barley flour paste made with water and honey until it heals; then heal it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	 And if the bone fracture comes with a small wound, then extract it with subtle forceps; I will tell you about head fractures afterwards.
de la plaie dou col	Of the neck wound
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound on the neck is simple and has no distinction from that of the head, but if the nerve of the neck or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	 If it is a nerve, there is no other remedy than to let it heal and not put anything restraining, as this harms nerves and makes them retreat; do not place anything cold on the wound, because the substance of nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member; but let the medicine be warm, such as warm water washed with sweet vinegar and mixed with rose oil, and boiled water washed in the same way, and other such stones according to this method, and moist immediately.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the wound is large, tie and bind it, then treat it until it heals.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	 And if the wounds are deep and swollen and filled with pus, pierce it or lower its position; if the arteries are cut, and blood flow comes out, stop it, ligate it, and cauterize as necessary; if the spines of the throat are cut, or the cartilages, and the windpipe is protected, so that the meat moves, if the cartilage rises above the throat's bone, but does not touch the throat, but rather return it according to its natural figure; then pull it gently, leave it for some days, then treat it with decayed onions until it heals; and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, drain it; and if there are bone fragments, pull them all out if you can, and those that you cannot remove, leave until the wound dries up and is drained and aligned; if the wound is fresh, put powder on it as I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and it has a fistula, treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the sword or knife wound
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	 If it is a sword or knife wound and the injury is deep, look to see if the patient bleeds spontaneously from the wound: know then that the wound is mortal; and if it is not deep and is fresh with all its blood, do not apply powder immediately nor bind it for the blood that stops it may clot completely and return to the heart, and kill the patient; instead, apply attractant ointment, and bind it twice a day; and if you have no ointment, put old cotton in the wound for absorbing moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound 3 or 4 days, or more; if spasm or bad tremor of heart or other signs of bleeding do not appear; and when you see good conditions, know that the wound is healed.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	 Treat it then with cauteries and other remedies while it is healthy; if it cannot heal and opens up, immediately recognize that there is a fistula; if so, treat it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	 If the wound is an incision from a sword or knife, and it is simple, large or deep, treat it in front; if it is large, stitch it; if it is small, apply powder; if it penetrated the bone and broke it into pieces, open the wound and pull out the fragments if they are visible; if they are not visible, let the wound drain and align the extractions; and for other wounds in other parts of the body, the judgment is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	The dislocation of the abdomen
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	 The first dismemberment of the abdomen is great, medium and small; from a large wound, the intestines may fall out once or the intestine's nerves, causing the insertion of them; and the stitching is more difficult, and sometimes a small wound is worth less than a large one, because it requires more effort to put the intestines back in, if not put in layer by layer; because the intestines swell suddenly when they feel cold, so they re-enter more forcefully, and therefore, medium wounds are more beneficial, because the intestines are reset at their place rather than others. And know that the rupture of the abdomen is according to four manners: the two common stitches occur in the abdominal stitch, and the stitches of other body wounds and two other specific ones are common for other wounds; and yet they are more appropriate with the abdominal stitch, and I will explain each one.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	 I say that when the wound is small and nothing from the intestines protrudes from it, it is easy to reset, this is by one of the two methods: either because of the small size of the wound as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	 And when it is cold, heat it in one of these ways: soak a sponge or a piece of cloth in warm water only, or cook it in hot squill and cyperus and spike root, and massage the intestines until the swelling disappears; and sometimes do this with wine restraining, and it is necessary to move it away as you would soothe a sore.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	 And when you see the swelling separate, massage the intestine with warm or hot and bitter medicines, for this closes the opening near nothing; and if it cannot enter, make a small incision in the wound using the instrument with which you cut hemorrhoids; and the first cure is to be soothed as the wound, we should not cut too deeply without great necessity; and this is the instrument to split: cut from within the curve and do not turn it, and look at its shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	 And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines fall out, you should put them back in their natural shape in their proper place, if you have the power to do so, for it is necessary.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	 When the wound is in the part below the belly, you should make the patient lie on his back and raise his legs higher than his head; if it is in the part below the belly, then lift the head and feet higher than the parts below; and similarly, if the opening of the belly is in one of the two parts, then take care that the injured part is higher than the other; and in this way, you should apply what I say to large and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	 In small wounds, use what is appropriate, then take a person with skill who will cover the entire wound with his hand and bring the lips together; this is the common way of stitching, and you should take an awl or more than one, according to the width of the wound; leave a gap at the top of the wound and pierce it with an awl or with a strong thread; perforate the two skin layers with the two skin layers underneath, which is beneath the skin, as far as you can pierce from that side, and bring the two sides of the layer beneath together three times; then wrap a double thread around the awl in two parts, then bring the two skin layers of the wound together again, leave a gap, and pierce another awl; tie the thread as you did with the first awl, and continue to do so according to the number of awls needed until the entire wound is stitched; and let the awls be medium-sized, neither too fine nor too thick, for very thin needles pierce all the flesh, and overly thick needles cannot enter well: therefore, they should be medium-sized; and do not push the needles too far from the flesh and skin, lest they cut and open the wound before it is sutured; then sew the needles' heads so that they do not hurt the patient while sleeping, and put weights or bandages on the needles to hold them in place, and leave them until the wound is healed; this kind of stitching with needles is more convenient for small wounds, because it needs only one needle or two as a second stitch, and is that you bring together the two skin layers and the two layers beneath with one needle or with a strong thread. I sewed a wound on a man who had a stomach, which was cut by a knife, and the wound was more than one palm wide, and the intestines were about two palms wide, and the wound was in the stomach.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	 I returned the intestine as it had been twenty-four hours earlier, and the wound healed up to fifteen days, and it was cured, and it became healthy.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	 They had judged that he would die, but it was a miracle; and I did not treat him with poultice, for I was in a place where no such thing or medicine was found; and I put old cotton over the wound twice a day, and washed it with water of honey until it healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	 Here I shall tell you the two proper ways of stitching: take the needle and pass it from the outside to the inside; when it has pierced through straight through, place the head of the sinew or thread where the needle is inserted, and pierce it again from the inside towards the outside; and the meaning of this stitching is that you sew as a tailor sews fur, and leave one side open, then take it up on the other side, until the stitching is completely finished.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	 The second manner of stitching, which Galen calls specifically, is as anyone does who join two parts together naturally, and apply one end of the suture to another end, in this manner: insert a needle or end of thread near the mirror image, and pierce only that spot; then turn the needle and pierce from the outer part towards the inner, through the two connected parts; then pierce both ends from the outer part towards the inner, in the two other threads that are on the opposite side; and this is the mending manner of stitching and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	 Galiens said this word, and anyone can testify that the stomach should be sewn with two needles, having thread in each; and one needle must enter from one side, and the other from the opposite, in the manner of those who sew purses; and know that when the wound is within the stomach, the stitching is more painful than other parts of the stomach.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	 The judgement of the wound is similar to that of other wounds: and it is that when you probe the fresh wound with all its blood, as soon as the arrow has moved it, you should replace the intestine and the fat; then apply a powder healing charcoal, and if the arrow has moved, apply any ointment present on the wound until it closes; sew the flesh, and suture the sides, and the mirach; then treat the wound as other wounds, until it heals; and if you don't have medicines, put old cotton on it, and move it two times a day until it heals.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	 You do not require any other medicine when the wounds are simple in many cases; and if you doubt whether the wound affects the principal members, then you must moisten light linen with warm oil (or rose oil), and place it around the joints, and under the saddle; and if there is pain or putrefaction in the joints, and this happens repeatedly, then cleanse them with black wine vinegar, and especially when putrefaction reaches the intestines; and pierce inside, and know that when it is the large intestines, it is easier to heal than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.
