The intestine called "jeun" cannot heal when it is perforated, and this is due to the inflammation of the veins that are there, and the subtlety of the whole body, and the closeness of its nature to nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	 And if the hernia leaps from the wound, put it back in place just like the intestines when it is fresh; but if it becomes old and turns black, you must tie the part that has turned black so that blood does not come out there, because there are veins and arteries; then cut what is between the hernia sac, and hang the two heads suspended from the part below the wound to straighten the extraction when the hernia falls, and the wound bows.
de la routure dou boueil	Of the rupture of the bladder
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	 When the intestine is torn and the wound is small, it can be restored in some people, because I saw that a man was pierced or stabbed in the stomach; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, became inflamed and turned into a fistula, and there were discharges and wind; I treated it according to what I knew, and did not stop subsiding until it healed, and the edges were sutured.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	 And when I saw it sutured, I suspected that the patient had trouble in his stomach; and there was no problem, but he stayed in better conditions, eating and drinking; and some experienced said that when he has a small wound in the intestine, it should be sewn up in this manner: take strong breaths, then gather the edges of the wound, and when the breath has opened the mouth, place it on the two lips so that it stretches its mouth out; and then strike the head, and hold it so that it cannot disengage, then put another breath after in the same way, until the wound is completely seized; and cut the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	 If the head (of something) becomes inflamed in the intestine and brings no harm to the patient, it can be sewn with a thin thread made from the intestine of an animal, as follows: take the head of this intestinal thread that is quite sharp, then tie it to the head of a linen thread twisted tightly, next insert the thread into the needle, and sew the intestine, and mend in the opening; and this method of mending does not exceed the path of faith and hope. If the wound is large and wide, especially when it is one of the great intestines, there is no trick or health, except for subtleness.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	 Know that every wound or abscess, when it grows, is called universally "fistula", and the same when it opens up and becomes a boil.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	 A fistula is according to truth a kind of hard and white nodule, where there is no pain felt, and it appears as a boil on a bird's feather; sometimes clear, and other times thick; sometimes small, and other times large; and I have spoken about it in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not healed, and there is no flesh inside, this is true except for one of the nine causes: namely, due to smallness of blood or body; or because of its malignancy; or because there is hard char within, and above the lips, which does not allow new flesh to grow; or because there is too much pus; or the limb is paralyzed, and the matter inside is of poor quality; or the medicine is not good for the cure; or because the corruption is a kind of plague; or because the region's property is slow in digestion and healing, and it naturally swells up; or there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, their signs, and the cures with medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Also, I will explain to you the treatment for fistula that is made by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	 Know that fistula occurs in all members of the body; for there are fistulas that come from large veins, arteries, nerves, or to the rectum, or intestines, or bladder, or one of the sides, or spine on the back, or any joints of hands or feet; and such as come to the property of the principal member, and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	 And all these fistulas of this kind are difficult to heal, and there is nothing except labor and ignorance; and if any fistula does not come to the place that I have said, and you have confidence in its cure, and you observe it, take a tent of lard or iron, if the fistula is straight, pierce it; and if the fistula is twisted, seek a thin tent of wood, for the splinters bend with the curvature; and if the fistula has holes and you cannot pierce it well with tents, cleanse it with one hole by lard, for moisture flows from one hole to another, and cleanses it; then pierce it skillfully in your power, so that you know whether there is bone or nerve, and if it is fully closed, ask the patient carefully about the pain he feels when you press your hand, and where he feels it; and when you truly know the place where it is, and if it is far from a joint, nerve, artery, vein, or in any of the places that I have said, then cut according to what I have said, and remove the foulness and rotten charcoal that are within; and then heal it until it is healed, and if the fistula is well penetrated from the right place, then you must cut completely, as much as you can, then put damp tents filled with medicinal oil inside, and push them to the head of the fistula, until the medicine corrodes the superfluidity that remains in the bottom; and then put soothing ointments on healthy char, until it heals; and if it does not heal by this, cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is rotten from the fistula, cut it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	 If a vein or nerve does not trouble nor the main limbs, as we have said; and if the bone is exposed, and there is decay and blackness, let it remain until all corruption is gone, then treat with healing salves until it is healthy; and if it is not healthy, and returns to bowed as before, know that you are not yet at the font: if you expose and dig as deep as you can, and remove all the decay, then restore the joint; and if it is thus healthy, that is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	 If the corruption is too deep that you cannot reach it; if there is no other means but to wait for nature; and if there is only a little decayed bone, and you can draw it with pliers, draw it as necessary for this purpose, and if there are many bones, draw them all out, do not leave any; and if the moisture opposes you and there is no mistake or fear, beat and press the moisture and heal the bone.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	 And if you cannot remove [the foreign body] within an hour, place something irritating pus on the wound, and let it stay until the flesh is pushed out around the bone; and then the bones will move more easily; and if it is a large bone, such as a thigh or leg bone, press on the corruption only until all the blackness is removed, then restore the wound; and if there is a large part of the rotten tissue and it reaches the marrow of the bone, you must be careful and cover everything up to the corruption, and then let it heal until it is healed; and I will tell you about a fistula that happened in a man's leg, so that you may take an example and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	 The young man was around thirty years old who had pain in his leg due to an internal cause that brought the matter to his leg, and he had a large abscess, and there was no reason for it to heal; but they foolishly operated on the abscess so much that the abscess opened, and they flowed out a lot of matter, and it became a fistula, and much pus came out that all ran from his body and moisture from his chest; and many people tried to cure him for two years, but no wise man was in the art of healing, until I was called upon, and I saw his leg and the medicines with which they were treating him, and what flowed out through the sores at great speed; and the young man's body became red, and he had a citrine color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	 I sewed up one of the wounds, and then searched all the wounds, and found that some came towards each other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	 I then hurried and sewed up one of the wounds as far as I discovered part of the bone, and found it rotten and pierced; corruption came up to the bone within; I thought that only that corruption was present, except for what I left out; and I began to heal the wound with strong medicines for a long time, but could not close it; then I tried again, and discovered the bone as before, and found the corruption continuing in the bone, and removed it, and left it open, and tried to sew up the joint; but I was unable to do so more than around a palm's breadth of the bone, and it broke apart everywhere, then I healed it with medicines; and it became healthy and closed quickly, and no further work was needed except for the weakness of the patient who could not endure, and the fear of death that I had of him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	 For it often bled due to the evacuation, but it was completely healed and a hard cyst grew in place of the bone, which had a good disposition and did not cause any harm or damage at all, neither in its location nor in its coming or going.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	 And if a bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be treated thus: take thread, and tie it at the open end of the bone, and command someone to pull it up; then take another thicker piece of thread and tie it over the cyst that is above the bone, and hold the chief so that you pull the corrupt cyst down into the bottom, and expose the healthy cyst on the place where you wish it to be, ensuring the corrupt cyst does not bleed; then put either a splint or a piece of wood under the bone to cover the corrupt cyst; and it should be thus until one can see and feel the corruption, and furthermore.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	 And if the bone is corrupted and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or a part, you must uncover all the flesh; then put iron under it, and then press from one side to another on the corruption, and hold the iron rod as long as the corruption, as we have said; and if the corruption is at the joint, hit the corrupted joint, and hold the bone or part that contains it from the other side; and if the corruption is between two joints, there is no other way than to cut; and if the corruption is at the end of the hand or foot, it is a difficult matter, but you must investigate the corruption and find out how it opens; and clean it in all possible ways, but let neither veins nor nerves prevent you; and know that the instruments for cutting these bones are numerous, according to the type of bone and appearance of the wound, and its thickness and subtlety, and size and smallness, and hardness; and therefore you must prepare a tool for each type of work; and know that the work will show you the instrument you need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the signs of the diseases; and choose the instrument you need according to what is required.
dou feu	hot fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	 The shoulder may dislocate due to internal or external reasons; and when you have administered that corrosive medication for the treatment of the ailment, and it proves ineffective, then it is necessary to cover the affected limb up to where the corrosion occurs, so that the patient may suffer from death or severe damage to the limb due to its failure; and the signs are that the limbs become black, as if they were burned by fire, and afterwards they turn darker; this spreads from one member to another and affects the entire body. Hasten to cover it, and if it is caused by the sting of certain venomous creatures such as sea scorpions, snakes, and similar, cover the head of the affected limb, and do not give any space for the venom to reach up to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	 And if it reaches up to the hand, strike at the joint so that the corrosion does not reach the arm; and if it reaches the arm, strike at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, it is death, and no remedy outside of the quantity of its virtue can save him; and thus act when the corrosion comes or falls: if it comes at the first joint, strike after the next joint; and if it comes or falls, strike the entire joint; and if it ascends to the leg, strike at the knee joint; and if it passes the knee, no remedy except making the patient weak and letting him die is available; and the method of striking or soothing the member is that you tie it above and below, extend one minister on one link below, and another minister on the upper link, and you separate the flesh which is between the two links with a spatter-stick wide, until the bone is exposed; then strike or soothe, and put linen cloths on each side to ensure that the hot iron does not touch healthy skin, and it brings the patient other lesions and abscesses.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	1. And when blood flow comes when you work, cauterize the area quickly, or apply some restraining powders; then return to your medicine until it is complete, then bind the limb with a suitable ligature, and heal it until it heals; and I will tell you what happened to a man in my presence: he had a blackness that looked like a burn from fire, and this corrosion first appeared on his foot of the leg, until it consumed the entire leg; and when the man saw the corrosion, he scratched the leg to cover it, and it healed; and long afterwards the corrosion returned at the hand or one finger, and it came to me, and I gave him things repercussive after the purification of the body, but the corrosion could not be stopped; and he asked that I amputate his hand, and I did not want, because I had hope of repercussing the matter; and also feared that if I amputated his hand, he would die, for the vitality of the man was weak; and he despaired of everything, and returned to his land, and scratched the leg to cover it, and it healed; and I have told this story only for this reason: one does otherwise if it is necessary.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	 Aposteme sometimes comes in charnut and remains so long that it causes a large swelling of the bowel; and then it runs and pierces, and the bowel jumps, and the place stays open, like a wound of a vassal; and the skin that is above is as delicate as unbleached linen, and does not penetrate to the bone or to the nerve, and such disease is called "sain", and is not called "fistule"; but if it is long enough to reach the bone entirely, it is called "fistule"; and the skin should be cut all around, just as unbleached linen; and it does not heal due to its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	 And if the skin hardens and the corruption is not complete, and the skin is thick with flesh, cure it with a clisterium in this way: observe if the breasts are large, and the nipples within them smell foul; then apply an Egyptian clisterium made thus: take asafetida, oil, litargire, equally, and cook these in a vessel over fire until the medicine turns red and becomes as thick as honey; then take as needed and make it into water and honey, and apply the clisterium to the breast, and squeeze out the pus; leave the medicine for two hours, then remove it by straining; do this frequently until the breasts are healed and the pus is gone; and at no time is the clisterium made with vinegar water, when this medicine is not present, but you take vinegar of vine ash, pour it on, then strain and apply the clisterium, until you know that the breasts are well healed; and if the patient cannot bear it, or the Egyptian medicine or the vinegar water, then use a clisterium made of water and honey with a little pulverized litargire; or apply a clisterium made of honey and sweet wine, as long as the honey has the property to purify and cleanse, and the wine makes the blood thicker; and when you have done this, and are certain that the breasts are well purified, then apply to those that cause discharge any medication that stops the flow, and make it with rose oil and in wine; or apply some medicines and ointments, of which I have told the properties or the treatment of ointments; and if the holes of the breast are small, and the opening of the clisterium cannot enter, then widen it slightly with a knife, and put on an Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment, until it is wide enough; and if the wound is too large, let it heal naturally as long as the level or the clisterium can enter, and if the nipples emit pus, apply vinegar or more below the level where it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	 When the bowel is full, do not allow it to be strained with a cord; and if you cannot cover the opening of the anus in this way, arrange it so that the bowel moves towards its lowest point because when the bowel is full, do not allow it to be strained with a cord and if you cannot cover the opening of the anus in this way, arrange it in such a manner: that the bowel moves easily downwards, and do not let anything remain from the stool; take consolidating medicines to put on the wound, and lay linen cloth over the entire wound; then press strongly towards the injured area near the opening, which is larger than the first, and place ointment on it according to the size of the injury, and put it on the injured area of the wound to align the bowel, and do not remove the large cloth except after several days once; and he who is on the injured area of the anus removes it frequently to extract the bowel, and learn what comes out from the bowel, whether it is venom or pus or bile or undigested food; and beware if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is abscess or not, and when your medicine has been spread in this manner and you see the nature that rises on the injured area of the wound, then know that the intestines have already turned inside out, and bring the healthy parts closer; and then uncover it in the morning or third day, and when you uncover the wound, change the other cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast falls inward improperly after many days, know that the breast does not heal itself.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	 And if subtle poisonous worms come after a long time, do not despair of health, for health approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	 For those whose flesh in wounds turns black and for those who do the opposite; and if the breasts swell indigestibly after many days, know that they will not improve; and if the breasts delay in drying up, and are swollen, apply medicines that dry up moisture in substance and are dry in effect, such as oil of roses, for there is much part of vitriol, and it is the last medicine; use oil of roses with rose oil, and equal old wine in substance; then boil it and use it; and do the same with mastic and aloe and incense, and grind them into powder and sprinkle on the honey when it is over the fire; and then apply a plaster to it, and place it on the breast, and at times administer long aristolochia root, and celestial root, which is like flour and cumin; and use simple or compound remedies: grind them, make into powder, and sprinkle on the honey I mentioned before, and use; and if the cure does not improve and is not cured by this remedy, know that corruption has spread throughout, and causes pressure in the bone, or hard members, or ligaments; treat it with the remedy for fistulas, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess on the nail bed.
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	 Pancreatic abscess is an abscess that arises beneath the nail of the finger or toe, or occasionally in other places; and when it is neglected, if one does not pay attention to it, the abscess grows, spreads and boils as it moves towards the root of the nail, and possibly affects the entire nail; and the corrosion reaches the bone, causing the joint to become wide, and the color becomes discolored.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	 When you treat it as we have said in the previous section and the treatment does not work, then you should amputate the entire excess that remains of the nail, and then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 The cauteries are very helpful if the bone is healthy and the nail is whole; and when the nail starts to grow into the flesh, and it begins to prick and bleed, you must put the lard under the nail so that it stops the flesh from growing, and push it upwards, and strike the flesh gently and lightly; then apply hot and corrosive medicines on top of it to remove everything; afterwards heal it with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	 And if the corrosion is in the bone, strike it and pull it out, for as much as the bone becomes corrupt, it cannot heal; and if you see it becoming corrupt, strike it with the iron as previously stated, afterwards heal it until it is healed; and if it is wounded and feels great pain, you must first make it clean; then cut the nail with a sharp spatula from above, but ensure that the cutting does not reach the flesh beneath the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain; and if it happens, place something over it to relieve the pain.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain in the deaf hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	 One must straighten the finger that is born in some people by chance, and by chance it has flesh, or it has bone, and sometimes it has a nail, and none of these grow from the root of the joint, or they are born in some knuckles.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	 The one that is born in any nail of the finger does not grow, and the one that is born at the joint of the finger, by chance grows; the size of the fleshy one is light, thus it should be cut off with a broad spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	If it is born in the root of the joint, it is difficult to cure; hold it covered.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 In the one who is born or should be in the last nail, you must first cut off the rounded flesh to the bone, then cut the bone with an appropriate size wire, and then heal it until it is healthy.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The swelling that comes at the joints happens at the same time by birth, or by injury of a wound, or by burning with fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	 If you need to suture that wound, it should be repaired according to its natural shapes; then put between two tents or dampened cloths oiled, so they do not stick; or you put between two thin planks until the edges are sutured, as necessary.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If one of its sides comes with the palm, then strike that joint as required.
des vils	 of villagers
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	 Those are veins that are large, swollen and full of melancholic superfluities, which come in many members of the body; and it happens more often in legs of those who walk much and work and carry loads, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you must administer purge of gall, and then the healthy from the basilica.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	 The iron treatment is done in two ways: one is that you cut it and drain the black blood; and the other way is that you tie up the vein and draw it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	 The thigh is to be cut as follows: first, raise the leg with very hot water, making the flesh soft; then hold the patient's leg from above the calf to the part below the knee; then cut the vein at one of the spots, either I, II or III, in a wide manner; then separate and draw out black blood up to your hand, from one end to the other, as much flesh as the sickness can bear; then tie it and command the patient to eat meat that is darkening quickly; and repeat the evacuation and cleansing when the veins are full, which benefits the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 The blistering is to be done as follows: reflux the patient's leg, if it has much hair, then put it in water and raise the leg with hot water until it turns red and the veins swell; and if you do not have water, heat it with fire, and then press towards the vein near the long side of the thigh or in the part below the calf; then cut the skin at the edge, and strip the vein from each side, as much as it appears when felt; and it will appear red and black, and where the vein enters the skin seems like a white cord; then push the root down, until it is swollen with the skin, and then lightly peel it off, then press in another place further III steps; then strip the skin above the vein as much as it appears, then draw it out to the root, as you have done, and then peel it again, as you did before; then make another cut, or more if necessary; then drain, and make another cut, as you did before; then make another incision, or more if needed, then drain, and then press at the end of the wound to the second cut; then remove the blood and pus layer by layer until it is all removed, then press; and if you cannot draw it out and lift it, insert a thick strong double threaded needle into it and tie and draw it, and insert it under the root, and turn your hand from one side to another until it comes out; and be careful not to press, for if it presses, it cannot be drawn out or lifted, which is harmful to the patient; and when you have treated it all, put on the wound linen soaked in vinegar and oil.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	 And if the face is contracted and twisted and swollen together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must cut it forcefully, but do not cover it; draw it out as we have previously mentioned.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	 The shape of the iron with which one strikes the face is curved and does not cut; it pierces the vein instead, and it is large because if it were thin, it would pierce the vein, but be thick as we have said, and here is its shape:
de la voinne civile	 of the common vein (civile means 'common' in this context)
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	 This vein (civile) is found in the legs, in warm areas where no herbs or trees grow and in dry land without moisture; however, it may also occur elsewhere, and this happens due to the corruption that comes from under the skin, as it rises within the body like a serpent and goes to the legs, piercing between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	 And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are that a very great inflammation comes in the leg and then the swelling changes, and the vein begins to bulge out like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	 When the shoulder is open, you must wind around a piece of cloth from 7 to 10 inches long and sew it, and leave the cloth on the arm, and whenever it swells towards the opening, you should wind around the cloth again and sew; if it becomes too long, cut off a part and wind around the remaining, but do not seal it at its root as it is released; for if you seal it, it will return to the flesh and cause abscess, corruption, and disease, which must be treated carefully until it reaches the neck, and nothing remains in the body; this vein can sometimes extend up to 5 or 10 fingers long, and once I had a patient whose vein was 10 fingers long. When you seal it, press on it with a flat iron or lead, puncture it to the bottom, so that everything comes out; empty the material inside, and apply external medicine for corruption every day, then treat as abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	 And sometimes at this opening [vein], the hand is plunged in, and especially when it opens in a joint, be it arm or leg, and there comes much damage, and from which it may pull away; then heal as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	 of worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	 This disease is called in our land "cattle disease", because it often happens to cattle, and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes throughout the body spreading and contracting, and it is felt along the limbs until it reaches the skin or moves away, and jumps out; it is caused by corruption of certain humors, as serpents and lizards and roundworms or tapeworms in the stomach; and there is doubt about its malice, for when it goes through the body, and it rises to the head, and comes to the eye, by chance enters, and destroys the eye; and this happens often.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	 When you see it to cure and draw, one can force it out only when it moves: therefore, you must tie the limb above and below with a strong cord tightly, then strike upward and pull it through, and if its end is buried deep in the flesh, and you cannot extract it, cauterize it with fire until it dies; and the greatest harm that it does is that it corrodes oil, as we have said; and if you see it coming out or near the oil, hold a bellows underneath it, then strike upward and pull it through; and you must use the patient with purification of body medicines soluble for bad humors, and avoid rich food putrefactive.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	 of the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	 This disease is called in our land "wind-ache," and it is a pain that comes in some members, and moves from member to member; and I have seen this myself.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	 I was called to a sick woman, and saw her arm swollen, and noticed a small swelling in the armpit of the arm; then afterwards, it began to rise like a worm at the shoulder, faster than anything, as quick as living silver when it is cut from one piece; the pain separated from that place, and pierced into the shoulder, and soon after ran through all the body, until it came in the other arm; then she told me that it returned again around the body, as I saw myself.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I wondered greatly how it moved thus from limb to limb, for I have never seen this sickness in such a manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	 I would have preferred that many move pain from one place to another, but I did not want it, as I saw in the woman; and I thought that this was because the woman had dry body and open veins, and due to this the constrained ventosity appeared; and it does not seem according to this reason for those who are delicate and have moist bodies and veins closed.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	 And when you see to cure this disease, and the patient feels that pain, if she opens as we have said, lay her above and below hastily, then press on top so that the constrained ventosity goes to the place; and cauterize the place; and if you do not see it at your eyes, cure it with those who drive away the ventosity, such as fetid pills, pills of serapin, and similar others.
des saiettes	 arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are varied according to their appearance and the parts of the body where they strike.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	 The differences among them are that some have large points, small, smooth, and sutured; some have two angles, and those with tongues, and those where they are split; and one that strikes in any member does so according to these manners: either it strikes at the principal member, like the head, heart, liver, stomach, spleen, intestines, kidneys, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	 When it strikes in any place of these members, and the signs of death that I will tell you afterwards, make you aware: if you must remove this arrow, for the death comes after in many ways; and when this ill sign is not clear to you, and the arrow is not entirely out, pull it and take care of the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	 And the sign of the brain when an arrow strikes and pierces it, and a swelling appears on top of the skull, is also accompanied by scotomia (partial blindness), softening and swelling, and turning yellowish in color, inflammation and yellowing of tongue, spasms and confusion of understanding, vomiting of bile; and perhaps without pus discharge from the nose or ears; and perhaps loss of speech and voice; and a white, moist discharge from the wound resembling pus, and it bursts as if with pressure; and if this sign appears, refrain from treatment, and remove the arrow if it is not embedded.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	 The sign of an arrow striking or lodging in the liver is that it presses on the left side of the breast and feels as if it is embedded in something hard, not empty; perhaps the liver becomes swollen like a pouch and turns black inside, and there comes cold fever, sweat, and fainting: know then without doubt that death is near.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	The sign of an arrowhead that has pierced the flesh is when there is no bubbling of pus from the wound, and the throat inflates, and the patient turns pale and sighs deeply and seeks cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	If the arrowhead falls into the bedclothes of the patient, it has passed through the ribs; and it causes great pain and sighing, and moves all the limbs of the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	If the arrowhead falls into the stomach, it may cause something undigested to escape from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow strikes or pierces the belly, and it does not jump out through the intestine hole, there is no hope in the cure, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	If the arrow strikes into the bladder and the urine jumps out and runs away, and the patient feels strong pain: know that the wound is deadly.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other member, such as the hand and arm, neck, shoulder, armpit, spine of the back, wrist, hip, legs, and similar parts, are safe according to various conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or the artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you what happened to me, do this instead.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	 It happened to the man that an arrow or splinter pierced the root of his nose: I tried to pull it out from another side beneath the ear fat, but it felt sensation without movement.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	 And pulled out a splinter that had pierced the fat of the oil beneath the paper, and the splinter was curved, and could not be reached except for the tip towards the body, and the splinter was large like a Turkish arrow, all the iron felt in the ears; the person was well and no bad incident happened.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	 And pulled out an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic with ears; I sharpened the beaks, and made it thin until I pulled it out, and the Christian was well.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	 And when an arrow is embedded in a person, whether it be in the head or abdomen, and I thought he would die; and after he had passed thirty days, his condition did not change; I made an incision over the arrowhead, and applied force, and drew it out without any adverse event.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	 And when the arrow pierces a man's head or back, and the wound is healed over; and the arrow remains inside him, not changing its natural position, nor causing any harm in its natural function.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	 And when another man is pierced by an arrow in his face and the wound is healed, yet endures much pain for a long time; and many other similar occurrences.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	 And I was called to treat an arrow that had pierced the body of a nobleman, the king's son, who had fallen in the snow, and it was slightly deviated towards the right side; and the arrow was completely embedded for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	 I found the wound narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	 I pierced it with a very thin needle and felt nothing; but he felt prickling and pain under his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	 I thought it was the point of the arrow. I placed a plaster with soothing and digestive ingredients on the spot where there was no swelling, and the arrowhead appeared.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	 I left the plaster for many days, healed the wound directly, and kept him in this state for a long time until he felt the arrow within his belly; and he told me about it.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	 I place the wound with corrosive medicine on it by hand for several days until it opens up, and then probe it, and feel the head of the arrow which adheres to the place; afterwards, I cauterize in the opening of the wound with that corrosive medicine until the head of the arrow appears clearly visible; and after a period of more than four months, the wound heals so much that I bind it with pliers on both sides and cannot move it anymore; then I stop refining and contriving means of instruments, until I make the pliers well-formed according to what its shape will be at the end of this chapter, while I am treating it and returning the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	 And the men say that the nose cartilage cannot be restored; I then restore it, and the wound is healed, and the patient is completely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	 I have told you the quality of extracting certain arrows, but do not put all your trust in it because the books cannot fully comprehend it; however, wise masters are able to find solutions for small things and those that are present and failing, and they often discover nine new works and nine instruments below the surface of foreign things happening within this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	 I say that arrows do not leave the body where they have been inserted except in two ways: either through the place where they enter or from another side; and one that bursts out from where it enters is an arrow entering flesh and sometimes bursts out again.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	 And if it doesn't jump now, leave it until the flesh is spread around and the joints are aligned; also, if it is embedded in the bone and cannot be pushed out, leave it for a few days and move it daily; then it will pop out, and if it still does not, perforate with a sharp instrument everywhere around until the opening is enlarged, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	 If the arrow is embedded in the skull bone and goes towards one of the ventricles of the brain, or any of the accidents I mentioned earlier: do not pull it out, but let it be for a few days until it is aligned again; for if the arrow comes to the ventricle, that is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	 And if the arrow is not fixed beyond the bone only and does not reach fully, and the patient suffers for some days with bad condition, then you must try to draw it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is very deeply inserted and cannot come out by itself, then you administer emolients around it, as I told you; afterwards, heal the wound when it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	 And if the arrow is lodged in the body and cannot be seen, seek it with all your might; if you feel it, draw it out with any implement possible; if you cannot due to the narrowness of the wound or the depth of the arrow and there is no bone, nerve, or vein, widen the wound as much as possible; then pull out the arrow and if it has ears like it is stuck, remove the flesh that is embedded in it from both ends that you can, and then break or bend the arrow's ears until you can draw it; be careful not to break the arrow, but rather to draw it more easily.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, press down the flesh around it, then draw it, as extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	 And if the flow of blood opposes it (the cautery), bring what we have said about treatment in its chapter; and be careful with incising the nerve and vein, and use device as you can safely draw out the arrow, quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and place the patient according to the shape they were in when the arrow struck them, for this is the greatest help that can be, and if you cannot do so, put them according to what the sign indicates.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	 The arrow that comes from another place, or anything related to it opens up somewhere, or the skin is swollen in the area that we can see or feel; cut then over it as far as the pliers can take hold, and then pull it out; if it leaps away now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, turn your hand round and round until it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	 And if it cannot come out, leave it alone for now, and then continue the extraction until it comes forth; and if there is an arrowhead in it, push it to the end; and if it has fallen off, you should administer glue, so that the point of the arrowhead enters the glue; and then push more, and when the arrowhead is covered with glue, push in the instrument at the pointed end for easier extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	 If the arrowhead is touched, you must cut all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, then treat the wound as appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And if the arrowhead falls in the chest or the abdomen or the bladder or the side, and it is near and you can cover it, do so; and be careful not to cut the vein and nerve, then extract it, and then sew up the wound, if necessary; and care for it until it heals.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the tweezers used for arrow extraction resembles an owl's beak, and here is its form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And they come in many shapes: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	 The shape of the growing hair is similar to a bird's feather, to guide the arrowhead, as shown here:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The form of pliers for pushing and pulling is as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	handles with common bodies (i.e., pincers)
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	 The number of veins to be cauterized is thirty-one, of which the first sixteen are as follows: two bandages that are after the ears, which are called "dous herbech"; and two arteries that are in the temples; and two veins that are in the corners of the eyes, which are called "aspirres"; and one vein that is on the forehead; and one vein that is at the base of the nose; and two tendons that are at the neck; and two veins that are above the lips; and those veins are called "augeherich"; and two veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	 The veins that are commonly healed in each arm: one is called the cephalic, and it is located on the left side of the chest, and the lay people call it "arm vein"; the median is called "fistula", and is composed of the cephalic and basilic, and the lay people call it "vein of the heart"; the basilic is either on the right side of the chest, and the lay people call it "vein of the belly", and it is above the elbow, and this is the one that heals, which opens manifestly above the wrist.
