Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	 The cubital vein is the one that is between the ulnar and the little finger, and it has two branches; and in the leg there are three veins: one under the wrist on the left side of the chest, and the second saphenous which is at the right ankle; and the vein called "nassy" that is at the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg there are three veins beneath these.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	 The patient should aid the veins behind the ears with the ancient cathartes and purge them; and the quality of the purging, as I tell you, is that you raise the head of the patient, and scrub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth; then hold the neck of the patient with a screw until the two veins appear behind the ears in the two dependant places of the head; afterwards, press down on them with your thumb where you feel the pulse beneath your thumb; then take the lancet and thrust it through the vein to the bone, then pull your hand all along the vein, and strike and the skin and the vein well two times through; and make the blood come out until you see; then hold and tie it until it is healed; and I have already said about incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	 The first artery of the two in the temples is useful for draining old, soft, and common otologies (ear diseases), and also for tears caused by the eyes; and the qualities of the drainer are as follows: the patient tilts his neck until both veins appear prominently; and you feel a pulsation under your thumb, then apply pressure on it; next lift the curved vessel to the top of your thumb and insert the lancet into it; lift the vein further and prick it, as you have done with other veins, and draw blood according to your need; afterwards release the patient, put your finger on the vein for an hour, then put cotton on it; and then tie it up and leave it until it is healed; and we have spoken of its dressing and its removal, or the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	 The incision of the vein in the forehead is worth as much as the incision of the skull in the diseases of the old face, and it has migrated and reddened; and the qualities are that the patient stretches his neck by twisting it, until the vein appears; then take the instrument called "fosseur", whose form is:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	 And place the point upon the vein, and support from your hand or something else, and let the blood flow according to the quantity that you see; then release the patient's neck, and tie the vein until it is healthy, and not working again with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Moreover, the flames should not be too sharp, and the vein should be cut obliquely because the bone is near, and by chance the flames may break when they are thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	 The incision of the two veins that are in the eyes helps with swelling, redness, and inflammation in the eye, and diseases of the face; and the qualities of their incision are that the patient stretches his neck by twisting from some chain, as before; then let it heal, and the incision should be a small piece of flame, a little long but wide because there is no char.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are subtle, perhaps they break; then correct the blood flow, as much as you need, and then cover it with linen, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	 The vein of the nose in the nostril is useful for ague, scrofula, and diseases of the face, such as migraines and redness that comes in the face, especially when it is old; and the qualities of the vein are that the patient holds his neck, then presses his nose to your left hand, and takes subtle flame long, and thrusts it between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open well otherwise, and the blood will start to flow immediately; do not go too deep, and make the bleeding stop according to necessity, then let it rest for a night, as it is quickly restored; and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	 The first guinea pig's small intestine helps in the straightening of the anus, and at the beginning of the process of healing, as well as many diseases, impetigo, corruption, herpes, and stomach ailments; and the quality of the small intestine is that the patient lowers their head under one and the other, as we have said; and the master being on top of the patient, and the patient lies on the chair, then open the vein gently along its length, then draw out the blood moderately, or as much as necessary; then repeat the process in the other vein, then untie the ligature, and hold all the veins moderately so that the patient does not strangle; and leave it until morning so that the wound heals.
de la sainie des leivres	 Of the liver purge
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The sinews of veins in the mouth above help in swallowing and contribute to gum corruption, lip fissures, and teeth and surrounding issues.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	 And the qualities of the purge are to make the patient sit before you, and hold his neck as I have said; then turn the liver, and observe both veins, one is on the right side of the liver and the other on the left, and they can be recognized by the fact that they are black, and by the fact that around them there are smaller black veins: so hit one and the other, and if you do not know which ones they are, and you are in doubt, hit the largest of each side, and likewise do with the two veins above and below, because it is the same method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	 Of the liver beneath the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	 The opening of the veins that are below the tongue assist after the head vein surgery, and it is at the narrowing of the throat, and in the diseases of the eye, and in the diseases of the mouth; and the qualities of the surgeon are that the patient swallows saliva between your hands before the sun, and wets the tongue, and looks under each side for a black vein: therefore, one and the other are healthy, but do not go too deep, as there are arteries below.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	 The incisions made in veins for common surgeries are done in two ways: either by piercing with a hot iron or a fine, olive-oil like tool, such as a scalpel, which is called "anesil"; and they can be wide and narrow depending on the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the flame mirrin is very renowned, and it is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	 And it is necessary to open the large veins with thick blood visible and containing thick and troubled blood; and this is the form of the olive oil flame.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is pointed more finely, and it is for thinning out the subtle veins that have a yellowish thin blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	 The basilica vein (one of the large veins), which aids the diseases that are below the throat, neck, breast, and abdomen; and it is necessary for the patient to bleed profusely, and to drain from the artery that is underneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	 If the artery is cut, and bleeding occurs, it must be stopped, as I have said; but the flame should not be touched, but rather extinguished like an ember.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	 If the basilica vein does not open up clearly, then you must insert another one or find another way to bleed it, or make an incision in the vein near the arm; it will open up clearly; and cut off the flame as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	 And if you wish to know the location of the wound, you must then strain the arm, touch the spot where you recognize the pulse; then mark that place, bind the arm, and cauterize the vein with fire carefully; be careful not to hit the artery when you see it swelling, for it is the artery: avoid it.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If it swells up high like a child's urine and the limb is red and thin, know that it is not an artery: hasten then, place your finger on it for a long time, then remove your finger if it stops bleeding, for many times this happens; bind the arm, leave it as it is, do not let the patient move it; be afraid, and do not let him move it until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the wound is not stopped and it bleeds, and no medication is present for you, strike the artery if it is open, because the head will retreat; stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	 And take a bark of willow, and cut it and take one of the halves and bind it well until the next day; if it does not stop bleeding, that is good; if not, cure it as we have said, with powders that stop blood; and the stopping of the bleeding should not be overly reliant on many positions due to the small size of the wound, and the power of the thread from the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	 The vein milk in the middle helps to treat blood from the head above and from the chest below, because it is composed of basilic and cephalic, as we have said; and the lord must be careful when he cuts for the nerve that is beneath, and if it bleeds too much, and he finds the nerve, and inflates and heals it should be cautious, and by chance may not heal; and this nerve opens up many times, and if it does not open in any man due to his subtlety, then you must heal it with an instrument anesthetic; and avoid the nerve as much as possible.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, make it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	 The first aid for the skull fracture is that it attracts blood from the head and helps the eyes; it must be drained with olive oil or myrtle fire, because it is the safest of all veins, as there is no nerve or artery beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	 Further, one should seek the lighter vein and not strain anything the first time it is needed, and then try again; and sometimes the veins swell in some men, when the first attempt is made, but do not strain anything.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the urine is according to your opinion.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	 The first thing you should know about draining is that draining is not done except to maintain health and to prevent future diseases; it must be done in one of the three veins: namely, cephalique, faste, and basilique; and it should be done at the beginning of the summer, in autumn and winter after eating, when the signs of repletion appear; and it should be done on the first or third day, after two or three hours.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	 The administration of medical aid is not limited by any fixed hour, but rather when it is required day or night, in every hour and at all times; and it should not be administered to children until they are 14 years old, nor to women during pregnancy for the fourth month up until the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Nor should the elderly who have passed 60 years be salved.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	 If anyone wishes to be treated, in whatever manner that may be, it is necessary that the intestines are cleansed with a gentle enema, if they have retained much wind, so that veins are not filled with superfluous waste which can harm the main organs; nor should one treat those who are excessively salty from foods, drunk, or intoxicated in any way, until they recover; and after colic affliction, vomiting, disturbance of the stomach, frequent urination, excessive sexual activity, heavy work, staying awake and fasting, and those whose vitality is weakened, either by something related to their weapon or body parts; then purify the humors if they are thick, by foods and drinks and medications, if you have that power; then immerse in water, unless anything forbids it, to purify the blood, and treat the vein with the third artery as we have said; and on that day, avoid work, pain, lust, and similar things; and be bound and joyful, and let the healer stand higher than the one being treated, and rub his arm two or three times, then gently pull the ligament above the affected area, for when it is too tight or thin, it cannot heal without that; then rub the affected area with your hands until the veins swell, and feel them; then moisten the healer's hand with a little old oil, then place his thumb of his left hand under the affected vein slightly below where one wishes to treat, so that the vein does not burst or tear when pierced.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	 For there are veins that run like cords in the body, and among these there are some that become filled with windiness, so that when fire is applied, it does not open the vein, and thus is one of these; and if the vein is opened, the wound is too narrow, for which reason the cauterizers should be aware of this.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if it opens the vein again for a second time, that is good; but if not, then start anew under that place or cut more quickly if the wound is not inflamed.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	 If the wound is swollen and the patient is afraid, let him wait a day or two and not tie up the arm: possibly abscesses will come out; do not enter into the bath, then repeat the cauterization if it pleases him; and if the puncture is small or shallow and you doubt that much blood will come out, apply all the fire directly to the puncture itself; and open it a little hastily, so that the wound swells; for this happens often when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	 If you see the joint swollen, do not start draining it immediately, but put a little bit of olive oil on it, because it alleviates the body from blood and is coagulated in this place by the oil; and administer the olive oil in every drainage of veins, to stop the flow of blood; and the same can be done with triacle and bowe when applied to the joint; if it becomes too thick, it should be made more subtle.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	 If there comes a large abscess, which happens many times, especially when the opening of the vein is small, hurry up and put on the joint a sponge moistened in vinegar and warm oil for an hour; you must do this after the blood flow from the vein, and if it remains at the joint for some days without turning black or green, it will not harm; and if you see it, apply anything of aloes or myrrh refreshed in calament, poultice, or something similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And there are often abscesses and appearances at the sanctuary (hospital): put your hand on it then, and if you find it soft to the pressure of your hand, that is a bad sign.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, you should not put anything on any of the things we have mentioned, for by chance without the artery; but he should be given one dry plaster to harden it, then cured with another treatment until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw blood from each according to the quantity of its virtue, and from the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the wound is black, let it drain until it turns red; and if you see it thick, let it drain until it becomes thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	 And for the one who is full and swollen, and requires extraction of blood, make a larger wound, and let the veins be wide; and for the weak one, do the opposite, and he must be bled little by little, and it should be done by cutting across, not by pricking; and this manner of bleeding is safe from displacement of blood and compression of nerve, and it is better than bleeding long instead of deep.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	 For the one whose body needs to be bled, it is necessary to give soft bread soaked in grape juice beneath; if he is heated, bleed him 3 or 4 times. And for the one of cold complexion, fast before bleeding with soft bread soaked in sweet syrup, or aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, and let it be a fragrant syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	 And if the palm (of the hand) is open to the wound, after the flow of much blood, it is necessary that he drink broth made from charcoal, and subtle-smelling syrup, and use the other things mentioned in the section or chapter on syncope for the evacuation of blood.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	If you want to burst open an arm, or draw blood another time, if it has been weakened by excessive bleeding, let it bleed drop by drop according to the amount of its strength continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wants to burst open the arm after the first bleeding, and has a strong constitution, should let it bleed for 6 hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wants to draw blood from another part, should draw it on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	 For there is much blood within the body that is already heated up and causes fever; therefore, it is necessary to draw a large amount of blood, open the wound wide until it closes over again (palm); then you reward all the conditions of the wound, and place your hand on top of the thumb when it heals, so that death does not come in its place, which happens many times when the healer is negligent; and it should not be that you separate the arm and let blood out a second time, and the wound is closed, that you press strongly; nor if it is curved, that you straighten the arm hastily, but rather leave it until it closes again a second time; or you prick it with the tip of the flame until the coagulated blood from the vein comes out, and place a piece of fresh linen on top, and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, do not bind it at all until the abscess has been calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to draw blood again, do so in the same vein, or another one, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is similar to the vein in the head because they are composed of the same thing.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	 And the manner of bleeding is that the patient pushes his hand into hot water until the flesh becomes red; then it should be bound somewhat, so that the vein appears well, then bleed carefully through the cross (of the hand), neither wide nor long; and let the wounds be large, and let the blood be bled near the joint of the hand, and if it cannot be removed, put the hand back into hot water, and let the blood flow out in the water, as much as you have; and if it is in the summer, do not hit the hand with hot water again because one puts more in winter than in summer; and the bleeding of this vein is safer than all other veins, for there are no arteries or nerves.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	 The hot iron of the salvation of the right hand is beneficial for all liver diseases, and this is how it is done: hold the hand, and apply hot sharp, until the vein flees if you can see it; and if the blood flow is sideways, and if you cover it completely with everything, it will cause no harm; do not go too deep because the nerves are entirely naked under the skin, and then replace the hand in hot water, but make sure that the wound is not frozen and the blood does not come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as needed, put oil and silk on the wound to heal it quickly, and do this for each wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The salve of the left hand is good for the disease of the mice, and do it just as I told you on the right side.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	 The hot iron is beneficial for all diseases that are beneath the body, such as the hernia, retention of fluids, kidney diseases, thigh and leg ailments, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	 And the quality of his health is such that the patient puts his foot in hot water and rubs it against the vein until it perishes, and binds it above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and from above the foot, it goes very deep; therefore, bind it where it is wider or at the ankle, which is more effective.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you have a wound on the foot, be careful of the veins that are below it, and keep it clean in the same way as you would when wrapping; let the flames not touch it.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the wound cannot be removed, immerse the foot in water and let the vein drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	 If the treatment of his health is necessary for the first time, begin it slightly higher up, because the area is salted; do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and do likewise with the soothing of the other foot in the same way.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The saline for the sciatic vein is at the ankle of the foot, and its application alleviates the pain of the haunch when it is used for hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	 And the quality of his health is such that the patient immerses himself or bathes and compresses above the ankle four fingers twisted, because otherwise it does not open the vein; and if it opens, heal in all ways that you can, and by crossing; and it is more effective to cut it, because the area is raw, and it is much inclined towards human hands.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	 And if you don't cure it, no remedy will open or close the back of the foot, and towards the little toe, and beware of the nerves; and make as much correction of the blood as you see, then undo the bandage, and put cotton on it and press; it is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	 of the boils' discharge
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Blisters of the bladder (or boil) are made of horns, or hairs, or glass; and blistering is done in two ways: either by cutting and drawing blood, or without cutting.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	 This ventosation, which is felt as if it needs to be injured, is according to two methods: it can be for all fire, or with fire; and the ventosation made by injury and bloodletting is performed in 14 leagues of the body, from which one is entirely in the head; and others are in the neck; and others in the two chests of the neck; and the boils under the chin; and the boils of the two shoulders; and the boils on the heels; and the boils of the two arms; and the boils of the two legs; and the boils of the two ankles; and the ventosation does not treat blood, except for small veins that are scattered in the flesh, and therefore it should not be administered at all, neither with fire nor without fire, in any disease that comes from repletion, until the entire body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	 And if due to necessity of illness it is necessary to use an enema, or for customs, we will administer one every hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end; because there are some who, when they need to use an enema, have a heavy head; and some who experience fullness and reddening in their body, and in their head, and at the neck, and darken their eyes; and some who experience a drop of blood in their mouth, and withdraw their tongue, and bleed; and there are some who dream, and see blood and navrez and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we observe these signs, especially during the month, we order to bleed after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	 The muzzle syringe helps with headache ... that comes to the eyes, and it should not be used after the evacuation of the entire body; and this enema is instead of the cephalic syringe, and it should not be used by those of cold constitution or who have diarrhea, as it causes them great harm; and for this reason, they should not use it, nor those with cold head diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who often heal themselves become indolent, and therefore it is necessary to place the cupping glass a little lower due to the fear of indolence.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	 The ventosation in the neck is located in the sinus of the head and the basilica, and therefore it is effective in the compression of the throat, and for splitting the channel of the jawbone, and completely, and filling; it should be pressed slightly, because if it holds too firmly, it can cause obstruction or inflammation of the throat or heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	 The ventosation on the costal bones of the neck is effective against headaches, otalgia and migraines, strangulation, pain in the roots of the teeth, and it is located in the sinus of the basilica; you should instruct the patient to press gently, so as not to press on the artery and avoid bleeding.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	Ventilations under the chin are good for mouth diseases and tooth decay, as well as similar diseases in the mouth; and they are located near the safety of the lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Ventilations under the shoulders are good for diseases that come from heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	 The ventosations of the ribs are as valuable as three veins in the arm, for it draws blood from these large veins; and instruct the lord not to pierce too deep, for the flesh is naked there, and knows nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The ventouse located on the rump is as much as for the emorroid from its foundation and diseases underneath, and the ventouse should be large and made of lead, as it needs to drain well; and in case it is fine, it would burst, causing great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The swellings of the legs open widely because they draw blood from all over the body, and are like the old pains of the kidneys, and bladder, and vagina, and diminish the flowers; and are in the position of the two shins, and the two ankles, and yet they weaken the body after a long time, and bring pus in various dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to put the swelling is that you empty it first, suck it promptly, apply pressure immediately and move it evenly, and do not stop doing so until you see the place become red and swollen, and the color of blood appears; then stop, and put the swellings, and take care in the disposition of the body, for there are some who have loose skin and clear pores: it is necessary to cut only once, and it is necessary to make wide wounds, and a little deeper; and suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the wound is large, it is necessary to cut twice: the first time to refine the path of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the bone is very thick, it must be struck three times; and when we wish to draw blood drop by drop, we should prick only once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	 If we wish to draw much blood, we often reward ourselves; if the flesh is thick, pierce not too deep, and let it be such that the veins are pricked suddenly, and it belongs to him who has thick skin and hard, who have narrow pores, to anoint the places of the ventosations with sharp and penetrating oil: if it is in summer, with spicy, penetrating oil, or sweet almond oil, or seed oil of cucumber; and if it is in winter, with watercress oil, lily oil, camomile oil, or something similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is thick and cold, take bitter almond oil, or balm of Gilead oil, anise oil, and similar.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	 And if the patient whose wound you are treating has thick and wide pores, no oil should be applied, but it should be washed after the lancing with rose water, or cold water, or water of morel, or water of cucumber, or porcelain water, or another similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And he who has much moisture should rise from asafetida or myrtle water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	 Those with excessive fluid rise from old wine or sour milk, or decoction of anise or chamomile, or others similar; and it should not be lanced before the bath or in the bath, but an hour or two after the bath; and he should not sleep after the lancing, and it is necessary that he walk when he is to be lanced and when he has been lanced.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	 And be aware that the one who is healing should take cool things, such as green apples and endive and lettuce leaves, and similar things; eat little, and pork fat, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	 And for the one with a cold complexion, take honey syrup and fragrant wine that is neither old nor new, eat little bread and little pork, small birds and sparrows; on the day he farts, he should drink more than eat; it is also necessary to give some men to some men a triple or muscat before or after farting, for strengthening the main members; but let them be subtle, but those who are hot should not drink.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	 The following harnesses placed to wound are those that are placed on the liver, spleen, gout, stomach and flank, for these members cannot bear to be wounded elsewhere, and they are only used to draw blood from one member to another as we do with nipples when a woman is nursing; to remove viscosity from the member, as we do with the ventouse on the stomach and flank to reduce it; and to alleviate pain when there is obstruction or stone, as it does by chance attracting the obstruction, or removing the stone from its place; and it works in the same way when placed on the liver and spleen when there is retained wind, and these ventouses are administered empty for sucusing only; and sometimes they are administered with fire, and sometimes filled with cold water, as in cases of pleurisy, and in this manner the ventouse is filled with hot liquid or with a solution of cooked herbs appropriate to the condition.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the blister administered with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	 And it should be two fingers and a half of width and depth, and have a hole through the middle small but not too deep, as if to push an awl, and made of bone or wood in front so as not to prick the patient when placed on the member; and there should be a rod of the thickness of a wand or iron, passing through the middle, for placing a splint, and they should be large or small according to the diseases and the age of those who take them; because the blisters of children are different from the old, and thin from the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	 And this blister should be placed on the member in such a way: take the splint of wax or linen, place it inside the hole of the rod that is inside the blister, so that the light penetrates into the blister and does not burn the patient; then place the splint on the member, over the hole mentioned earlier, so that when you look at it, if the vapor escapes, you remove the blister; and take the linen again as before, and repeat it often, if needed.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	 In the bladder which is administered in disease of pleurisy, it has no rod nor piercing, and it is not administered except when it is full of water, and it is placed on the body only; and this is its form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	 Suction is not administered except in bodies where bladder stones cannot be placed, such as lips and gums, and similar places; and in bare skin areas, such as the ear or nose, and others; and the quality of the user is that when you find bladders that are in sweet clear water without purulence, take them; place one nut in sweet water until they become familiar and have nothing inside; then sanitize the area with vein and bladder, then rub the body as much as it becomes red, and put the bladders on it; and when they are full and warm, if it is a place where a bladder can be placed, put it there, because this works well.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	 If not, lift the shoulder blade slightly, then deeply, carefully, and then press it back into place; if the shoulder is injured too close to the chest, moisten a linen cloth with cold water, put it on, until the pain subsides; if the pain persists or multiplies, put on vinegar powder, or other similar things, until it subsides; or you may apply half-peeled beans to the shoulder, and leave them there until they harden on the shoulder, which will stop the pain now; and if necessary, take more painkillers.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	 And if the pain does not want to take medicines, rub the shoulder with fresh blood or poke an needle into it until the pain subsides and then apply them, and as soon as they feel the blood, let them harden; and when you see that they stop bleeding, sprinkle some powder of aloes and horehound, or ash, which will stop them now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is frequently necessary in the art of medicine, and it is for the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	 Know, dear child, that the foolish man casts himself from this chapter, who has never seen any old books nor read letters in them; and because of this, science is alienated in our land, for I have never found a good one; and I do not know anything else, except through the knowledge of the old books, where I have studied the science and treated it, and by experiment, and by the custom of my life; and I have described in this chapter what is contained, and summarized it at the end, and clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are brought about, as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, it is necessary that we say the prologue of this book and the subjects where wise men put their understanding, and dwell on truth, so that those who are experienced know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	 When injury or dislocation or twisting or swelling comes to anyone, it is necessary that you first heal the patient on both sides, unless something prevents you, such as weakness of body, old age, or illness; or if the time is very hot or cold; and eat cool foods, namely raw fish and mutton and eggs and drink no wine, nor consume any fatty meats, and do not fill too much with foods that fill the veins with blood, until you have doubt about pus formation or spreading of matter to the member; then the patient will recover in the first stage as he has used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary to nourish the patient with meats that make thick nourishment or have viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water and rice, meat pie, beef, mutton, fish eggs, fresh fish, strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For prolonged nursing leads more often to fractures.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	 And know that the broken bones of the old and weak cannot be well restored or joined according to their nature due to the slackness of the limbs; neither can those who are too tender, such as the bones of small children; but do not despair, set the broken bone above it with a large piece that straightens and joins the limb together, as it was before; and never apply any traction, and for this reason feed it with rich foods, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the break of the neck is different from the break of the leg or foot; and I will tell you in this chapter all ways of breaks.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	There are breaks that heal by themselves, and others that grow worse if not treated, like the tip of a feather for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a break with a wound, and a break with a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	 And each one should have its tool and instrument suitable for the restoration, according to what memory comes to mind; and it is known that bone fractures occur when the limb is twisted, and opens wide by dislocation, and presses against the hand; and when there is no twisting or touching, and the patient does not feel great pain, there is no break; but there may be twisting, fissure, or small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	Do not move the hand but put medicines that come after this on it, and then hold it gently now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	 And know that the fractures that go in the arm, and are the two parts disjointed, they must now be put evenly back together, so that the abscesses come to life; and if the abscesses grow close, you should leave it for a day until the abscesses subside; then bring it even with the muscles that you can easily and skillfully move, and know that the restoration of it is lighter than the restoration where there are pieces; then press, as necessary hereafter.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	 If the bone is broken into pieces and divided into two parts, whether it be a hand or foot, or a finger, or two tendons, or one tendon and your hand; then put the member according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the broken member are disjointed, you gather all additions in their places to the muscles that you can, and ensure by your work no injury or pain comes to the patient; and join well the two bones of the os according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And it feels well to the touch if it seems not quite right to you: straighten it properly, and do not strain it too much, nor force it as those who bring it by their work, abscess hot and contraction to the member, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	 And when the limb is set in place, ensure that you punish the patient so he does not move it, neither while awake nor sleeping, nor turning, nor in any other way; and carefully watch to make sure the limb remains as firm as possible, without feeling any pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	 When there is no pain, it is not properly set, and it must be put in such a position that there is no pain; and watch to make sure it is straightened, so twisting does not come when it is restored; and the qualities of the broken limb are according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that the broken limbs can be various in smallness and size and shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	 When there are small members such as fingers, wrists and similar: you must wrap them with soft and thin linen cloths; for those that are large such as thighs and legs: you must wrap it with a wide and hard bandage, because the wider bandages hold the whole large member firmly and equally on all sides, without any gap. Then tie three or four turns around lightly, depending on the member, and pull your hand slightly on the entire bandage, then go to the broken part and pull less than the break, and move away from the break a bit; and soften the bandage little by little, until you take a large part of the healthy tissue, then take another bandage, and turn it around directly over the broken limb. Then return to the under side of the break, and tighten slightly, not too much or too loosely, as we have said in the first section above; then put linen or cloth between the bandages until they are all even, then tie them all together, and finally place well-made splints on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	 And if there is an abscess or boil, place a warm poultice over it, and remove the abscess; leave it as such for several days; then apply sharpened steel on top of your steels (levers), and let them be about half the thickness of a large cane, or a fust used for splitting logs, or splinters from a palm tree, and they should be shaped like this:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	 But the lever that one places over the fracture should be a little larger and wider than the others; and it should also be as long as is required for the member whether small or large; then apply pressure with the levers as you did in the first instance, then tie a thread above it as in the first instance on the fracture; the thread should be tighter at the beginning, then gradually looser; it must be of moderate thickness, not too thick nor too thin, and made of flax yarn. For if the thread is thick, like what I have seen in the works of foolish people who make their rope from twisted flax yarn, it is a great mistake, because the splint cannot be even if it is too fine, and it must not have less space between each lever than two fingers.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is wounded by the heads of the ribs after the resetting in healthy places, place linseed poultices or cotton wool over them to prevent bleeding.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with fracture and the bones are broken, I shall tell the remedy afterwards.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	Know that it is not necessary to reset all the fractured limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	 For when the limbs are large, it is not necessary to put hot irons on them before five or seven days, or more, according to your certainty of the abscess erupting; and here follows the method of ancient plasters for restoring fracture, dislocation, and torsion: and it is that you take flour which is kept at the walls of the mill, and mix it with a lot of egg, and put this mixture, neither too clear nor too thick, on and this is the common method of the plaster restoring the fracture in various positions, and especially for women and small children, for it is not too hot or cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Here is another method for plasters that heal fractures, dislocations, and twists: take barley meal, salt, vinegar, asafetida, and Arabic gum, in amounts of ten; myrrh and aloes, in amounts of five; alchil, eight; grind these ingredients into powder and mix with plenty of egg. If the patient's complexion is hot, use this plaster, because it has a good composition and quickly heals broken bones for many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	 Another method of plaster for torsion: take mugwort and wormwood, soak in ten; myrrh and aloeswood, soak in nine; acacia six; Armenian bolex ten, grind well, and mix with vinegar or a lot of egg, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	 Another method of dislocation and bone setting at joints, and alleviate the pain that occurs, and cut the bone with this tool, and break it: take new linen, moist it in oil and boiling water, and place it on the joint.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	 This plaster does not restore [the bone], but it is good for alleviating abscess pain and treating actual pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method of plaster to restore broken bones: take dried fig leaves and ground ivy leaves, grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	 Another method of plaster for the restoration of broken bones and to hasten the healing of abscesses.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	 Take root of mallow, camomile, violet flowers, powder of beeswax, each in equal parts; grind them and mix with wine; if the limb is scalded, mix it with coriander juice or water instead, and apply it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	 Another method of emplastrum (a healing ointment or plaster) stronger than the first, when an abscess hard comes to the restoration of the member.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	 Take roots of comfrey, flaxseed, balm of Gilead (balsam poplar), alfalfa, and sage, and flowers of violets and camomile, all in equal parts; grind, and mix with salt water, or sweet water, or wine, according to the heat of the member and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.
