Hippocrates wrote in his book that nothing should be placed on a broken member for restoration except a plaster made of wax and oil, and no other thing more, and he said it should be between soft and hard but not too much of either.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	It seems Galen said that for restoring a broken member, dry and slightly warm things should be placed on it, such as myrrh, aloes, incense, and similar things, as we have stated.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another method of plaster that is good for injuries and pain: take mugath (possibly a kind of flour) and crushed bones from men or feathers of birds, also mallow, and mix it equally; grind them into a paste and apply the mixture.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then loosen the wound a little afterwards, and make sure the patient feels no pain, nor has the bone moved from its place; do not loosen it by hand for many days. If pain comes to the place, or itching, without rest or swelling, you hasten, and loosen, and remove the plaster immediately; and take a light cloth, sea sponge moistened, dip in water, and lift the wound, until the itching stops, and the pain is relieved; then let the member rest for an hour, then place dry linen, damp with water or rose oil, and tie on a nut, as long as you are sure of the abscess being hot; and let the inflammation of the member subside, and the pain be removed, then continue the binding gently, and a little plaster, and not to strain too much as before; and bind softly until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess has healed and turned red, swollen, and pain has disappeared, and you need plaster and linen, then resume tying it as you did before equally.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	 And if no swelling comes to the limb as we have said, do not dislocate it unless after 3 days or 4 or 5 or 7; and at no time should you leave it for 20 days, according to what one sees, until the fracture heals, and the joint approaches the flesh above; then hold it more firmly than before, and make the flesh thicker as I have said earlier; and if you see that the joint dries out more than necessary, know that nourishment cannot enter there; therefore warm with hot moist heat, every time you dislocate it, and stretch the joint a little; by this work, cut off the nourishment from the limb, and heal promptly what the foolish surgeon leaves twisted: this is harmful, and such work is fearful, and I see no other remedy but to rest and work properly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of various ways of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	 Many kinds of breaks are, and they have various shapes, and their causes are determined; for there are breaks made by sword impact, and the bones fractured all along the bone up to its tip which is beneath the bone, as done by a haunch or fist; and this manner of break is called "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	For the sword strikes the bone from above causing it to be broken completely, and such a breakage is called "complete break"; and these are the wounds caused by either great or small complete breaks.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a thrust-through injury, a fracture or falling on stone, or other similar injuries.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a persistent fracture, which reaches up to the membrane that is beneath the bone, or it is on the bone, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	 And if there is a wound that penetrates the bone as thinly as hair, and it has a small crack, and for this reason it is called this kind of break "capillary"; and if a wound is made by striking with stone or falling, or in some way, and forces the bone piece inside, and the ends of the bone are shaved like a blacksmith does on top of pots; if the stone enters within.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	 And this happens more often in those who have moist bones, such as a child's head; and it happens in all these ways of fracture that small pieces are dislocated, like teeth; and I shall speak about it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	We know all ways of fracture by the distraction on them, and the examination with probing, and by the rotten flesh that is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The similarity of hair-like appearance is known by those who, when the bone is discovered and scraped over it, an opening appears black at the fracture.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a fracture, beware of the sick person's condition, and if you see any harmful symptoms such as vomiting of blood, loss of consciousness, swelling, numbness, fever, pallor, and other signs in various conditions, it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any doubtful symptoms and expect a healing, then start the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wound first comes to you, and it is in winter, then remove the bone before the fourteenth day if possible.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if this is the case, hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the tissue underneath the bone is not corrupted, and the incidents mentioned will occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	 If the fracture of the bone reaches up to the layer that covers the brain, then you must cut open the broken part as follows: and it is that you take hold of the child's head of the patient, and expose the bone in all possible ways, and on the shape of the wound more gently than possible, and if bleeding comes out when exposing the bone or pus, help yourself with whatever is needed, and it is that you fill the place with damp cloths soaked in rose oil; and let the wound rest until the pus has subsided, and be sure of the stoppage of blood; then begin to remove the bone around it, and this is done according to two ways of work: the first way is that you cut crossways in front, and this is its shape:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then make another incision larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second way is that you have various incisions, some narrow and others wide, pointed and made with an iron blade; and work lightly, so as not to cut the tendons.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is out of place and hard, it is necessary that you pierce around it, in such a way as you administer incisions with trephines, but not so much that they cut through the bone to the other side, and there must be a margin or circle above the point to prevent the tip from passing beyond the bone; and you must have more than one, so that each comes into its place along the width of the bone, so that you have trephines for all sides; and this is the form of the four kinds of trephines.
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The qualities for piercing around the broken bone are that you put one trephine on the bone, and turn it with your hands until you feel that the bone is pierced; then move the trephine a little farther away, and do this all around, then cut the space of the bone between the perforations as subtly and gently as possible, following what has been said, until you draw out the bone or any of the tools you have such as pliers or tweezers; and be careful not to touch the brain or the sinus.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	 And when you have pierced the bone and treated it, it is necessary that you reset the tightness that remains of the bone to all other instruments resembling an incisor, but it must be thinner and more subtle than the other incisors; and if anything from small bones or scales remains, remove them gently with the instruments; then treat the wound with cauterization and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other method of work is that which Galen describes, who was very skilled; and he holds it in high esteem, and this is his saying.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	First, you should expose a part of the bone where the break is open, so that when you have exposed that part, place the lenticular anvil on top of it as shown by its form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	 Do not cut from one side, and let the part be hollow in two sides, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then strike with a small hammer above, so that you cut lightly around the bone carefully, paying attention to the cloth below; if it is torn against the bone, remove it gently, as it is cut badly without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	If the bone breaks through to the cloth, and the bone is chipped only from above, and there are small fragments, then it is necessary to smooth over the roughness, and remove the scales with a sharp scraper of different sizes, in order to bring the most suitable one for each place, according to the work and shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	The patient should shave himself with great razors, then with more subtle ones afterwards, and should not cease until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each other kind of hair cut and subtle breakage, it is necessary that you bring the cause according to his guidance; this is not a matter for anyone who has put his study into this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	 If the wound is open, you must take a linen cloth, according to the size of the wound, and moisten it in rose oil, then place it on the wound; next, take another linen cloth doubled over once or twice, moisten it in wine and rose oil, and place it on the first cloth; do this as gently as possible, so as not to burden the wound, then administer more linen bandage over the top, but do not tighten it more than necessary to cover only the wound; leave it like that for a day or two until the abscess has subsided, then remove it and administer medicines such as root of lilies, flour of wheat, incense powder, aristolochia, and similar things; from these things make a powder and place it on the wound, and immediately administer reliable medicines without bitterness; and keep the wound clean, do not leave any ointment or bandage, as when pus gathers on the cloth of the brain, it will rot and may cause great harm to the patient, for when something bitter is placed on the wound, it will burn through from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore, take care that no bad accident happens to the patient as we have said, for it is doubtful with a doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if blackness does not come violently except for the medicine that has been placed upon it, its virtue being such, you must take a part of honey, and three parts of rose oil and in glue the cloth, and place it on the sore; then treat it according to the methods of treatment as necessary, until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two parts of the nose above are broken, or just one of them because they are two bones; and the one below is cartilage, and does not break but only bows or twists, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	 If one of the two parts is broken, you must bite your little finger or thumbnail and place the breakage within your index finger hole, and at the back, until the nail grows again according to its natural figure; do this gently, and be careful that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	If the breakage is in the upper part of the nose and the finger cannot reach it, then you must insert a small splint into the nostril.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	 If the breakage is in two parts, do as before and hasten to restore the first day if you can; if not, after the seventh or tenth, when the abscess has calmed down, then place linen bandages on the root of the nail where the breakage is.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you apply another to the other side, if the break is there; and let the dressings be as thick as they fill the openings of the needle.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	 And they said any restorer that one should soften the tents with butter, and to stir each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	 It does not seem good to me, but they should be softened in an egg yolk concoction, and flour powder; then leave the tent until the bone is hard and the cartilages are hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes feathers of goose are inserted in place of tendons, and if one side is wrapped with a thin cloth, and the breakage is held, breath is blown through it; do as you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	If abscesses come up while you are working, put either wax or cotton soaked in rose oil, or a little bit of quicklsilver.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If abscesses do not open themselves, then apply a plaster outside, made of flour from the earth, and incense powder, mixed with egg yolk, then place light bandages on it, but do not tie them too tight; and if the break in the nail is small, and it is broken into small pieces, take it out with suitable tools, then sew the wound, and treat with things that heal quickly, such as plasters and ointments appropriate for this; and if there is no wound within the nail, then treat the tent, and put cotton in it until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the fracture of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the lower jaw is dislocated and there is no wound outside, and the break is only outside but not broken through, if one knows it easily, it means there is a curvature within.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the break is on the right side, you must insert your index finger into the patient's mouth; if the break is in the left lower jaw, insert your index finger of the right hand, and gently push it inside, then adjust it from outside using the other hand, and make it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the break in the lower jaw is dislocated by .2 (two fingers), you must administer an extension of .2 parts to make it equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if there is movement of the teeth or fracture, hold them with a thread of gold, silver, or silk, then place a broken bit gag on the mandible and put one double cloth on top; put a large, well-made splint or equal piece of leather on top, long and wide according to the mandible, and attach it where you can, and instruct the patient to rest and eat light food.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	If you see the figure changing, dislocate it after a day, then reset it to its original position; put a plaster on top, with flour from the mill mixed with egg or oatmeal after removing the gag; put a light linen bandage on top, and if the plaster sets, and the dislocation does not change, leave it until it is healed; many times it is healed in four weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if an abscess appears, apply what we have said many times before.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, make sure no piece of the bone has been removed; if necessary, remove the splinter with suitable tools.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrowed, stretch it with fire according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all the pieces and none remain, if necessary, close the wound if it is wide and apply one dressing suitable for that purpose to promote healing until it is healed.
de la forcele	of the forceps (instrument)
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The forceps break multiple times towards the shoulder, and the fracture is in four ways: either it is broken and dislocated in two parts, split into pieces, and is the easiest to restore; or there is a fracture with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the work is when the fracture has a wound, you should have two assistants, one of whom holds the shoulder that feels the forceps broken; and the other stretches the neck towards the affected area; then align the fracture in your hands so that the form is as it should be, and there is no appearance or deformation.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to stretch more, put a round cushion of cloth or linen on the patient's shoulder, and make it as large as necessary; then extend and raise the forceps, and press the cushion with your hand so that the fracture is aligned as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the shoulder out by force because it comes in fully, then the patient must lie on his affected side, and place one pillow under the shoulder, and push the ministers to move the shoulder downwards until the bone of the socket is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then direct the fracture to your fingers, and if you see debris, then it is necessary that you cut across; and separate the pieces gently, and if the bone cannot join due to any obstruction, hit it in one of the incisions you have made; but place this instrument under the socket to prevent dislocation.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	 And it seems like a spoon, and is not closed, and should be as large as required, according to the size of the bone and the nature of the work; and let it have two holes, as you see, and let one be wide, and the other narrow, as the opening of the wound that you made when you treated the bones; and when you are sure about the abscess depth, if the wound is deep, then cut the wound, and if the wound is small, or you doubt about the abscess depth, then use linen and cotton, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if hot irons come for it, moisten a cloth with rose oil, asafetida, and wine, and place it on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	 The setting of the bone, when it has wounds and is cut, is that you place a plaster of flour mill and egg yolk on the bone, and put light wicks on top, and put a splint under the affected area if needed; then take a very wide bandage about one palm in width, then put two layers of linen over the wicks, and the plaster; then take a thin strip of three fingers in width and length, and wrap it around that bandage so that the ends of the bandage are hanging; and place the strip on the fracture, and turn the bandage towards the neck, and under the affected side and the patient's healthy side; and tighten each part, and when you see that the fracture aligns correctly, and you clearly see that the strip does not move above the broken bone, then check it every day, and when the ligaments loosen, hold it in place; and position the patient on his back, and place a small pillow under the affected side to lift the shoulder up; this will help the shoulder heal by aligning the fracture of the shoulder blade through the alignment of the shoulder, or you tie the arm to the neck, and do not untie it unless a bad accident occurs, for up to twenty days; then repeat the plaster, if necessary, and tighten and leave it in place until it is healed; and it will be healed in no more than twenty-eight days, and less in some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	on the fracture of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	 It happens that the shoulder breaks or is displaced from its joint, and one can feel it only by touching; then you should align it according to the shape of the break, and reset it according to its natural form in all ways possible; then sprinkle powder from the mill with an abundance of egg and light feathers on it, and cover it with a double cloth; then place a large and thin awl slightly larger than the shoulder on it, and if there are any hollows in the shoulder beneath the awl, fill them with feathers of linen so that the awl is equal in all places; and then tie it firmly in a great bond so that the awl does not move from its place, and watch the ligament each day; and whenever it softens, tighten it again, and equalize the awl if it is displaced from its place, and have the patient lie on his side; and the shoulder will be restored in twenty or twenty-five days. And when this number is accomplished, release it, and be careful, for it is not bone that easily becomes displaced.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a bone fragment protrudes in front and not beneath the skin, lift it up, remove it, and follow what was said earlier to heal an abscess with hot cautery.
de la brisure dou pis	of the fracture with fish
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	 The limb is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; however, it often breaks at the edge.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	 When it is broken obliquely, it slips downwards, and the patient feels great pain, lack of nourishment, fainting, and may vomit blood, and the fracture opening widens in the broken bone, and the limb becomes numb.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies on his back with one cushion between the shoulders, then presses the shoulders, and assembles the ribs of both sides to your hands, and subtly puts it all in equal alignment in every way possible until the bone figure is as required; then put a plaster and bandages over the broken bone, or a lighter splint, and wrap it in one cloth, and tie it on the bone so that it does not move; then turn the limb round and round, and tighten it gradually, and check each hour whether it heals, and if it swells, tighten it; and if it needs to be dislocated due to corrosion or pruritus at the joint, or pain or abscess, hurry up and dislocate it, remove the plaster, and direct the one who has come there in ways of treatment; then reset the plaster, and tighten it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	of the broken ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the fracture of ribs does not occur except in large ones behind the back and near the neck, and they do not break unless they are slippery; and it hurts greatly upon examination at the joints.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	 And the reduction is when you set the break as required.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	 Then put a splint and bind with a stick, if needed.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	If the fracture of the rib is slanted within, the patient feels great pain and swelling, as if from pleurisy, for the bone points to the skin; and the fingers become hardened, and immediately vomits a large amount of blood, which is a grave illness, and the ancients have made great effort to treat it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if among those who say that it is necessary to administer foods that swell the abdomen, to push the fracture outward.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not bring hot irons unless they have come (to be used).
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if they have come, then let them be heated.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they said that one puts vents on the side to suck out pus, which seems reasonable; however, there is doubt whether the vents do not attract the superfluidities to the side due to weakness in position.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they said that one should cover the side with damp linen dipped in hot oil and place bands between the ribs to make the wound equal on all sides, then it should be cured with the cure of pleurosy (inflammation of the pleura), meat and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the patient feels great pain that he cannot endure due to the broken bone not bearing pressure, and there is doubt in the patient, then it is necessary to make an incision above the level of the fractured rib, and place a tool beneath it to prevent it from sinking; then the fracture must be cut, gently pulled apart, and the edges of the wound sewn together if it is large, and the wound treated with splints until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if an abscess comes, place moistened wool soaked in rose oil on top of it; and treat the area as necessary for abscess, and let the patient lie still on the side where it is, until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the broken collarbone
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Never does a break occur in the bones of the collarbone, and it never bends; and similarly in the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	 And when this happens to anyone and you want to know if it will heal or not, if you see his hands becoming soft, swollen, and dead, and he cannot move or extend them, and when you prick with a needle, he does not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	 Know that it is deadly in many positions, and if they do not speak or feel when you pull or prick them, know that the bone joint is saved, and the patient will be healed if treatment is given.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	 And if a similar thing happens in the spine of the back, and you wish to know whether it is diseased or not, take care if the limbs are weak, and if there are accidents that are in hands; and when it moves with a sudden ventosity and evacuation without will, when it has been lifted on the stomach, it also moves with ventosity and evacuation without will.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	 And when it is placed on the back and wishes to lie down, it cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	 Know that it is mortal: do not labor in its care.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	If this event does not occur to them, then the situation is easier.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that you soothe if there is an abscess that burns hot, put on top of it rose oil or egg yolk oil until it calms down; then put on top one of the soothing and drying plasters, and tie it with a string, and command the patient to rest; and do not let him sleep on that part where he feels pain, until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If any bone dislocates, it is necessary to cover it with a cloth; then remove the bone, next join the two edges of the wound together with stitches if it is large, and heal it with soothing ointment for as long as it heals; and if the head of the bone is broken (which is called "the head of the cow"), push your left hand's pocket into it and hold it equal to your right hand strength, then put on an plaster and a dressing, if you have them; then tie it, and if there is bone dislocating, make it go back, and remove it, and heal the wound until it heals.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the break of the shinbone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It happens that the bone of the thigh is broken, and if it happens, there is only a slight reduction in mobility at the hip; it becomes long, bends toward the outside, and causes pain at the site where it is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand above [the break], until you are above the broken area; and recognize which [bones] are broken and their shape; and if the break is only at the hip, set the break straight, until it is in its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is long or bends inward, place the patient on his back, so that the restoration of the break can be seen.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have set it straight, place the plaster on top, then put a stick or a splint on top, and hold the fracture in place so that it does not move; apply the [medical] solution under the ribs until the fracture is healed.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	Instruct the patient to sleep on his healthy side or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if an abscess appears, do not touch it until the abscess has calmed down, and apply what we have previously mentioned; then return to the treatment, and hold it as necessary, if there is no bad incident; and this is the manner.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	Of the shoulder breakage
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder joint is between the neck and the chest of the shoulder, and if it is broken, it should be restored according to one of the two methods: one of which is that you take a large splint made of wood or bone, in this shape:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two shoulders with two ropes, and place them high up, and make the patient lie on one seat; then lower the broken arm onto the splint, so it comes to rest, and have a slight curve of the splint in the middle; then place a heavy object or the assistant holds it down below; then have the assistant hold the breakage equal with his hands until the breakage returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is that you lay the patient on his back and tie his hand to his neck, then command two assistants that one holds above the breakage with both hands, and the other holds below with all the ropes, extending each rope to its side.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	 And if you wish that the extraction is stronger, hold the ligament below the fracture, and above the fracture, and extend each of the helpers to its part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	 And if the fracture is near the head of the shoulder, you must place the sling beneath the armpit, and the other side towards the fracture; and similarly if the fracture is towards the chest, you must gently place the sling without exertion, until the fracture is level on the bone, and on the chest; then make it even, as necessary, and hold it in place, unless an abscess comes.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	If an abscess does come, do not hold it for more than seven days, and place a soft cloth in oil on top of the abscess to soothe it; then you can hold it, and the method of holding is that you put the clamp on the fracture, then bring the arm towards the shoulder, and place your hand on the shoulder or chest; place the bandage, and hold towards the shoulder and towards the arm, such that the arm remains in a straight position, unless something prevents it, or if the bone is not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	If you doubt that the bone does not move, use splints and place a larger and stronger splint than the others on the fracture, and let there be one inch of space between each splint, and let each splint be so large that it passes the break two inches from each side; then hold on the splints, as I said at the beginning of the chapter on the fracture, stronger and less in alignment.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	 If you see the swelling and tightening, as we have said, during the operation to restore the broken limb, and you doubt the abscess is hot, leave it to heal for seven days, as we have said; then observe every three days the sling, that pus does not swell or come to the bone, or that the nerves do not come to the member because it is too narrow.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	 If the direction, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	 And if no such accident happens, he should not be dislocated before three days or more, and the patient should sleep on his back with his hands on his stomach; and place a cotton sock of equal size under the shoulder, and observe every hour of the day or night that the figure of the broken limb does not move or become softened tendons; if it moves through the power of medicine, and give him the meat we have previously mentioned in such a way that the meat is at first subtle; and when he begins to recover, let it be thick.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	 And it is custom that the shoulder and leg should be reset within 40 days of all; and then he must be dislocated again, administering a bath and ointments to set it right.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	 And if the narrowing is deformed and swollen, it remains to loosen for days or two months.
de la brisure du bras	of the break in the arm
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is made of two bones, which are called the "two shinbones". One is small and it forms the elbow joint; and the other one is large, and it is located below, near the little finger. Sometimes, only the large shinbone breaks, or sometimes both break together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	 When the small fractures are broken, the restoration is easy, and the healing; but when the large ones are broken, the healing is poor, and more painful than when they are broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	 If it is only the small fracture that is broken, it should be stretched slightly and put in a splint.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	 And if it is the large fracture that is broken, it should be held more firmly; stretch it above the splint, and raise the hand cuff higher than the others, and the small bones lower than the others, and cross the patient over himself, and the splint in front of him higher, so that the patient does not suffer any labor; then extend the ministers' arms to the part below his hand or his elbow, and another minister above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	 And then make the limb equal, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it is broken into pieces, place each one back in its place, and if any of them cannot be held straight and you cannot restore it to its place, make a bone splint, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	If with the break into a wound (i.e., fractured open), I have spoken of it in the specific chapter; take care.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	 And if at the beginning of the reset there are abscesses that burst, apply a linen cloth soaked in a mixture made of rose oil and white beeswax, which should not be too hard or too soft; and place the cloth gently over the abscess until it is healed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	 Then remove the linen cloth, and apply a plaster made of milled powder with egg, then place the splints, and ensure that the splint for the fracture is stronger and slightly wider than the others; and remember that it should have six splints or more in various positions: whether the fracture is in one bone or two; and tighten more around the fracture than elsewhere, and always less when moving, as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and ensure that the linen cloths over the fracture are soft and moist, not hard nor rough; and ensure that the thread used for tightening is of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	 And hold the member and the joint after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	 And if any bad accident comes to the member, such as itch that comes to the member, then you should irrigate the member with hot water until the itches are calmed down; and let the member not be restricted from resting.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	 And then resume the binding, and if the ligaments are destroyed and the bones are dislocated, and similar things, give advice accordingly.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	If the narrowing of the anus cannot come to the limb because it is too tight, then you must soften it for a little while, and leave it for some days until the narrowing passes, and then set it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	 And if none of these things mentioned above come to the patient, do not unbind it until twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	 In addition, he should place his hands at his neck and keep his neck even, and beware of movement and dislocation; and sleep on his back. Know that this break will heal in thirty or forty days or maybe twenty, according to the compositions and complexions of the properties.
de la brisure de la main	Of the break of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	The back of the hand and fingers rarely suffer breaks, but it often bends multiple times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is broken or bent, the patient should lie down crosswise, straight in front of him equally; then place his hand on a cloth spread out, and extend the broken bones, and align them with mirrors, until they are well joined; and apply a poultice and lint, if an abscess does not develop, then apply a splint according to the size of the limb; and it should be wrapped in one linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture occurs at the front near the abdomen of the foot, make a bandage from rags, and instruct the patient to bind it to their broken foot; then bind it with a long strip of cloth, and ensure the wound is covered as well as the hand's palm, and bind it as needed.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	If the fracture is at the back, it is necessary that you place a bandage on top and another under the foot to keep the hand straight, then bind it all around the hand, and tighten the lace between the fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	If the fracture comes in any of the fingers (such as the thumb), make it straight as needed and bind with the palm; if you see that a splint is needed to lift the fracture and keep it from moving, place a small straight splint there; if the fracture is in other fingers, such as the index or another finger, make it straight and bind with the healthy finger that is next to it; or bind them all together in one place, as you would for a thumb; take care in restoring its position and proper healing of the abscess, and watch for any signs of infection, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken leg
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bones of the leg are often broken, and one can see it when it twists in front and behind; and the restoration is such that one tie is placed above the break, and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his face, then extends each minister evenly to their respective positions; and this is when the break has been set in the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	 And if the break is near the root of the thigh, it is one of the ligaments towards the knee, and the other ligaments on the opposite side of the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	 And if it is near the knee, then the ligaments are below the knee, and the extension is distal; then place the hands on the bone equally to its two sides, so that it conforms to its natural figure, and then apply the plaster and splint, until the abscess does not appear.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is an abscess boiling, let it calm down before returning to your work and care; the treatment is made in this manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	 It is necessary to wrap above the break and bind tightly in two or three layers, and remove any excess, then rotate the leg so that the heels come to the root of the thigh, and place the long thread between the thigh and the leg, below the knee, and bring the end of the thread to the top; then rotate the leg and wrap above the break and above the thigh, then put straps on the break and a splint on the bone of the leg; then apply soft fabric for eight inches between the leg and thigh to equal the strain, then begin to bind three or four turns above the break; and as you proceed higher on the break, loosen the strain; then take the two threads that you placed between the leg and thigh, and tie three straps that are above, then return to below the end of the thread, so that you come alongside the foot; and tighten, so that it does not move from its place, then leave it like that, until no abscess or swelling or similar thing appears.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if there is a fracture, dislocate it and treat the part that is injured, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone protruding, they must be cut off, if possible; and if not, the limb must be broken and marrow extracted; and cure it as we have said until it heals.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And sometimes the thighbone is broken in such a way that pegs are inserted, as in the shoulder or arm; however, in restoration of this kind, the patient does not experience any pain.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	Know that the thighbone is restored in one or two days, depending on the different complexions [of patients].
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the groin [area]
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	 Know that in the knee joint, there is little damage, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	 If it breaks, it is not really a fracture, but rather a crack or puncture, causing all sorts of pain and wound, and this feels very painful.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that one puts equal traction on what is round at its ends, as long as it can be assembled; then place the splint, and put a round bandage, if necessary, and tighten it as required, then check all the dispositions as we have said in other fractures, such as abscess or other similar things; place whatever is needed for each accident until it heals.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	 Know that in the leg there are two bones, one of which is called "ham" and the other "shin"; and it breaks like the arm does, and for this reason the restoration is similar to that of the arm, and the work is all the same. And if the two bones are broken together, then the leg turns in all directions.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the thin bone is broken, it bends forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	 If the large bone is broken, there is great pain and it can be seen clearly, and it turns underneath.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	 Then you should apply extension and make it equal, and tie the joints equally; but if the break is misshapen or there are many parts, the extension should be less and lighter; align accordingly to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you have completed your task, take two fists full of straw that will bind the leg from one side and the other, and be as long as the leg from the knee down to its end; then wrap it in two layers, one above and one below, and tie it in the middle so that the leg cannot decline to either the right or left, and thus it is good; and no one should bind one arrow-length of the leg, and it should be made of straw, and put the leg for protection from movement, and properly apply it at the fracture where there is a wound; move the leg every day, to see if there is an abscess or any other accident; cure it until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the bone fractures of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there comes no break, but the bones of the foot sometimes suffer a break and also the toes; no fire is needed except in various positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	If the bones of the foot suffer a break and you see them overlapping each other, then place the patient's foot on the ground, as if he wants to walk, and now place your foot on his, where the bones are raised, then press it until they align again; then put a splint and padding on, and put a small table under the foot with two flat cushions, then tighten the splint towards the affected foot, then when you have wrapped cloth around it, and other things that you may need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, loosen the splint, for you will find the bones aligned, whether they are broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if any of the two [bones] is broken, restore them as we have said for the bones of the hand; then place a splint on the broken bone according to its length, and let it be slightly larger, then put a small board underneath the injured one that I mentioned, and tighten it accordingly; and if there are 2 or 3 [broken bones], or more, break each bone separately, place a splint on top of each bone wrapped in one linen cloth, and tighten the board beneath the foot; and let the protrusion be facing the abdomen of the foot so it covers it well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	Also do not neglect the other things I said about other fractures, after what we have said; and treat each accident according to its needs.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the bone of the thumb
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When the bone of the womb is broken, you should make it enlarged, then incline it to the back part and hold it from behind; then fill the cavity with the patient's cotton and also stuff it as thick as possible; then turn the woman, and lift her buttocks little by little, and then pull the cotton until it reaches the entrance of the cavity, and the bone comes out with the cotton; and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has urinated, replace it, and do this for 7 days or more: the break will heal, and if you see, take a bladder of goat, tie one end to the buttocks, and push the whole bladder into the cavity; then blow strongly into the tube until the bladder is inflated inside: the cavity will return the break; then fill it with cotton, and leave it for some days until it heals.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	 And when the bone of the thumb of man or woman is broken, restore it as we have said in the elbow bone; and these nearby breaks are not hidden from him who applies his study and skill, and read my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	 The break signifies in various ways the right path of restoration; therefore, pay attention.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the shaft (long bone), when it is broken, put a goose's gullet around it; then wrap cloths around it and leave for 3 or 4 days, and it will heal quickly.
