de brisure avec plaie	Of breakage with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	To the one who has a breakage with wound, especially if it is large, such as the bone of the shin or shoulder or similar, it must be set immediately, so that the settings we have mentioned take place.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is healthy, clean it with vitriol, if you have nothing else, then continue to restore the breakage in that same hour or day, unless an abscess comes.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	If an abscess comes, leave the restoration until the ninth day, until the abscess is calmed, and do not touch it for three days or four, because you would bring a bad outcome.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the bone breaks through, it must be set lightly by your hands, in a small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	If the extension is not provided for setting equal to your hands, it should be made with this tool that is made of iron, which has 7 or 8 inches long, and the width is according to the size of the wound; and therefore, the mirror must grasp 3 or 4 depending on what is needed in each cure of breaking; and be round and slightly large, so that it does not bend during the compression on the member during your work, and be sharp before, and thick from the middle forward, like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	 And it is called "elbow," so the curved shoulders should be placed on top of the visible bone; and push it once, until it returns to its place, and make them even one against another.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	 And if the break is subtle and the instrument cannot take hold of the bone, then you must cut the top of the bone so that the instrument has power over it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot reset the bone as we have said, then strike it with an appropriate instrument, either chisel or saw, to your power; then remove that which is stuck in the bone with sharpness and small shavings.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	 And when the bone is reset, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	 Keep it in its place, then moisten the cloth in black bitter vinegar and apply it properly if it is hot; do not put any ointment or other substance on the wound that might cause corruption; then provide bandages when you have restored the bone, leave the wound exposed, and cover it with a layer of linen according to the size of the wound, be careful not to constrain the wound with the fracture; and many times this has been done by foolish surgeons, causing harm or death to the patient or sometimes rotting; and the bindings should be softer and more pliable than other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	 And if the wound is bad or large and you doubt that a bad incident may come to it, as we have said, and you feel pain at the place, do not put sticks on it; but wrap around, in place of sticks, hard cloths and tie them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	 And after a day or two, if you see swelling in the wound, remove what you have put on it and apply healing ointments for wounds, such as healing ointment made from four ingredients and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And you must release the member twice a day, in the morning and at evening, until it is healed and sound.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	The limbs should be set in such a manner that the bone moves downward lightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	If it passes for several days without healing but the bone continues to break, knowing that there are small bone fragments; therefore, you must treat the wound with care and remove all those dislocated bone fragments that cause pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	 And if a fistula comes to the place or any other form of corruption, you must treat it according to what he said in the chapter above.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	 And when the bone is broken and open on the limb, like the bone of the thigh or shoulder, and other similar large bones, do not drain it because many times death comes to it, but let it remain as long as possible; perhaps later a piece will come out through it after 20 days or 30, then treat the wound if you can; and if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	The arriving bruises upon the sore
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often see it following the breaking of health, particularly near the joint, and it is displeasing to see the appearance of the limb's figure; and unfortunately, the limbs cannot perform their natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Therefore, be cautious: if it is fresh, administer medicines such as aloes, incense, myrrh, and gum arabic, and similar things, so that you take one of these substances or all together, and mix them with a strong wine or with egg white or oil, and put them in poultices, and keep them on for a long time without removing them; and then loosen it, and start another, until the nodulation is removed; or you hold above a well-made piece of wood because the properties of wood are to remove all swellings from the limbs; and if the nodulation has already hardened like stone, it must be removed by cutting off the top, making the excess appear; or you shave it with any razor until it is removed, and cure it until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	The weak member after being treated or healed
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the bone fracture is restored and remains weak and subtle afterwards, this occurs for many reasons: one of them being that it was tied too tightly, but not properly bound as required; or because there were too many bandages, preventing blood supply to the limb; or due to excessive bleeding; or due to excessive movements, not at the right time; or because there is little blood in the body, making it weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat, make the body lean, until the blood multiplies in him; administer baths, and give joy and peace to him; then apply wax over the limb so that the wax attracts strong blood supply to the limb; frequently drain off the pus with warm water, until the blood flow returns to the member; and return it to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	twisted limb after health
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When a limb is twisted after restoration and the bones are broken open, and the shape of the limb is deformed, yet it does not lose its natural function; do not believe in the foolish who say that one must break a limb anew, and many foolish men have done this in our land; this practice is condemned, and great harm comes from it, and perhaps death; however, if the swelling and torment are fresh, you should apply hot water or softening herbs such as mallow leaves, root, medicinal trefoil, and similar things; and make a soothing emplaster, like dittany well made, and take the myrrh of mallow, mix it with ginger oil or sesame oil, and make an emplaster; or use figs greased, grind them with wheat bran, and similar medicines that alleviate pain.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	 And sometimes, the dislocation is removed by continuously and persistently rubbing with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	 Bring movement to the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the tortuosity is growing hard like stone, it needs to be cut with iron, it must be covered up to the bone, with a subtle and gentle incision; and put dressing and study in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs to anyone, it must now be reset carefully.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	 For if one delays, the limb swells, and in case it is reset at that point; this should not be moved until it has subsided: many times it brings spasm and other pains; nevertheless, when such a thing occurs, make the patient bleed, then let him rest, until all abscesses have been pacified; then heat the limb with hot water and oil, then gently move it, and cure each limb according to where the injury is located.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have organized the chapters on shoulder dislocations from head to feet.
des mandibules	jaws
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It often happens that the jaws are dislocated in two ways: either they are somewhat disjointed from their places and softened; or they are completely dislocated, hanging towards the lower part, and saliva flows out of the mouth which it cannot hold, nor can close its mouth, and wraps its tongue with the speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When a small dislocation returns, it often does so in multiple ways.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	 If it is whole and complete, then you must quickly reset it, and not delay; and in such a way that the servant holds the head of the patient, and pushes one of his fingers from one hand into the root of the dislocation of the lower jaw within the mouth, if the dislocation is on two parts; and the other hand should be spread apart to equalize it; and instruct the patient to soften their jaws, and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the thumb is placed evenly, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it is difficult to set it, just as if it were two jaws together, warm them with hot water and oil, until they are easy to move back into place; do not force it to return, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	 And when they are reset equally, the patient's mouth should be closed well with soft cloth made of rose oil and wax, then gently tied with several bands; and let the patient sleep on his back, and his shoulders between two cushions so that he does not move either right or left, nor exerts himself at all, but takes light food, until the pains are removed, and the jaws are held together; and then eat lightly whatever he wants, and do not strain himself to open the mouth for eating and drinking, until the jaws are well healed and sound.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two mandibles cannot be set right within an hour and are not returned to their places, fevers and usual sickness follow, and perhaps abdominal distention, and perhaps vomiting of clear bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, know that it is destruction; and many times the person who experiences it dies within eight days.
de la forcelle	of the noose (traditional English translation: neck)
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forceful cannot dislocate from the inside along with the ribs and it is dislocated once at the back, and this is felt.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	 Then the restoration is that the patient lies down on his back and extends his arms; then presses firmly at the shoulder joint with your palm, and it will return to its place; then put on the splint and bind it, and hold the shoulder from dislocating; the shoulder which is towards the spine cannot dislocate again, unless it does so once, and if it does, reset it to its place as we have said; then put on the splint and bind it, and hold the shoulder, and command the patient to rest until he is healed; and in this way, the shoulders of the back are also reset when they are dislocated from their place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	When the shoulder is dislocated, it must be reduced first.
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	 Know that the shoulder is dislocated in only three ways: one is when it dislocates at the socket part below; the second is at the hip part; and occasionally at the top part, but this happens rarely; it never dislocates behind the shoulder nor inside the nerves; and it often dislocates below towards the socket, especially for those with little flesh, as it can come back quickly; for those with enough flesh, it comes back slowly and goes back slowly.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes it happens to some men that they get struck or broken, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they think it is dislocated by this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Therefore, you should verify it, as long as you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	 And it is known that the dislocations are downward towards the socket, and you will find a difference between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find on the chief of the shoulder a hollow, and beneath the shoulder at the toucher the chief of the shoulder, as if there were an eye; and the sick cannot return his hand to its place nor move in any way; similarly, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, as you can see clearly at the toucher; and this type of dislocation is not always easy to return, unless the child is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	The method is that the minister lifts the patient's hand upwards, then places their thumbs under the dislocated joint and pulls it upwards forcefully to its place; and the minister lifts the hand, extending it upward, then places it back in; it will come quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	 And if it does not come as we have said in a few days, the patient must be bathed in hot water; and prepare a soothing, softening and calming mixture such as decotion of elderflower, fennel and melilot in hot water, and give it to him; then lay the patient on his back, place a piece of linen equal in size but not too soft or too hard under his shoulder, then put the heel of another person on the linen, and carefully lift the head of the shoulder; pull the hand of the patient with the other hand; have another attendant hold the head of the patient so it does not move forward; that shoulder immediately returns to its place, and if you see that it dislocates in this way: make a man who is larger than the patient stand near; have him be straight towards his side, and push his shoulder beneath the patient's shoulder, lift the patient's shoulder upwards so that he hangs in the air; and another attendant pulls the patient's hand downwards towards his stomach.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	 And if the patient is too lightweight, he cannot bear anything heavy, and the dislocation returns immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	 And it is also done in another way: one pushes a long needle into the ground, so that the head of the shoulder is as round as a pea and not too large or too small; then it should be placed under the patient, but with soft linen beneath, and the patient should be lying along the pole; then stretch out your hand towards the other side and join the jointure back into its place immediately; if it does not return due to all these things we have said, this is the treatment: take a needle from both hands, four inches long and wide, which has a rounded tip to enter easily through the flesh, in the shape shown below:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	then put the head of the rod wrapped in cloth on top, so that it does not hurt the patient, then place it inside the anus of the patient; extend one arm above the rod, and hold the instrument above the rod, and the forearm at the end of the hand, then place the forearm on a small stone of large width, and let the hands hang down below, and let the body hang down from another side: the joint will return in the meantime.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is inside, in whatever manner it may be, it is necessary that you put a spherical piece of linen equal to the size of the instrument, then apply the plaster made of milled powder, with incense and egg white, all over the shoulder and around, then tighten it below the anus appropriately, turn the string around the instrument, and bind the hand to its neck, and let the hands remain in this position.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it must be fed little by little, until the limb is comforted, for it will heal faster; and then feed more after 5 or 7 days, and move it; and if it becomes firm and is not softened, it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	 And if the joint is dislocated due to moisture that has come or for some other reason, you must administer three fire cauterizations as mentioned in the chapter on cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	If you do all this and it dislocates again after 7 days, and the joint does not hold, and cannot lift its arm upwards, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is severed or stretched or softened; and know that the joint will never be set in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation which is towards the hip, and limbs, whether front or back, is made by force, and extension of hands, and some other means are administered; and it is treated until it heals.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And after healing comes stiffness in the limb, and late movement, the patient should use hot baths many times, until the stiffness is alleviated, and it returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation cost
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the thumb is dislocated at the knuckle, and it comes back at the knuckle; and if it has been dislocated from all sides, both front and back, and the dislocation is not corrected, for it can be clearly seen and felt; and it dislocates according to each shape.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	 And when you join the broken bone with the healthy one, you should see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	 For the joint is dislocated, and the arm cannot bend nor touch its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And you must reset it in such a way that the abscess does not come back, for if an abscess comes back, it would be difficult to reset; and it may not be possible to reset it entirely, especially when it is at the back; it is worse than other dislocations, and causes greater pain, and perhaps death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is, when it can be returned to its state, you extend your hand towards his two hands; and his arms should be extended, and his hands facing each other according to the cut around, above and below, and push the joint at his fleshy parts together, or at the root of his palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	If the dislocation is in front, it returns when you fold your hand over your hand, and press the root of the palm that is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	 If it does not return to its place, you must administer strong traction; and two people should stretch the arm, and two more should hold it still while stretched; then you should wrap a double-length and wide cloth around it; when the healer joins the dislocated joint with his hand, he should apply some oil to soften the joint, then push the joint back into place as far as it will go; and when it is in place, you should put dry plaster with egg on it, hold it firmly, and keep the patient's arm at the neck for several days, then release it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	If the joint is closed in its place, release the bindings and leave it; if you see that the joint is not binding well, renew the plaster and bindings, and leave it like this for some days until it is firmly set; then release it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	 And if there is pain after the joint has been reset and it becomes motionless, bathe and rub it gently and press until it is soothed; or you may place a woolen pad of sheep fat on the joint, leave it for a day and night, then remove it, let him enter water bath; and when it sweats, rub the joint moderately, replace the pad, then enter water again; and do this two or three times until it is healed; and if you see, place warm moist sheep's wool with butter on it and press it there; it will return to its position.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The dislocation of the wrist occurs easily and more so than other joints; therefore, it must be returned to its place promptly, immediately when it is dislocated, before the muscles become swollen or an abscess forms in the wound.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	 And the resetting of the hand, place the sick hand on a table, and extend the fingers of the assistant, align the mirror so that he places his palm on the appearance of the jointure, and press until it returns completely. It is important that you look to see if it is in its proper position; then have the patient rest the back of their hand on a table for extension and resetting.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	 And if the dislocation is in the back of the hand, put the patient's palm of their hand on the table, and have them place their other hand above that appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	 If it returns now, it is well; if not, apply warm plasters to abscesses and let him rest until sensation begins again.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	 And if he cannot bear it and you cannot put it back after some days, the dislocated joint remains twisted; this does not harm the patient as long as the hand is disabled and cannot exert any force: thus know that nerves are cut or arteries; there is no other remedy but to strain by cautery in this case, and possibly nothing else.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is at the joint, place it in the plaster that we have mentioned, then tighten and leave for 5 days, then untie and leave so.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it cannot move well and there is no inflammation, moisten with warm water and rub until it heals.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	About the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	 Sometimes the fingers of the hand are dislocated on both sides, sometimes at the back of the palm or the belly; then push the dislocation towards your pockets until it returns, then hold the finger's head, and turn it towards the part where it is disjointed; and leave it for two days, and on the third day make it equal; and bind it as we have said, and unbind it from the fourth day, make it move, and rebind it; and do this often, until it becomes straight, and do the same if it is dislocated on the belly of the hand, and do the same as you have done above, until it heals; and do the same, when it is dislocated from another side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	the dislocation of the vertebrae in the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the vertebrae of the back or neck are dislocated, where there is none to cure, death quickly follows the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	 And the signs are that the exits leap without voluntary control, cannot be held, and many limbs are softened, where it is either both knees or the two arms or neck; many times the vertebrae become silent in four parts; that which becomes silent at the back is called "gilbositez": the cure is that you examine whether the gilbositez has come from childhood: if not, there should be no cure or healing.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	 And that which falls or due to blows or similar things, the ancient methods of cure used to speak in large words, but there is no great benefit in them all; but I have shortened it according to my intention, and I have made instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	 I say that in the swelling which comes before, there is no remedy nor health; and similarly, that which comes straight between two sides, and cannot be cured except by the one properly coming from behind, as I have said; and it is that the patient should lie with their face equal in one place, and have a support beneath them so they do not bruise; then insert the needle into the head in earth firmly, and another at the feet, and tie a bandage over the affected area of the patient, and another at the thighs, and knees, and ankles; and two assistants know the bands, one at the head and others at the feet, among the two needles; and they should be well fastened, the needles as we have said, and the assistant places their palms on the spine firmly until it returns.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	 And if the dislocation does not return by this cure, take a board three arms long and rounded at one end, place the patient on his side, push the head of the board under the armpit, then put the middle of the board on the spine; place the hands on the other end of the board and press firmly until it returns to its place; if you see it not turning, do it on the tether that turns with the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	 And you should stick two thick thorns into the patient's head, one arm apart, and between each thorn have a handspan of length; and have in each thorn a pin or a tether, and let the pins be firmly rooted so they do not move; and between the two pins have a turning pin, like how the cord turns, and have in the turning two small pins of a handspan long, to turn the tether; then tie the cord that is among the shoulders to the tether on the head, and the other cord to the tether on the feet, and let each assistant turn his tether along the entire cord, and the master should adjust the spine equally as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	 And when it is equalized, place a drying plaster with plenty of egg on top, then compress, and then press it with a wooden rod three feet long, which pierces the joint and the healthy part of the spine, then tie it with a cord, as we have said, and let the patient rest until he is well; and if something comes at the end of healing, administer softening and calming medicines, along with the rod we have mentioned above; and sometimes a piece of wood is administered, and sometimes the appearance is in the back spondile of the spine, and it is believed to be dislocation; and this is the bone that opens, which should not be presumed. In case of accidental death.
des dislocations de la hainche	the dislocations of the hip
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Know that the joints of the hip and shoulder come dislocated only by dislocation, not otherwise like other joints; and the hip joint is dislocated in four parts: within and without, front and back; and more within than out, and less dislocated in front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	 And the recognition of its dislocation inside is that when you join the sick leg with the healthy one, it is longer and more open at the knee than the healthy one; and the sick person cannot bend their knee in fire; and it is the joint which is dislocated swollen with abscess that burns hot, because the head of the calf comes there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of the one who it comes to discharge, is that this incident is contrary to those beforehand.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of the one whose it comes beforehand, is that his leg is well positioned according to completion; however, do not double bend the knee due to pain, and if you wish to make it walk, it cannot move forward, and retains its urine, and when it goes, it passes above the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of the one whose it happens behind, is that he cannot extend his knee nor bend it, and this leg is more twisted than the other, and the ankle is softened, and the hip of the calf is in place beneath the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The re-alignments of this type of dislocation are as follows: you examine whether the dislocations are old and remain according to their position without any treatment; and it is not necessary that there should be any presumption.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in the one whose dislocation is recent, and it is of the four types of dislocation, you hasten to return the joint, pushing it inward and outward, moving it left and right; by chance if it returns, there is no need for further treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	 And if it does not return in this manner, you must summon a strong minister and hold the leg firmly between his hands or tied above the knee; another minister extends his hand over it in such a way that he puts his hands under the calf, then tightens a strong cord around the thigh; another holds the head of the cord; all extend upwards and downwards at once, until the patient is lifted off the ground at one time, and hangs suspended.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common for the four similar cases, and if the dislocation returns, as we have said, it is well.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	 If it is not [the case], then one must apply a cure to its appearance. When the dislocation is at the front, you should remember to lift the patient on his healthy side, then tie a rope around the root of the thigh, and the place that is below the ankle, then pull the rope up towards the ankle and towards the knee; then take another attendant with his arms, grasp the large part of the diseased thigh, and stretch it out backwards in this manner: it will return to its place now; and this method of dislocation is easier than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	 And if you cannot hold it in this manner as we have said, then you must bind the two feet of the patient together tightly with a strong rope above the heels and above the knees, and let the diseased leg be extended two fists more than the others; then let him be hung from a post by his head, and be suspended above ground by his arms; then command the attendant to grasp the thigh's head, and another attendant hanging with the patient, who grasps the thigh in this manner, because the joint will return quickly now.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	 And when the dislocation is out of place, the patient lies down, as we have said in the case of gout; and stretches the ligament above the affected leg properly, and above the foot as well; then insert two needles, one at the head and one at the toes; then thrust the needle between the knees toward the patient, in the correct position; and place wet rags around it to prevent the patient from bleeding; then extend each minister towards him, and the mirror places his hand equal to the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	 If it returns (to its place), that's good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	 If not, put him on a table and press it as we have said in the case of gout, and let the patient lie on the healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when there is a dislocation in front (of the body), it is necessary to stretch the affected leg immediately, and as I have said; and the surgeon should be on top of the injured angle, then press with the other hand, and pull downward towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	 And if the dislocation is to the side, it should not extend the patient below, nor lift above the ground, but rather it should be as if the hip were dislocated to the side, as we have said in the reclining position on two hips; and be facing downward, and the leg extended as we have said before, and should press upon the joint at the table; and will be proper when the patient extends his legs and they are even; then adjust the thighs, and place the pillows, and bind with a bandage so that the hip does not move; and rest for three or four days, then release, and place the pillows again; and if you see that they are even, bind as before, and leave for three days; then release, and let him walk well until the limbs are comforted.
de la dislocation dou genoil	On the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee can be dislocated in four ways: inside, outside, and backward; but not forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	 And the signs are that you command the patient to bend his leg at the knee, and if it does not bend at the knee, know that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all such is that you make the patient sit straight, extend his leg if he can, place your back on his thigh, and place his foot on your feet; then take his shin in your hands, pull it apart between your hands, then bend the two sides of the shin; another servant extends his foot until the shin returns to its place, and the signs are that it bends lightly to the knee; put the plaster on, bind the leg to the thigh, and let them heal together strongly for three or four days, then release it; do not let the patient walk, until the limbs are comforted.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	 And if the limb is not straight, apply strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of clubfoot, until it becomes healthy.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the ankle dislocation
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are sometimes swollen, and sometimes completely dislocated, both within and outwardly.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	 The signs show that the ankle is swollen, and it tends towards the part where it is dislocated; the readjustment should be gentle, and it should be extended gently to the hands when it has been reduced only.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	 And when it has been fully dislocated, you must make the patient sit straight, and hold the leg with the hands above the ankle; then pull the foot towards yourself with your right hand, and then to the left hand twice, then extend the foot upwards, and push the foot upwards strongly; and do this twice, as we have said, pushing and pulling the foot; if it returns, that is good; if not, you must continue the work because it can return again; and if it cannot return in this way, lay the patient on his back on the ground, drive the spike firmly into the ground between his legs, and tie rags around to prevent bleeding of the patient; then hold the leg with one hand, and another person holds the ankle or ligament up above the knee, so that it is held near the foot joint; then each person extends equally, and the spike should be placed firmly between the patient's legs to keep him in place while he is extended; then the mirrors equalize the dislocation with their hands, and another person holds the leg straight below, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	 And when it is at the joint, put the plaster and wool on top, press firmly, tie the foot to the leg, watch the nerves that are above the heel behind, so the bandage is not too tight; then leave it for 2 or 3 days, and if the bandage softens, tighten it; then untie it on the third day or the fourth, and let the patient walk for four days; and if he goes before this term, it is not certain that it will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If an abscess has come to a head, then you must open it, as we have said elsewhere, until it is healed.
des dois	of the hands
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the fingers are dislocated, they should be carefully stretched out without strain, and it is an easy thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the dislocation is in any knot of the back of the foot, you must make the patient sit on a flat surface or on a bed straight up, and put your foot on the opening of these jointures, then press firmly on the foot until it aligns; and when it is even and there is no gap, put a two-toed table under the sole of the foot, then tighten it, and leave it for 3 days, then untie it; and let him rest as long as he is healthy.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	Of wounds and dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	 When a wound occurs with dislocation and it is to be restored, often the patient dies: do not be presumptuous in treatment, if you are not wise in the art and have not used it for a long time, and if you are not pitiful, merciful, and slow, nor hasty; first use warm poultices to abate the abscess, and let the patient in the hand of God, if you see no hope of health; and when you see hope, then reset the limb to its place, as soon as the abscess subsides; and when the limb is in place, administer warm poultices to the abscess, treat the wound, as necessary, using dry onions; and if with the dislocation there is a fracture, and small bones are displaced, set them, and do what we have said for simple diseases; and take care not to enter into fear, according to what I have said, for it depends on your Creator, and for the sake of the wisdom of your weapon and body.
Amen	 Amen (In English: Amen)
